The Permissibility of Pronoun Reference Before Explicit Mention (Idmar Qabl al-Dhikr)
Explaining a usul rule on pronoun reference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule of idmar qabl al-dhikr, explain when a pronoun may refer to a mentally present antecedent, and apply the rule to Quranic examples.

Core Idea
A pronoun may refer to an unmentioned antecedent if the referent is mentally present — the mind serves as implicit mention.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle regarding pronoun reference. Normally, a pronoun must refer to an explicitly mentioned antecedent. However, Hanafi scholars recognize an exception when the referent is mentally present. The passage explains this via an objection to the pronoun in 'ilayhi yas'adu' and provides Quranic support.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Identify the issue: the pronoun 'ilayhi' in 'ilayhi yas'adu' refers to Allah, but Allah is not explicitly mentioned in the preceding text. This is the problem of idmar qabl al-dhikr (pronoun before mention).
Normally this violates the rule that a pronoun must have an explicit antecedent.
2
Recognize the Hanafi response
The author argues that explicit mention is not needed because the referent (Allah) is mentally present (madhkur fil-dhihn) for every believer, especially when beginning a book.
Mental presence can substitute for explicit textual mention.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage cites 'wa bil-haqqi anzalnahu' and 'innahu la-qur'anun karim' where the pronoun 'hu' refers to the Qur'an, though not mentioned before, but the reader's mind contains it.
These examples establish the precedent that mental presence justifies pronoun reference.
4
Apply the rule
Now apply this rule: whenever reading a Quranic verse or text where a pronoun lacks an explicit antecedent, check if the referent is mentally present in the context (e.g., known from common knowledge or religious context).
The rule is not unlimited; it requires genuine mental presence.
5
Understand the usul principle
This illustrates the Hanafi approach that language is understood in context, including the context of the mind. It is a form of qara'in (contextual indicators) that guide interpretation.
This is a nuanced departure from strict grammatical literalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قولہ انتخ۔ اس عبارت میں صاحب توضیح نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ الیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ اللہ ہے حالانکہ اس کا ماقبل میں کوئی ذکر نہیں ۔ یہ تو اضمار قبل الذکر ہے ۔ جو کہ نا جائز ہے۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہاں اضار قبل الذکر لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ اگر چہ ماقبل میں لفظ اللہ کا صراحتا کوئی ذکر نہیں ہے۔ لیکن حکماً ذکر موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ ہر مومن کے دل میں اللہ کا ذکر پایا جاتا ہے۔ خصوصا کتاب کو شروع کرتے ہوئے تو اللہ کا ذکر ضرور پایا جاتا ہے۔ ورنہ ذی بال کام کا افتتاح بے برکت ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی تائید و بالحق انزلناہ اور انہ لقرآن الکریم ،، سے ہو رہی ہے کیونکہ انزلناہ اور انہ میں ضمیر کا مرجع قرآن ہے لیکن ما قبل میں اس کا ذکر نہیں ۔ لیکن پڑھنے والے کے ذہن میں قرآن موجود ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا مذکور فی الذہن کو حکما با ضمیر کا مرجع بنا دیا۔
Explanation of his statement 'intakha': In this phrase, the author of al-Tawdih answers a hypothetical question. The question: The pronoun in 'ilayhi' refers to 'Allah' although it was not mentioned before; this is 'idmar qabl al-dhikr' (pronoun before mention), which is impermissible. The answer: Here, 'idmar qabl al-dhikr' is not necessary because, although the word 'Allah' is not explicitly mentioned before, it is implicitly present. Because every believer has the remembrance of Allah in his heart, especially when beginning a book, the remembrance of Allah is definitely present; otherwise the opening of a meaningful task would be without blessing. This is supported by 'wa bil-haqqi anzalnahu' and 'innahu la-qur'anun karim', because in 'anzalnahu' and 'innahu' the pronoun refers to the Qur'an, but it was not mentioned before; however, the reader's mind contains the Qur'an. So what is mentioned in the mind is treated as if it is actually mentioned, and it becomes the referent of the pronoun.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule discussion about the permissibility of a pronoun referring to an antecedent that is not explicitly mentioned (idmar qabl al-dhikr). The commentator explains al-Tawdih's response to an objection: the pronoun in 'ilayhi yas'adu' (to Him ascends) refers to Allah, but Allah is not explicitly mentioned in the preceding text. Normally, this is not allowed. However, the response argues that it is permissible because the referent is mentally present: every believer has Allah in their heart, especially when starting a book. Support comes from Quranic examples like 'wa bil-haqqi anzalnahu' (And with truth We sent it down) where the pronoun 'hu' refers to the Qur'an, though not explicitly mentioned before, but it is in the mind. Thus, the rule is that a mentally present referent can serve as the antecedent for a pronoun. This is a nuanced understanding of Arabic grammar as applied to Quranic text.

Key Terms
اضمار قبل الذکر (idmar qabl al-dhikr): A pronoun that refers to an antecedent that has not been explicitly mentioned in the preceding text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what justifies the pronoun 'ilayhi' referring to Allah in 'ilayhi yas'adu'?
A) An explicit mention of Allah in the previous verse.
B) The mental presence of Allah in every believer's heart, especially when starting a book.
C) The word 'Allah' is actually written in the text but omitted in recitation.
D) A grammatical exception for pronouns in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul rule allows a pronoun to refer to a mentally present antecedent, even without explicit mention, as supported by Quranic examples.

Morphological Analysis of 'Fasl al-Khitab' in Usul al-Fiqh
Resolving a grammatical objection about the idafa in 'fasl al-khitab'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the morphological form (ism fa'il) in a Quranic phrase and explain how it resolves a grammatical objection by indicating both substance and quality.

Core Idea
In 'fasl al-khitab', 'fasl' is an active participle, so it correctly describes speech as both substance and quality.

This passage tackles a subtle grammatical objection to a Quranic phrase from Surah Sad. The objection arises if one misidentifies the morphological form of 'fasl' as a verbal noun. By reclassifying it as an active participle, the Hanafi usul scholar demonstrates how precise morphological analysis (sarf) is essential for correct textual understanding — a key skill in usul al-fiqh for deriving rulings from Quranic expressions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical objection
The question claims that if 'fasl' is a masdar (verbal noun) and 'khitab' is a substance, then the idafa of adjective to its described noun would attribute a quality to a substance, which is grammatically invalid.
The key is to recognize that the idafa is of the attribute to its possessor (musnad ilayhi).
2
Analyze the answer: reclassification of 'fasl'
The answer states that 'fasl' is built on the pattern of tafa'ul, which here functions as an ism fa'il (active participle), meaning 'the one who distinguishes'. An ism fa'il indicates both a substance (the doer) and a quality (the action).
This resolves the objection because now 'fasl' carries a substance, so the idafa is of an adjective to a described noun that both have substance.
3
Extract the usul principle
The underlying principle is that morphological forms (sighaat) affect meaning. The Hanafi school pays close attention to the distinction between masdar and ism fa'il, as this can change the interpretation of a text.
This principle is applied in usul to determine whether a Quranic expression indicates a singular act or a continuous attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ای الخطاب الفاصل :۔ اس عبارت میں ماین نے سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ سوال کی دو تقریر میں ہیں۔ تقریر اول یہ ہے کہ فصل خطابہ میں صفت کی اضافت ہے ۔ موصوف کی طرف اور قاعدہ ہے۔ صفت کا موصوف پر حمل ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہاں حمل درست نہیں کیونکہ خطاب موضع مسند الیہ میں واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے ذات پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اور فصل مصدر ہے۔ جو صفت پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ تو اس سے صفت کا عمل ذات پر لازم آتا ہے۔ جو درست نہیں ہے۔ جواب : فصل مبنی التفاعل ہے اور فاصل بین الحق والباطل کے معنی میں ہے۔ اور اسم فاعل ذات مع الوصف پر دلالت کرتا
His statement 'ayy al-khitab al-fasil': In this phrase, the matn author answers a question. The question: There are two presentations of the question. The first presentation is that 'fasl al-khitab' is an idafa of the adjective to its described noun, and the rule is that the adjective is predicated on the described noun. Here, predication is not valid because 'khitab' occurs in the position of musnad ilayhi, so it indicates a substance (dhat), and 'fasl' is a masdar (verbal noun) which indicates a quality. This would necessitate attributing a quality to a substance, which is incorrect. The answer: 'Fasl' is built on the pattern of tafa'ul, and it means 'the one who distinguishes between truth and falsehood' (fasil bayn al-haqq wa al-batil). And the ism fa'il (active participle) indicates a substance along with a quality.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage deals with a grammatical analysis of the Quranic phrase 'fasl al-khitab' (decisive speech) from Surah Sad (38:20). The objection is that 'fasl' (distinguishing) is a masdar (verbal noun), and 'khitab' (speech) is a substance; if we take the idafa as adjective + described noun, then we would be predicating a quality (fasl) on a substance (khitab), which is grammatically problematic. The answer is that 'fasl' is not a masdar here but an ism fa'il (active participle) on the pattern of tafa'ul, meaning 'the one who distinguishes' (fasil). An ism fa'il indicates both a substance (dhat) and a quality (sifa), so the predication is correct. This shows the importance of morphological analysis (sarf) in understanding Quranic expressions correctly.

Key Terms
فصل خطاب (fasl al-khitab): Decisive speech; the ability to distinguish truth from falsehood in speech.
اسم فاعل (ism fa'il): An active participle indicating the doer of an action, which carries both substance and quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is 'fasl' interpreted in 'fasl al-khitab' according to the answer in this passage?
A) As a verbal noun (masdar) meaning 'distinguishing'.
B) As an active participle (ism fa'il) meaning 'the one who distinguishes'.
C) As a passive participle (ism maf'ul) meaning 'distinguished'.
D) As a noun of place (ism makan) meaning 'place of distinguishing'.

Key Takeaway
Morphological precision is essential in usul al-fiqh: a single shift from masdar to ism fa'il can resolve a grammatical objection and clarify the meaning of a Quranic phrase.

The Rhetorical Device of Damir Qabl al-Dhikr in Hanafi Usul
Analyzing the rhetorical benefits of opening with a pronoun before referent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of damir qabl al-dhikr and explain the three benefits mentioned by al-Taftazani in the Talwih commentary.

Core Idea
A pronoun before its referent signals the mental presence of the referent – here, Allah’s remembrance in the believer’s heart.

In the opening of the matn al-Tawdih, the author begins with the pronoun 'ilayhi' before mentioning the name 'Allah'. This is not a grammatical error but a deliberate rhetorical device. In this lesson, we will explore why the commentator al-Taftazani praises this opening and what it reveals about the author's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pronoun and its referent
Find the pronoun 'ilayhi' in the matn and determine what it refers to. The referent 'Allah' is mentioned later in the sentence.
The pronoun is attached to the verb yas'adu.
2
Recognize the device: damir qabl al-dhikr
Understand that using a pronoun before mentioning its referent is a known rhetorical figure in Arabic (الضمير قبل الذكر) used to indicate the mental presence of the referent.
3
List the three benefits cited by al-Taftazani
From the text: 1) Indicates the presence of Allah's remembrance in the believer's heart. 2) Shows that Allah is the sole object of praise. 3) Implies that the scholar should direct all his attention toward Allah.
These benefits are explicitly stated in the passage.
4
Examine the refutation of the Basmala objection
The anticipated objection is that if the matn began with Basmala, there would be no pronoun before referent. The author responds that the Basmala can be uttered, thought, or written separately; it does not need to be part of the written text.
This shows the author's careful awareness of potential criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلویح قَولُهُ إِلَيهِ يَصْعَدُ افْتِتَاحٌ غَرِيبٌ وَاقْتِبَاسٌ لَطِيفٌ أَتَى بِالضَّمِيرِ قَبلَ الذِّكرِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى حُضُورٍ ذِكرِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فِى قَلبِ المُؤمِنِ لَا سِيَّمَا عِندَ افْتِتَاحِ الكَلامِ فِي أُصُولِ الشَّرعِ وَإِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى مُتَعَيَّنْ لِتَوَجُهِ المَحَامِدِ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى التصريح بذكرِهِ وَلَا يَذْهَبُ الوَهمُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ إِذ لَهُ العَظَمَةُ وَالجَلالُ وَمِنهُ العَطَاءُ وَالنَّوَالُ وَإِيمَاء إِلَى أَنَّ الشَّارِعَ فِي العُلُومِ الإِسْلَامِيَّةِ يَنبَغِي أَن يَكُونَ مَطْمَعُ نَظَرِهِ وَمَقصَدُ هِمَّتِهِ جَنَابَ الحَقِّ تَعَالَى وَتَقَدَّسَ وَيَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى طَلَب رِضَاهُ وَلَا يَلتَفِتُ إلَى مَا سِوَاهُ لَا يُقَالُ : إِن ابْتَدَأَ المَتنَ بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ فَلا إِصْمَارَ قَبلَ الذِّكرِ وَإِن لَم يَبدَأ لَزِمَ تَركُ العَمَلِ بِالسُّنَّةِ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ يَكفِي فِي الْعَمَلِ بِالسُّنَّةِ أَن تُذكَرَ التَّسْمِيَةُ بِاللَّسَانِ أَو تَخطُرَ بِالبَالِ أَو تُكتَبَ عَلَى قَصدِ التَّبَرُّكِ مِن غَيرِ أَن تُجعَلَ جُزءٌ مِن الكِتَابِ وَعَلَى كُلِّ تَقدِيرٍ يَكُونُ الإِصْمَارُ قَبلَ ذِكرِ المَرْجِعِ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَالصُّعُودُ الحَرَكَةُ مِنَ الأسْفَلِ إِلَى الْعَالِى مَكَانًا وَجِهَةً أَسْتَعِيرَ لِلتَّوَجِهِ إِلَى العَالِى قَدْرًا وَمَرتبَةٌ وَالكَلِمُ مِن الكَلِمَةِ بِمَنزِلَةِ التَّمْرِ مِن السَّمَرَةِ يُفَرَّقُ بَينَ الجِنْسِ وَوَاحِدِهِ بِالتّاءِ وَاللفظ مُفرَدٌ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ كَثِيرًا مَا يُسَمَّى جَمْعًا نَظَرًا إِلَى المَعْنَى الجِنسِي وَلا عَتِبَارِ جَانِبَى اللَّفظِ وَالمَعنَى يَجُوزُ فِي وَصفِهِ التَّذْكِيرُ وَالتَّانِيتُ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كَأَنَّهُم أَعْجَازُ نَحْلٍ مُنقَعِرٍ أَى مُنقَطِع عَن مَغَارِسِهِ سَاقِطٍ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ وَقَالَ كَأَنَّهُم أَعْجَازُ نَحْلِ خَاوِيَةٍ أَى مُتَآكِلَةِ الأجوَافِ ثُمَّ الكَلِمُ غُلبَ عَلَى الكَثِيرِ لَا يُستَعمَلُ فِي الوَاحِدِ البَتَّةَ حَتَّى تَوَهَّمَ بَعضُهُم أَنَّهَا جَمعُ كَلِمَةٍ وَلَيسَ عَلَى حَدٌ تَمرٍ وَتَمرَةٍ إِلَّا أَنَّ الكَلِمَ الطَّيِّبَ بِتَذْكِيرِ الوَصفِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرنَا مَعَ أَنَّ فَعِلا لَيسَ من أبنِيَةِ الجَمعِ فَلَا يَنبَغِي أَن يُشَكَّ فِي أَنَّهُ اسْمُ جَمْعٍ كَتَمَرٍ وَرَكَبٍ وَأَنَّهُ لَيسَ بِجَمع كَنِسَبٍ وَرُتَبٍ فَفِى قَولِهِ وَالكَلِمُ إن كَانَ جَمَعًا خَزَازَةٌ لَا تَحْفَى وَالصَّوَّابُ وَإِن كَانَ بِالْوَاوِ . ترجمہ: قولہ الیہ صعد عجیب افتتاح ہے اور بار یک اقتباس ہے۔ لے آیا ضمیر کو ذکر کرنے سے پہلے دلالت کرتے ہوئے
Talwih: His saying 'Ilayhi yas'adu' is a strange opening and a delicate quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention [of the referent] as an indication of the presence of the remembrance of Allah Almighty in the heart of the believer, especially when opening speech on the principles of the Shari'a, and as a sign that Allah Almighty is specifically the one toward whom praises should be directed; He does not need explicit mention, nor does the mind go to other than Him, for He has greatness and majesty, and from Him is giving and bestowal. And it is a gesture that the scholar of Islamic sciences should make the focus of his vision and the aim of his aspiration the presence of the Exalted and Holy Truth, and should confine himself to seeking His pleasure and not pay attention to anything else. It cannot be said: 'If he began the matn with the Basmala, then there is no pronoun reference before the mention; and if he did not begin, it would be abandoning practice with the Sunnah', because we say: It is sufficient for practicing the Sunnah that the Basmala be mentioned by the tongue, or pass through the mind, or be written with the intention of blessing without making it a part of the book. In any case, the pronoun reference before the mention of the referent occurs in the book. And 'al-ṣuʿūd' (ascent) is movement from a lower to a higher place or direction, borrowed for directing toward what is higher in degree and rank. And 'al-kalim' (words) is to 'kalimah' (word) like 'tamr' (dates) to 'tamrah' (a date); they are distinguished between the genus and its individual by the tā' (feminine suffix). The word is singular except that it is often called a plural due to considering the generic meaning, and without considering both linguistic and meaning aspects, it is permissible to describe it using masculine or feminine. Allah Almighty said: 'as though they were trunks of palm trees uprooted' (54:20), i.e., cut off from their planting places, fallen on the ground; and He said: 'as though they were hollow trunks of palm trees' (69:7), i.e., with hollow interiors. Then 'al-kalim' came to be predominantly used for the many, never used for the singular at all, such that some thought it is the plural of 'kalimah', but it is not on the pattern of 'tamr' and 'tamrah'. However, 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib' (good words) with the masculine description indicates what we mentioned, and since 'faʿil' is not a plural pattern, there should be no doubt that it is a collective noun like 'tamr' and 'rakab', and that it is not a plural like 'nisab' and 'rutab'. So in his saying 'wa al-kalim in kāna jamʿan' there is subtlety not hidden, and the correct is 'wa in kāna bi al-wāw'. Translation: His saying 'ilayhi yas'adu' is a strange opening and a delicate quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention indicating...
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is Talwih (super-commentary by Taftazani) on the opening words of Al-Tawdih. The author analyzes why the matn author began with the pronoun 'ilayhi' (to Him) before mentioning the noun. He lists several rhetorical benefits: (1) it indicates that the remembrance of Allah is present in the heart of the believer, especially when discussing usul al-fiqh; (2) it shows that Allah is the only true object of praise; (3) it implies that the scholar should direct all his attention toward Allah. The author then anticipates and refutes an objection regarding the absence of explicit Basmala. He explains that practicing the Sunnah of Basmala does not require it to be written in the book; it can be uttered, thought, or written separately. Then he analyzes the word 'kalim' in Q. 54:20 and 69:7, arguing that 'kalim' is a collective noun (ism jam'), not a plural (jam'). He supports this with linguistic evidence, including that 'faʿil' is not a pattern for plurals and that masculine description (al-kalim al-ṭayyib) is used analogously to other collective nouns like 'tamr' and 'rakab'. This is a refinement of the matn's reading, showing that Taftazani corrects a possible misunderstanding.

Key Terms
ضمیر قبل الذکر (ḍamīr qabl al-dhikr): A pronoun used before its referent is explicitly mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Talwih, what is the primary reason the matn author began with the pronoun 'ilayhi' before mentioning 'Allah'?
A) To make the sentence grammatically easier.
B) To show that the remembrance of Allah is already present in the believer's heart.
C) To avoid repeating the word 'Allah'.
D) To follow the style of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The use of damir qabl al-dhikr in the opening of a Hanafi usul text is a deliberate rhetorical choice to signal the mental presence of the referent and to orient the reader's focus.

The Linguistic Status of 'Kalim' as a Collective Noun (Ism Jam')
Linguistic analysis of 'kalim' as an ism jam' with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ism jam' and jam' and explain why the Hanafi tradition treats 'kalim' as a collective noun (ism jam') using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Kalim is a collective noun like 'tamr', not a plural; this affects grammatical agreement in Quranic interpretation.

In the Talwih commentary, al-Taftazani addresses a common misconception: that the word 'kalim' (words) in the Quran is a plural of 'kalimah'. He argues that it is actually a collective noun (ism jam'), similar to 'tamr' (dates). This distinction has implications for how we understand Quranic phrases like 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib' and the verses about palm trunks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word under analysis
The word 'kalim' appears in the phrase 'wa al-kalimu' in the matn. The commentator is analyzing its linguistic category.
2
Recall the two categories: jam' (plural) vs ism jam' (collective noun)
Jam' is the regular plural pattern (e.g., nisab, rutab). Ism jam' is a singular form that indicates a group, like 'tamr' (dates) and 'rakab' (riders).
Ism jam' does not have a regular plural suffix and is treated as singular for grammar.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The commentator cites Q. 54:20 and 69:7 which describe palm trunks (نَحْل). He shows that 'nahal' is used both with masculine (munqa'ir) and feminine (khawiya) descriptions, reflecting its nature as a collective noun.
This is the dalil from the source text.
4
Apply the principle to 'kalim'
Like 'nahal' and 'tamr', 'kalim' is on the pattern 'fa'il', which is a pattern for collective nouns, not for plurals. The masculine description in 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib' further supports this.
The author corrects those who mistakenly thought kalim is a plural.
5
Understand the refinement in the matn reading
The matn originally said 'wa al-kalimu in kāna jamʿan' (if it is a plural), but the commentator suggests the correct reading should be 'wa in kāna bi al-wāw' (and if it is with the waw), indicating it is not a plural.
This is a critical refinement of the textual reading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلویح قَولُهُ إِلَيهِ يَصْعَدُ افْتِتَاحٌ غَرِيبٌ وَاقْتِبَاسٌ لَطِيفٌ أَتَى بِالضَّمِيرِ قَبلَ الذِّكرِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى حُضُورٍ ذِكرِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فِى قَلبِ المُؤمِنِ لَا سِيَّمَا عِندَ افْتِتَاحِ الكَلامِ فِي أُصُولِ الشَّرعِ وَإِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى مُتَعَيَّنْ لِتَوَجُهِ المَحَامِدِ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى التصريح بذكرِهِ وَلَا يَذْهَبُ الوَهمُ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ إِذ لَهُ العَظَمَةُ وَالجَلالُ وَمِنهُ العَطَاءُ وَالنَّوَالُ وَإِيمَاء إِلَى أَنَّ الشَّارِعَ فِي العُلُومِ الإِسْلَامِيَّةِ يَنبَغِي أَن يَكُونَ مَطْمَعُ نَظَرِهِ وَمَقصَدُ هِمَّتِهِ جَنَابَ الحَقِّ تَعَالَى وَتَقَدَّسَ وَيَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى طَلَب رِضَاهُ وَلَا يَلتَفِتُ إلَى مَا سِوَاهُ لَا يُقَالُ : إِن ابْتَدَأَ المَتنَ بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ فَلا إِصْمَارَ قَبلَ الذِّكرِ وَإِن لَم يَبدَأ لَزِمَ تَركُ العَمَلِ بِالسُّنَّةِ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ يَكفِي فِي الْعَمَلِ بِالسُّنَّةِ أَن تُذكَرَ التَّسْمِيَةُ بِاللَّسَانِ أَو تَخطُرَ بِالبَالِ أَو تُكتَبَ عَلَى قَصدِ التَّبَرُّكِ مِن غَيرِ أَن تُجعَلَ جُزءٌ مِن الكِتَابِ وَعَلَى كُلِّ تَقدِيرٍ يَكُونُ الإِصْمَارُ قَبلَ ذِكرِ المَرْجِعِ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَالصُّعُودُ الحَرَكَةُ مِنَ الأسْفَلِ إِلَى الْعَالِى مَكَانًا وَجِهَةً أَسْتَعِيرَ لِلتَّوَجِهِ إِلَى العَالِى قَدْرًا وَمَرتبَةٌ وَالكَلِمُ مِن الكَلِمَةِ بِمَنزِلَةِ التَّمْرِ مِن السَّمَرَةِ يُفَرَّقُ بَينَ الجِنْسِ وَوَاحِدِهِ بِالتّاءِ وَاللفظ مُفرَدٌ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ كَثِيرًا مَا يُسَمَّى جَمْعًا نَظَرًا إِلَى المَعْنَى الجِنسِي وَلا عَتِبَارِ جَانِبَى اللَّفظِ وَالمَعنَى يَجُوزُ فِي وَصفِهِ التَّذْكِيرُ وَالتَّانِيتُ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كَأَنَّهُم أَعْجَازُ نَحْلٍ مُنقَعِرٍ أَى مُنقَطِع عَن مَغَارِسِهِ سَاقِطٍ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ وَقَالَ كَأَنَّهُم أَعْجَازُ نَحْلِ خَاوِيَةٍ أَى مُتَآكِلَةِ الأجوَافِ ثُمَّ الكَلِمُ غُلبَ عَلَى الكَثِيرِ لَا يُستَعمَلُ فِي الوَاحِدِ البَتَّةَ حَتَّى تَوَهَّمَ بَعضُهُم أَنَّهَا جَمعُ كَلِمَةٍ وَلَيسَ عَلَى حَدٌ تَمرٍ وَتَمرَةٍ إِلَّا أَنَّ الكَلِمَ الطَّيِّبَ بِتَذْكِيرِ الوَصفِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرنَا مَعَ أَنَّ فَعِلا لَيسَ من أبنِيَةِ الجَمعِ فَلَا يَنبَغِي أَن يُشَكَّ فِي أَنَّهُ اسْمُ جَمْعٍ كَتَمَرٍ وَرَكَبٍ وَأَنَّهُ لَيسَ بِجَمع كَنِسَبٍ وَرُتَبٍ فَفِى قَولِهِ وَالكَلِمُ إن كَانَ جَمَعًا خَزَازَةٌ لَا تَحْفَى وَالصَّوَّابُ وَإِن كَانَ بِالْوَاوِ . ترجمہ: قولہ الیہ صعد عجیب افتتاح ہے اور بار یک اقتباس ہے۔ لے آیا ضمیر کو ذکر کرنے سے پہلے دلالت کرتے ہوئے
Talwih: His saying 'Ilayhi yas'adu' is a strange opening and a delicate quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention [of the referent] as an indication of the presence of the remembrance of Allah Almighty in the heart of the believer, especially when opening speech on the principles of the Shari'a, and as a sign that Allah Almighty is specifically the one toward whom praises should be directed; He does not need explicit mention, nor does the mind go to other than Him, for He has greatness and majesty, and from Him is giving and bestowal. And it is a gesture that the scholar of Islamic sciences should make the focus of his vision and the aim of his aspiration the presence of the Exalted and Holy Truth, and should confine himself to seeking His pleasure and not pay attention to anything else. It cannot be said: 'If he began the matn with the Basmala, then there is no pronoun reference before the mention; and if he did not begin, it would be abandoning practice with the Sunnah', because we say: It is sufficient for practicing the Sunnah that the Basmala be mentioned by the tongue, or pass through the mind, or be written with the intention of blessing without making it a part of the book. In any case, the pronoun reference before the mention of the referent occurs in the book. And 'al-ṣuʿūd' (ascent) is movement from a lower to a higher place or direction, borrowed for directing toward what is higher in degree and rank. And 'al-kalim' (words) is to 'kalimah' (word) like 'tamr' (dates) to 'tamrah' (a date); they are distinguished between the genus and its individual by the tā' (feminine suffix). The word is singular except that it is often called a plural due to considering the generic meaning, and without considering both linguistic and meaning aspects, it is permissible to describe it using masculine or feminine. Allah Almighty said: 'as though they were trunks of palm trees uprooted' (54:20), i.e., cut off from their planting places, fallen on the ground; and He said: 'as though they were hollow trunks of palm trees' (69:7), i.e., with hollow interiors. Then 'al-kalim' came to be predominantly used for the many, never used for the singular at all, such that some thought it is the plural of 'kalimah', but it is not on the pattern of 'tamr' and 'tamrah'. However, 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib' (good words) with the masculine description indicates what we mentioned, and since 'faʿil' is not a plural pattern, there should be no doubt that it is a collective noun like 'tamr' and 'rakab', and that it is not a plural like 'nisab' and 'rutab'. So in his saying 'wa al-kalim in kāna jamʿan' there is subtlety not hidden, and the correct is 'wa in kāna bi al-wāw'. Translation: His saying 'ilayhi yas'adu' is a strange opening and a delicate quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention indicating...
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is Talwih (super-commentary by Taftazani) on the opening words of Al-Tawdih. The author analyzes why the matn author began with the pronoun 'ilayhi' (to Him) before mentioning the noun. He lists several rhetorical benefits: (1) it indicates that the remembrance of Allah is present in the heart of the believer, especially when discussing usul al-fiqh; (2) it shows that Allah is the only true object of praise; (3) it implies that the scholar should direct all his attention toward Allah. The author then anticipates and refutes an objection regarding the absence of explicit Basmala. He explains that practicing the Sunnah of Basmala does not require it to be written in the book; it can be uttered, thought, or written separately. Then he analyzes the word 'kalim' in Q. 54:20 and 69:7, arguing that 'kalim' is a collective noun (ism jam'), not a plural (jam'). He supports this with linguistic evidence, including that 'faʿil' is not a pattern for plurals and that masculine description (al-kalim al-ṭayyib) is used analogously to other collective nouns like 'tamr' and 'rakab'. This is a refinement of the matn's reading, showing that Taftazani corrects a possible misunderstanding.

Key Terms
کلم (kalim): A collective noun for 'words', not the plural of 'kalimah'.
اسم جمع (ism jamʿ): A collective noun that indicates a group but is singular in form.
نَحْل (nahal): Palm trees as a collective noun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does the commentator use to support classifying 'kalim' as an ism jam'?
A) That it cannot be used for a single word.
B) That it is on the pattern 'fa'il', which is not a pattern for plurals, and the Quranic example of 'nahal'.
C) That it is always used with feminine adjectives.
D) That it is derived from 'kalimah' by removing the 'hah'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the classification of nouns like 'kalim' as ism jam' rather than jam' is based on linguistic pattern analysis and Quranic evidence, affecting how we interpret scriptural language.

The Allusion to the Good Tree in Praises: A Hanafi Textual Analysis
Expansion of a talmih with objection-resolution structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a talmih (allusion) in a matn, explain how the commentator expands it using a Quranic verse, and distinguish between linguistic and terminological definitions in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Praises of Allah have roots (faith) and branches (deeds); the matn's description alludes to the Quranic tree.

This lesson examines how a Hanafi commentator unpacks a subtle allusion (talmih) in the matn. The author's description of praiseworthy qualities (mahamid) as having roots from the sources of Sharia and branches in the heavens is shown to be an echo of the Quranic parable of the good tree. Through a structured objection and answer, the commentator deepens the understanding of hamd, revealing it to be a compound concept encompassing belief, speech, and action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the talmih
Locate the matn's description that hints at the Quranic tree. The matn says: the mahamid have roots from the sources of Sharia and branches in the heavens. This is the talmih.
Talmih is a rhetorical device where a text alludes to a well-known verse, story, or figure without explicit mention.
2
Locate the Quranic verse
Recognize the allusion to Surah Ibrahim 14:24: 'Do you not see how Allah sets forth a parable: a good word is like a good tree, its root firm and its branches in the sky.' The commentator explicitly cites this verse.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah, used as a primary proof.
3
Follow the expansion
The commentator breaks down the tree analogy: root = faith (iman, i'tiqadat), trunk = verbal praise (al-hamd al-lafzi), branches = righteous deeds (a'mal, ta'at). He cites Imam Razi to argue that hamd is not merely verbal but encompasses all that indicates Allah's greatness.
The expansion uses the Quranic dalil to derive a compound definition of hamd.
4
Trace the objection and resolution
An objection arises: the tree is compound (roots, trunk, branches) while praise is simple (only verbal). The resolution distinguishes linguistic hamd (basit, verbal only) from terminological hamd (murakkab, including belief and deeds). The talmih is valid because the matn uses the terminological sense.
This is a classic Hanafi usul method: resolving apparent contradictions by distinguishing levels of meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ
و حكامٍ وَأَشَارَ إِلَى الاحْتِصَاصِ وَالدَّوَامِ بِقَولِهِ إِلَيْهِ يَصْعَدُ الْكَلِمُ بِتَقْدِيمِ الطَّرْفِ
المُفِيدِ لِلاحْتِصَاصِ وَلَفظِ المُضَارِع المُنبِى عَن الاستمرار. ترجمہ: پھر محامد کی صفت ذکر کرنے میں اس شے کے ساتھ جس کا ذکر کیا ماتن نے اشارہ ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول ضرب اللہ مثلا کلمہ طیبہ کشجرہ طیبہ الخ کی طرف اس لیے کہ جب محامد کلم طبیب ہیں اور کلمہ طیبہ پاکیزہ درخت کی طرح ہے تو حمدہ ایسا درخت ہو سکی جڑ ہے اور وہ ہے ایمان اور اعتقادات اور فرع ہے اور وہ اعمال اور طاعات ہیں۔ اور تحقیق اس کی یہ ہے کہ حمد اگر چہ لغت میں خاص طور پر زبان کا فعل ہے۔ مگر اللہ تعالیٰ کی حمد جیسا کہ امام رازی نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ اپنی تفسیر میں صرف کہنے والے کا الحمد للہ کہنا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ہر وہ چیز جو مشیر ہو اس کی عظمت کی طرف اور خبر دے اس کی بزرگی کی صفات کمال کے ساتھ متصف ہونے کے اعتقاد کے ساتھ اور اس کی ترجمانی کرنے کے ساتھ کلام کے ذریعہ اور ساتھ لانے ان اعمال کے جو اس پر دلاٹ کریں۔ پس اعتقاد جڑ ہے۔ اگر یہ نہ ہو تو حد ہو گی مثل خبیث درخت کے جو زمین کے اوپرا کھڑا ہوا ہو اس کو قرار حاصل نہ ہو۔ اور عمل ٹہنی ہے۔ اگر یہ نہ ہو تو حمد کو نماء ( بڑھوتری) حاصل نہ ہو ۔ اور اس کے ہاں قبولیت حاصل نہ ہو مثل اس تنے کے جس کی ٹہنیاں نہ ہوں۔ اور اس درخت کے جس پر پھل نہ ہو۔ اس لیے کہ عمل ہی وسیلہ ہے جنات کو حاصل کرنے کا " درجات کو بلند کرنے کا اللہ تعالیٰ فرماتے ہیں کہ عمل صالح اس کو بلند کرتا ہے۔ اور حدیث میں ہے جب اس کے لیے عمل صالح نہ ہو تو اس کو (حمد کو) قبول نہیں کیا جاتا ۔ پس مصنف نے اشارہ کیا کہ محامد کے درخت کے لیے ایک مضبوط جڑ ہے۔ اور وہ مضبوط اسلامی عقیدہ ہے جس کی بنیاد علم تو حید و صفات پر رکھی گئی ہے۔ اور ایک فرع ہے جو بڑھنے والی ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف اس کے ہاں مقبول ہے اور وہ عمل صالح ہے جو شرعیت مطہرہ کے موافق ہو جس کی بنیاد علم شرائع اور احکام پر رکھی گئی ہے اور اشارہ کیا اختصاص اور دوام کی طرف اپنے قول الیہ یصعد الکلم الطیب سے ظرف کو مقدم کرنے کے ساتھ جو مفید ہے اختصاص کے
لیے اور لفظ مضارع کے ساتھ جو خبر دینے والا ہے استمرار (ہمیشگی )
لغوى تحقيق: - يشعر : دلالت کرنا، ترجمه عنوان، تر جمانی کرنا
اجتشت: اجتثا نما بیخ کنی کرنا۔ جڑ سے اکھیڑنا اصل میں اختیست تھا پھر پہلی ٹاء کو ساکن کیا پھر ٹا ء کا ثا ء میں ادغام کر دیا۔
دوحة : بڑا درخت بڑا سائبان
المنبنی : از افعال خبر دینے والا ۔
تشریح ثم في وصف المحامد : یہ عبارت کا پندرھواں حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے متن کی خوبی بیان کی ہے۔ کہ متن میں محامد کی جو صفت ذکر کی ہے (الاصولہا من مشارع الشرع والی صفت) اس سے ماتن نے قرآن مجید کی آیت کے مضمون کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے وہ اسطرح کہ اللہ نے ارشاد فرمایا ضرب الله مثلا کلمہ طیبہ اصلحها ثابت وفرعها فی السماء باقی رہا کہ اشارہ کیسے ہو گیا کیونکہ الحامد یہ بیان ہے الکلم الطیب کا اور مین (با نفتح) اور منین (بالکسر ) میں اتحاد ہوتا ہے۔ پس محامد یہ بعینہا کم طیب ہوئے اور قرآن کریم میں کلمہ طیبہ کو تشبیہ دی گئی شجرہ طیبہ کے ساتھ اور یہ بعینہ حمد کو تشبیہ دینا ہے شجرہ طیبہ کے ساتھ وجہ تشبیہ ظاہر ہے کہ شجرہ میں تین چیزیں ہیں (۱) جڑیں (۱) تنا (۳) شاخیں۔ بالکل ایسے ہی حمد میں بھی تین چیزیں ہیں ۔ (۱)
جڑیں۔ یہ ایمان اور اعتقاد ہے۔ (۲) تناوہ حمد ہے (۳) اس کی شاخیں یہ اعمال ہیں۔
تحقیق ڈلک :۔ یہ عبارت کا سولہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال: کہ یہ تشبیہ درست نہیں کیونکہ مشبہ بہ (شجر ) مرکب ہے۔ اور اصول و فروع اسمیں داخل ہیں۔ اس کے جز ہیں ۔ جبکہ مشبہ (حمد) بسیط ہے۔ اس کا تعلق صرف زبان سے ہے۔ جبکہ اعتقاد کا تعلق دل سے ہے۔ اور اعمال کا تعلق اعضاء سے ہے۔ تو یہ حمد کے اجزاء اصول و فروع کیسے بن سکتے ہیں۔
جواب:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حمد لغوی تو زبان کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور بسیط ہے لیکن حمد اصطلاحی مرکب ہے کیونکہ زبان سے الحمد للہ کہنا حد نہیں یہ تو حمد کے صدور کی خبر دینا ہے۔ حمد ہر اس فعل کو کہتے ہیں جو باری تعالیٰ کی عظمت پر دال ہو چاہے دل سے یا زبان سے ہو یا اعضاء سے ہو تو اعتقاد بمنزل اصل کے ہے اس کے بغیر اللہ کی تعریف شجرہ خبیثہ کی طرح ہے جو زمین کے اوپر پڑا ہو اور اس کو قرار حاصل نہ ہو اور اعمال کے بغیر حمد ایسے ہے جیسے درخت کا تنا بغیر ٹہنیوں اور بغیر پھلوں کے ہو تو اعمال بمنزل فرع کے ہیں حمد کے لیے۔
امام رازی کے کلام سے مقصود تشبیہ الحمد لشجرہ کی تائید پیش کرنا ہے
سوال:۔ یہ تحقیق تب تام ہو سکتی ہے۔ کہ محامد کی طرح کلم طبیب بھی مرکب و عام ہو ۔ اس کے مفہوم میں بھی اعتقاد عمل صالح داخل ہوں حالانکہ حکم طبیب کا معنی و مفہوم اس طرح کسی نے بیان نہیں کیا اور کم طیب میں اس عموم کا پایا جاتا اس لیے ضروری ہے کہ ماتن نے محامد کو کم طبیب کا بیان بنایا ہے ۔ لہذا جب امام رازی کی تفسیر کے مطابق محامد مرکب ہیں تو پھر کم طیب کا مفہوم بھی
At-Tarwih li Hall at-Tawdih wa at-Talwih. And he indicated exclusivity and continuity by his saying 'To Him ascends the good word' by placing the adverbial phrase first which benefits exclusivity, and by the imperfect verb which indicates continuity. Translation: Then in describing the praises along with that which the author mentioned, he alluded to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Allah sets forth a parable: a good word like a good tree...' because when the praiseworthy things are good words and the good word is like a pure tree, then praise is like a tree: its root is faith and beliefs, and its branch is deeds and acts of obedience. And the verification of this is that praise, although in language is specifically an act of the tongue, but praise of Allah the Exalted, as Imam Razi clarified in his commentary, is not merely the speaker saying 'al-hamdu lillah'. Rather, it is everything that indicates His greatness, informs of His majesty, with the belief that He is characterized with perfect attributes, and expresses that through speech and through accompanying deeds that demonstrate it. So belief is the root; if it is not present, it becomes like a filthy tree standing above ground with no stability. And deed is the branch; if it is not present, praise has no growth and no acceptance, like a trunk without branches and a tree without fruit. Because deed is the means to attain gardens and raise ranks; Allah says that righteous deed elevates it. And in hadith, when there is no righteous deed for it, praise is not accepted. So the author indicated that the tree of praises has a strong root — that strong Islamic creed based on tawhid and attributes — and a growing branch that is accepted by Allah, which is righteous deed according to pure sharia, based on knowledge of laws and rulings. And he indicated exclusivity and continuity by his saying 'To Him ascends the good word' by placing the adverb first for exclusivity and the imperfect verb for continuity. Lexical verification: yash'ur: indicates, tarjama: interpret, tarjuman: interpreter. ijtashat: uprooted, originally ikhtashat, then the first ta' was made silent, then the ta' was assimilated into the tha'. dawha: large tree, large canopy. al-munbini: derived from af'al, indicating. Clarification: 'Then in describing the praises' is the fifteenth part of the text. In this part, the commentator explains the excellence of the matn: that the author, in mentioning the attribute of praises ('their roots are from the sources of sharia' etc.), alluded to the meaning of a Quranic verse, that is, Allah said: 'Allah sets forth a parable: a good word, its root is firm and its branch is in the sky.' He asked how the allusion is made, because 'praiseworthy things' (al-mahamid) is an expression of 'good word' (al-kalim at-tayyib), and there is agreement between 'muhammad' (with fatha) and 'muhammad' (with kasra). So the praiseworthy things are exactly good words, and in the Quran the good word is likened to a good tree, and this is exactly likening praise to a good tree. The aspect of comparison is clear: the tree has three things: roots, trunk, and branches; similarly praise has three things: roots (faith and belief), trunk (the act of praising), and branches (deeds). Verification of this: This is the sixteenth part of the text. The purpose is to answer a presumed objection. Objection: This comparison is not valid because the object of comparison (the tree) is compound, having roots and branches as parts, while the subject of comparison (praise) is simple, related only to the tongue, whereas belief relates to the heart and deeds to the limbs; so how can these be parts, roots, and branches of praise? Answer: The gist is that praise linguistically is specific to the tongue and simple, but praise terminologically is compound, because merely saying 'al-hamdu lillah' with the tongue is not the limit; rather it informs of the occurrence of praise. Praise is every act that indicates the greatness of the Creator, whether from the heart, tongue, or limbs. So belief is like the root; without it, praising Allah is like a filthy tree lying above ground without stability. And without deeds, praise is like a tree trunk without branches and fruit; so deeds are like the branches for praise. The purpose of mentioning Imam Razi's statement is to support the likening of praise to a tree. Objection: This verification can only be complete if the good word (kalim tayyib) is also compound and general, including belief and righteous deed in its meaning, whereas no one has explained the meaning of 'good word' in that way, and the word 'good' (tayyib) does not include this generality. So it is necessary that the author made the praiseworthy things an expression of the good word. Thus when, according to Imam Razi's commentary, praiseworthy things are compound, then the meaning of 'good word' is also...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn, specifically explaining a literary device (talmīḥ, allusion) used by the author. The author had described the 'praises' (maḥāmid) as having roots from the sources of Sharia and branches in the heavens. The commentator points out that this is an allusion to the Quranic verse (Ibrahim 14:24) where a good word (kalimah ṭayyibah) is likened to a good tree with firm roots and branches in the sky. The commentator then expands on the analogy: just as a tree has roots, trunk, and branches, so too does praise (ḥamd) have roots (īmān and beliefs), a trunk (the verbal expression of praise), and branches (good deeds). He cites Imam Razi to argue that praise is not merely verbal but includes inner belief and outward actions. Then a question arises: how can praise be likened to a tree when the tree is compound and praise is simple? The answer distinguishes between linguistic and terminological praise: terminologically, praise is every act indicating Allah's greatness, so it is compound. The passage ends mid-objection about whether 'good word' also includes this generality. This is a classic Hanafi usul exercise in textual analysis, showing how a matn's wording can carry deeper allusions and how objections are resolved.

Key Terms
تلميح (talmīḥ): A literary allusion in the matn to a Quranic verse, where the description of mahamid hints at the tree parable.
محامد (maḥāmid): Praiseworthy acts or qualities of Allah; in this context, the subject of the analogy, comprising belief, verbal praise, and deeds.
كلم طيب (kalim ṭayyib): Literally 'good word'; in the Quranic verse, it refers to the declaration of tawhid, but the commentator expands it to include all forms of praise.
بسيط/مركب (basīṭ / murakkab): Simple vs. compound; praise is linguistically simple (only verbal) but terminologically compound (includes belief and deeds).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the analogy presented in the passage, what do the 'roots' of the tree of praise represent?
A) The verbal utterance of praise
B) Belief and faith
C) Righteous deeds
D) The sources of Sharia

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi textual analysis, recognizing a talmih allows the commentator to expand the meaning of a term using a Quranic dalil, distinguishing between linguistic and terminological definitions to resolve apparent contradictions.

Tree Analogy: Praise Requires Righteous Deeds
Commentary on Imam Razi's tree analogy for hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relationship between verbal praise and righteous deeds in Hanafi usul, and explain the textual evidence for their interconnection.

Core Idea
Praise without righteous deeds is like a tree without branches — acceptance requires both.

This lesson explores a commentary on Imam Razi's tree analogy for praise (hamd). The commentator uses this analogy to demonstrate that verbal praise (hamd lisani) must be accompanied by righteous deeds (amal salih) for it to be accepted. We will examine the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish this relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core analogy
The commentator compares hamd to a tree. Understand that the root represents faith (i'tiqad) and the branches represent righteous deeds (a'mal).
This is a visual aid to show that both are essential.
2
Extract the legal implication
The analogy shows that praise without deeds is incomplete, implying that deeds are a condition (shart) for acceptance of praise.
This is a key usul point: a condition for validity.
3
Locate the textual proofs
The commentator cites Quran 16:32 ('Enter Paradise because of what you used to do'), Quran 35:10 ('Good words ascend... righteous deed raises it'), and a hadith ('When there is no righteous deed, it is not accepted'). Identify how each proof links deeds to acceptance.
These are the primary dalil for the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the Hanafi usul principle
The use of the preposition 'ba' in the verse indicates causation (sababiyya). In Hanafi usul, such a clear causal link is considered qat'i in indicating that deeds are the cause of reward.
This is a linguistic argument central to the derivation.
5
Contrast with opposing view
The Murji'ah claim that faith alone suffices. Compare their interpretation (ba' as accompaniment) with the Hanafi interpretation (ba' as causation). Understand the practical difference: a person who praises without deeds is not accepted according to Hanafi view.
This highlights the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب:۔ مصنف کا مقصد امام رازی کے کلام سے اس کی تائید پیش کرنا ہے کہ حمد کی تشبیہ درخت کے ساتھ درست ہے حمد کی تعمیم یا ترکیب مقصود نہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ امام رازی کی تفسیر کے مطابق اعتقاد و عمل صالح کو حمد لسانی ولغوی کے ساتھ ایک خاص نسبت حاصل ہوگی کہ جس طرح درخت بغیر جڑ کے بے کار ہے اس طرح محمد بغیر اعتقاد و ایمان کے بے کار ہے۔ اور جس طرح درخت کے لیے ٹہنیاں کمال اور خوبصورتی کی درجہ رکھتی ہیں اسی طرح محمد لسانی کے لیے اعمال تحمیل کا درجہ رکھتے ہیں یعنی اگر حمہ ہو عمل صالح نہ ہو تو وہ ایسے ہے کہ درخت بغیر پھل وٹہنیوں کے ہو۔ اذا العمل : یہ جملہ معترضہ ہے اور اس میں شارخ نے اعمال کے بغیر حمد کی عدم قبولیت کی علت بیان کی ہے۔ لقولہ تعالٰی ادخلو الجنہ بما كنتم تعملون جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اعمال کی وجہ سے جنت حاصل ہوگی اور رفع درجات ہو گا اس لیے قرآن میں ہے وا مل الصالح يرفعہ یعنی کلمہ طیبہ کو اللہ کی دربار میں عمل صالح بلند کرتا ہے۔ اور قبولیت بخشتا ہے۔ اور حدیث میں ہے کہ اذلم یکن له عمل الصالح لم يقبل یعنی عمل صالح نہ ہو تو قبولیت حاصل نہیں ہوتی۔
Answer: The author's purpose is to present support from Imam Razi's words that the simile of praise (hamd) to a tree is correct. Generalization or composition of praise is not intended. The conclusion is that according to Imam Razi's interpretation, belief and righteous deeds have a special relationship with linguistic and lexical praise. Just as a tree without roots is useless, similarly Muhammad (?) without belief and faith is useless. And just as for a tree, branches have the level of perfection and beauty, similarly for linguistic praise, deeds of carrying (?) have the level of perfection. That is, if there is praise but no righteous deed, then it is like a tree without fruit and branches. 'Therefore action': This is a parenthetical sentence, and in it the commentator explains the cause of the non-acceptance of praise without actions. Due to His saying: 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do' (Quran 16:32). The conclusion is that through actions, Paradise is attained and degrees are raised. That is why in the Quran: 'Good words ascend to Him, and righteous deed raises it' (35:10). That is, righteous deeds raise the good word to Allah's court and grant acceptance. And in the hadith: 'When there is no righteous deed, it is not accepted.'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's (probably from Al-Tawdih) analogy between praise (hamd) and a tree. The commentator explains that just as a tree needs roots and branches to be complete, praise needs belief (root) and righteous deeds (branches). The parenthetical remark 'Therefore action' provides the illah (cause) for non-acceptance: deeds are necessary. The proof is the verse 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do' and the hadith that without righteous deeds, praise is not accepted. This is a standard Hanafi position that faith and works are inseparable for acceptance.

Key Terms
حمد لسانی (hamd lisānī): Linguistic praise with the tongue.
عمل صالح (‘amal ṣāliḥ): Righteous deed that accompanies praise for acceptance.

Key Takeaway
Righteous deeds are a necessary condition for the acceptance of verbal praise in Hanafi usul, as established by Quranic and hadith proofs.

Entering Paradise: Cause or Reward
Three answers reconciling Quran and Hadith on entry to Paradise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of reconciling apparently contradictory Quranic and Hadith texts by identifying the linguistic category of 'ba' (causal vs. compensatory) and distinguishing between basic entry and degrees in Paradise.

Core Idea
Entering Paradise is by mercy; deeds are the compensation or the means to higher degrees.

This lesson addresses a classic usul challenge: how to reconcile a Quranic verse that appears to make deeds the cause of entering Paradise with a hadith that declares no one enters by deeds alone. The Hanafi school resolves this through precise grammatical analysis of the preposition 'ba' and by distinguishing between basic entry and degrees. You will explore three Hanafi interpretations and learn which is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two seemingly conflicting texts
Locate the Quranic verse (implied: 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do') and the hadith ('None of you will enter Paradise by his deeds unless Allah envelops him with His mercy'). Note the apparent contradiction: the verse suggests deeds cause entry, the hadith denies it.
The hadith is mutawatir and qat'i al-thubut.
2
Analyze the grammatical role of 'ba'
In the verse, the preposition 'ba' (ب) before 'what you used to do' can be either causal (sababiyya) or compensatory ('iwadiyya). The Hanafi scholars examine the linguistic context to determine which meaning resolves the conflict.
The choice of interpretation affects the theological implication.
3
Examine the three Hanafi reconciliations
Work through each of the three answers provided in the text: Answer (1) 'ba' is compensatory, so deeds are the exchange for Paradise, not the cause; Answer (2) 'ba' is causal but only apparent, the real cause is Allah's grace; Answer (3) the verse refers to attaining degrees, not basic entry.
Each answer resolves the contradiction by reinterpreting either the preposition or the subject.
4
Determine the preferred view
Identify why the Hanafi school gives tarjih to the third answer: basic entry is by grace, degrees are by deeds. This aligns with Quran 46:19 and preserves both texts without forcing the grammar.
This view also avoids the Mu'tazili position that deeds necessitate entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دخول جنت کا سبب اللہ کا فضل اور احسان ہے
سوال:۔ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اولوالجیہ بما نتم تعملون میں ہاسپیہ ہے تو دخول جنت مسبب ہوگا اور مسبب بغیر سبب کے نہیں پایا جا تا تو لازم آئے گا کہ بغیر عمل کے جنت میں جائے گا ہی نہیں حالانکہ ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ ان احد کم لا یدخلہ الجزیہ عملہ الا ان یغمد اللہ برحمتہ یعنی تم میں سے کسی کو بھی اس کا عمل جنت میں داخل نہیں کرے گا مگر جب اللہ تعالی س کو اپنی رحمت میں ڈھانپ لیں۔ جواب (1) : ۔ آیت میں باسیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ عوضیہ ہے اور یہ اعراض پر داخل ہوتی ہے یعنی عمل صالح کا عوض اور بدلہ جنت ہے اور ضابطہ ہے کہ معطی کو معطی ونٹی کبھی بغیر عوض اور بغیر بدلہ کے بھی عطاء کر دیتا ہے بخلاف ہاسبیہ کے کہ اس صورت میں عمل صالح دخول جنت کا سبب ہوگا ۔ اور مسبب بغیر سبب کے نہیں پایا جاتا۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ آیت میں ہا عوضیہ ہے اور آئمیں یہ بیان اور کیا گیا ہے کہ عمل صالح کا عوض جنت ہے اور حدیث میں یہ بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ دخول جنت کا سبب اللہ تعالیٰ کا فضل و احسان ہے لہذا آیت و حدیث میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔
با
جواب (۲) ۔ آیت میں باسی یہ ہے لیکن یہ ظاہر حال پرمحمول ہے تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ دخول جنت کا ظاہری سبب اعمال صالحہ ہیں حقیقی سبب تفضل باری تعالی ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ آیت ظاہری سبب پر محمول ہے اور حدیث تفضل و احسان باری پر محمول ہے۔
جواب (۳):۔ دخول جنت تو خدا کے فضل و احسان پر موقوف ہے لیکن جنت میں نیل درجات اعمال صالحہ پر موقوف ہیں۔ کما قال اللہ ولکل درجات مما عملوا لیکن اس صورت میں آیت حذف مضاف کے قبیل ہوگی ۔ ادخلوالجربہ (ای دور جاتھا) بما کنتم تعملون ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ آیت میں نیل درجات کا ذکر ہے اور حدیث دخول جنت پر محمول ہے کہ دخول جنت تفضل پر موقوف ہے۔
The cause of entering Paradise is Allah's grace and favor.
Question: It occurs that in 'with what you used to do' the 'ba' is causal (sababiyya), so entering Paradise would be a result, and a result cannot exist without a cause. Then it would necessitate that without deeds one would not enter Paradise at all, whereas a hadith says: 'None of you will enter Paradise by his deeds unless Allah envelops him with His mercy.' Answer (1): In the verse, the 'ba' is not causal but compensatory ('iwadiyya), and it enters upon the exchange, meaning that righteous deeds are the exchange and reward for Paradise. And the rule is that the giver (Allah) sometimes gives without exchange and without compensation, unlike the causal 'ba', in which case righteous deeds would be the cause of entering Paradise, and a result cannot exist without a cause. So the conclusion is that in the verse the 'ba' is compensatory, and in the hadith it is stated that the cause of entering Paradise is Allah's grace and favor. Hence there is no contradiction between the verse and hadith.
Answer (2): The 'ba' in the verse is causal, but it is carried upon the apparent situation. The detail is that the apparent cause of entering Paradise is righteous deeds, while the real cause is the grace of the Almighty. So the verse is carried upon the apparent cause, and the hadith upon grace and favor.
Answer (3): Entering Paradise is dependent on Allah's grace and favor, but attaining degrees in Paradise is dependent on righteous deeds, as Allah said: 'For all are degrees according to what they did' (Quran 46:19). In this case, the verse would be of the type of ellipsis of the annexed noun: 'Enter Paradise (i.e., degrees of it) because of what you used to do.' So the conclusion is that the verse mentions attaining degrees, and the hadith is carried upon entering Paradise, that entering Paradise is dependent on grace.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential contradiction between the Quranic verse 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do' (appearing to make deeds the cause) and the hadith that no one enters Paradise by deeds alone but only by Allah's mercy. The commentator provides three Hanafi reconciliations. First, the 'ba' in the verse is compensatory (bā' al-'iwad), not causal, meaning deeds are the reward-exchange for Paradise, not the cause. Second, the 'ba' is causal but only apparent; the real cause is Allah's grace. Third, entering Paradise (basic entry) is by grace, but higher degrees are by deeds. The Hanafi school typically prefers the third view: deeds are for degrees, grace for entry. This avoids any contradiction and upholds both texts.

Key Terms
باء عوضية (bā' al-‘iwad): The preposition 'ba' indicating exchange or compensation.
دخول الجنة (dukhūl al-janna): Entering Paradise, distinguished from attaining degrees.
باء سببيه (bā' al-sababiyya): The preposition 'ba' indicating causation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi answer, what does the verse 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do' refer to?
A) The cause of entering Paradise
B) The compensation for deeds
C) Attaining degrees in Paradise
D) The apparent cause only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, apparent contradictions between Quran and Sunnah are resolved through linguistic analysis and contextual interpretation, affirming that true entry to Paradise is by divine mercy alone.

Ranking of Islamic Sciences: Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh
Commentary on matn's opening, ranking of three sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for the ranking of Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh, and distinguish between instrumental and non-instrumental dependence.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is superior to Fiqh because fiqh depends on it; Kalam is superior to usul for the same reason.

This lesson explores the hierarchical relationship between three fundamental Islamic sciences: Kalam (theology), Usul al-Fiqh (jurisprudential methodology), and Fiqh (positive law). The commentator argues that their rank is determined by the nature of their dependence on each other, distinguishing between a foundation-branch relationship and a tool-user relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy being argued
The commentator states that Kalam is the highest, then Usul al-Fiqh, then Fiqh. Look for the explicit ranking in the text.
The ranking is based on the concept of mawquf and mawquf 'alayh.
2
Understand the argument from dependence
The argument is that a science that depends on another (mawquf) is inferior to the one it depends on (mawquf 'alayh). Trace the chain: Fiqh depends on Usul al-Fiqh; Usul al-Fiqh depends on Kalam.
This is the core of the talil argument.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection presents a counterexample: Tafsir depends on grammar (sarf/nahw) but grammar is not superior. How does the commentator respond?
The response distinguishes instrumental dependence from genuine foundation-branch dependence.
4
Distinguish the two types of tawaqquf
Instrumental dependence (e.g., carpenter on tools) does not imply superiority, whereas foundational dependence (e.g., branch on root) does. The dependence of fiqh on usul and usul on kalam is of the second type.
This is a crucial nuance in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the principle
Confirm that the hierarchy holds given the distinction. Then consider if other sciences can be ranked similarly.
This step solidifies understanding of the rule.

التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويُحِ
المعاد: خود سے اسم ظرف ہے۔ لوٹنے کی جگہ (قیامت) کیونکہ سب کو وہیں لوٹ کر جاتا ہے۔
حمد کی نعمت علم کے ساتھ تعلیق کی وجہ
قولہ علی ان جعل : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال :۔ یہاں ماتن نے حمد کو بعض نعمتوں کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا یعنی صرف علم والی نعمت کو محمود علیہ بنایا حالانکہ حمد عام ہے تمام نعمتوں (کے لیے)۔
جواب: - حمد کو علم والی صفت کے ساتھ اس لیے خاص کیا تا کہ علم اصول فقہ کی عظمت معلوم ہو جائے ۔ اور علو مرتبہ ظاہر ہو جائے اور وہ اس طرح کہ محامد کو معلق کیا اصول الشرعیہ کے ساتھ اور اصول سے مراد دلائل اربعہ ہیں جو کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع ہیں یعنی ماتن نے اشارہ کیا کہ تمام نعمتوں میں سے بڑی نعمت انہی اصول کا علم ہے باقی تو کالعدم ہیں تو اس سے اصول کی شرافت معلوم ہوئی اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس سے نفس موضوع کی شرافت اور عظمت بھی معلوم ہو گئی اور موضوع کی شرافت سے علم کی شرافت معلوم ہوئی ہے تو اس طرح علم اصول فقہ کی عظمت و شرافت بھی ظاہر ہو گئی۔
قولہ الشرعیہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ متن میں واقع الفاظ کی وضاحت کرنا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ متن میں لفظ شرعیہ عام ہے۔ فقہ کو بھی اور ان امور کو بھی جو دلائل سمعیہ و نقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں۔ جیسے روئیت باری تعالٰی قیامت کا حق ہونا اجماع وقیاس کا حجت ہونا گویا کہ شرعیہ میں علم فقہ اصول فقہ اور علم کلام سب شامل ہو گئے ۔ اور اصول شرعیہ سے مراد دلائل کلیہ ہیں یعنی قرآن، حدیث، اجماع، قیاس اور مبانی سے مراد علم ذات وصفات ہے جس پر اصول فقہ بنی ہے۔ تمہید سے مرادان اصول کی اصلاح کرنا ہے تا کہ وہ حق و ثواب کے طریق کے موافق ہوں ۔ فروع شرعیہ سے مراد ا حکام تفصیلہ ہیں جن کو فقہ میں بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ معانی سے مراد علل جزئیہ ہیں جو ہر ہر مسئلہ کی تفصیل میں واقع ہوتے ہیں۔ اور معانی کے دقیق ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ علتیں اتنی باریک ہوں کہ وہاں تک ہر آدمی آسانی سے نہ پہنچ سکے۔
قولہ و جمیع ڈلک:۔ یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ ان چیزوں کے ساتھ حمد کو معلق کیوں کیا ؟ جواب:۔ یہ سب چیزیں اللہ کی نعمتیں ہیں۔ اور یہ نعمت حمد کو واجب کرتی ہے۔ اس لیے ان اشیاء کے ساتھ حد کو معلق کیا ہے۔
قولہ اذ بالشرعیہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں ان اشیاء کے نعمت ہونے پر دلیل بیان کی ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شرعیہ جو کہ عام ہے۔ فقہ، اصول فقہ، علم کلام ، دلائل کلیہ، دلائل تفصیلہ اس سے دینا کا کام چلتا ہے ۔ اور آخرت میں ثواب ملتا ہے۔ اور فقہ کے دقیق ہونے سے علماء کے درجات بلند ہوں گے اور قیامت کے دن اس کو بہت بڑا اجر ملے گا۔ تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بہت بڑی نعمتیں ہیں۔
بیان درجات علوم ثلاثہ یعنی علم کلام واصول فقہ وفقه
قوله وفى هذ الكلام : ۔ یہ عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ اس میں شارخ متن کی خوبی بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ متن کے اندر اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اصول فقہ کا مرتبہ فقہ سے بلند ہے۔ علم کلام سے کم ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ سب سے اونچا مرتبہ علم کلام کا ہے۔ اس سے نچلا درجہ اصول فقہ کا ہے اور اس سے کم درجہ علم فقہ کا ہے۔
دلیل: یہ ہے کہ علم اصول فقہ میں بحث ہوتی ہے۔ ادلتہ کلیہ سے۔ اور فقہ میں بحث ہوتی ہے احکام جزئیہ سے ۔ اور احکام جزئیہ کی معرفت موقوف ہے اولہ کلیہ کی معرفت پر پس علم فقہ یہ موقوف ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر ۔ لہذا علم اصول فقہ کا مرتبہ زائد ہوا علم فقہ پر موقوف علیہ ہونے کی وجہ ہے۔ اور ادلہ کلیہ کی معرفت موقوف ہے۔ اللہ کی ذات وصفات و نبوت و رسالت کی معرفت پر پس علم اصول فقہ موقوف ہوا علم کلام پر اور موقوف علیہ عظیم الشان ہوتا ہے۔ موقوف سے الہذا علم کلام کا مرتبہ زائد ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر ۔
باقی رہا یہ کہ متن میں علوم ثلثہ کے مراتب کی طرف اشارہ کیسے ہوا۔ وہ اس طرح کہ ماتن نے کہا اصول الشرعیہ الخ کہ اصول فقہ کوفقہ کے لیے اصل قرار دیا۔ اور مٹی کا اصل بھی سے فائق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا علم اصول فقہ یہ فائق ہو اعلم فقہ سے پھر علم کلام کو مبانی قرار دیا ہے علم اصول فقہ کا۔ لہذا علم کلام مبنی علیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اعلیٰ مرتبہ پر ہوا اور اس طرح علم کلام فائق ہوا علم اصول فقہ پر۔
سوال :۔ اس بات کو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ موقوف علیہ موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے کہ علم تفسیر کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے۔ علم صرف و نحو پر حالانکہ علم صرف ونحو کا مرتبہ علم تفسیر سے کم ہے۔
جواب (۱): توقف کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ نمبر ا ۔ ذی آلتہ کا موقوف ہونا آلہ پر جیسے تو قف نجار اس کے آلات پر اور مشروط کا موقوف ہونا شرط پر جیسے صلوۃ کا تو قف وضو پر تو اس صورت میں موقوف علیہ کا موقوف پر مرتبہ مقدم ہونا درست نہیں ہے۔
At-Tarwih li-Hall at-Tawdih wa at-Talwih. The return: it is a noun of place by itself. The place of return (resurrection) because everyone returns there. The reason for attaching praise to the blessing of knowledge. His statement: 'ala ann ja'al: this is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The purpose of the commentator is to answer an implied question. Question: Here the author (matn) specified praise with some blessings, i.e., he made only the blessing of knowledge the object of praise, whereas praise is general for all blessings. Answer: He specified praise with the attribute of knowledge so that the greatness of the science of usul al-fiqh becomes known, and its high rank becomes apparent, and that is by attaching praiseworthy things to al-usul ash-shar'iyya, and by usul he means the four evidences which are the subject of usul al-fiqh. That is, the author indicated that among all blessings, the greatest blessing is knowledge of these usul; the rest are as if non-existent. Thus the nobility of usul becomes known, and it is clear that from this the nobility and greatness of the subject itself becomes known, and from the nobility of the subject the nobility of the science becomes known. So in this way the greatness and nobility of the science of usul al-fiqh is manifested. His statement: ash-shar'iyya: this is the second part of the commentary's phrase. The purpose of the commentator is to clarify the words occurring in the text. The conclusion is that the word 'shar'iyya' in the text is general: it includes fiqh and also those matters that are established by auditory and transmitted evidences, such as the vision of Allah on the Day of Judgment being true, and consensus and analogy being proof. So it is as if 'shar'iyya' includes the sciences of fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and kalam. And by 'usul shar'iyya' he means the universal evidences: Quran, Sunnah, consensus, analogy. And by 'mabani' he means the science of the essence and attributes (of Allah) upon which usul al-fiqh is based. By 'tamhid' he means correcting these usul so that they conform to the path of truth and reward. By 'furu' shar'iyya' he means the detailed rulings that are explained in fiqh. By 'ma'ani' he means the particular causes (illa) that occur in the details of each case. And the subtlety of the ma'ani means that those causes are so fine that not every person can easily reach them. His statement: wa jami'u dhalik: this is the third part of the phrase. The purpose is to answer an implied question. The question is: why was praise attached to these things? Answer: All these things are blessings of Allah, and blessing necessitates praise. Therefore, praise was attached to these things. His statement: idh bi-shar'iyya: this is the fourth part of the phrase. In it, he provides proof that these things are blessings. The conclusion is that 'shar'iyya', which is general — fiqh, usul al-fiqh, kalam, universal evidences, detailed evidences — through it the work of this world is carried out and reward is obtained in the Hereafter. And due to the subtlety of fiqh, the ranks of scholars will be elevated, and on the Day of Resurrection they will receive great reward. So it becomes known that these are great blessings. Statement of the ranks of the three sciences: kalam, usul al-fiqh, and fiqh. His statement: wa fi hadha al-kalam: this is the fifth part of the phrase. In it, the commentator is praising the excellence of the text, that in the text there is an indication that the rank of usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh and lower than kalam. The summary is that the highest rank belongs to kalam, then below it is usul al-fiqh, and below that is fiqh. Proof: The science of usul al-fiqh discusses universal evidences, while fiqh discusses particular rulings. Knowledge of particular rulings depends on knowledge of universal evidences. So fiqh depends on usul al-fiqh. Therefore, the rank of usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh because it is the thing on which fiqh depends (mawquf 'alayh). And knowledge of universal evidences depends on knowledge of Allah's essence and attributes, prophethood, and messengership. So usul al-fiqh depends on kalam. And the thing on which something depends (mawquf 'alayh) is greater than the thing that depends. Hence, the rank of kalam is higher than usul al-fiqh. As for how the text indicated the ranks of the three sciences, it is that the author said 'usul ash-shar'iyya' etc., making usul al-fiqh the foundation (asl) for fiqh, and the foundation is superior to the branch. So usul al-fiqh is superior to fiqh. Then he made kalam the foundation (mabani) of usul al-fiqh, so kalam, being that on which it is built (mabni 'alayh), occupies the highest rank. Thus kalam is superior to usul al-fiqh. Objection: We do not accept that the thing on which something depends (mawquf 'alayh) is necessarily superior in rank to the thing that depends (mawquf), because understanding tafsir depends on grammar and syntax (sarf and nahw), yet the rank of grammar is lower than tafsir. Answer (1): Dependence (tawaqquf) has two types. First: the dependence of the possessor of a tool on the tool, like the carpenter's dependence on his tools. Second: the dependence of a conditioned thing on the condition, like prayer's dependence on ablution. In this case, it is not correct that the thing on which dependence occurs (mawquf 'alayh) is superior in rank to the dependent thing.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a usul al-fiqh text (likely al-Tawdih). The commentator explains why the author specifically praised Allah for the blessing of knowledge of usul al-fiqh, even though all blessings deserve praise. The reason is to highlight the greatness of this science. He then clarifies the scope of the term 'shar'iyya' (relating to Islamic law) as including fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and kalam (theology). The commentator argues that usul al-fiqh is superior to fiqh because fiqh depends on it (fiqh deals with particular rulings, which are derived from universal evidences studied in usul). Similarly, kalam is superior to usul al-fiqh because usul al-fiqh depends on knowledge of Allah and prophethood, which is the subject of kalam. The passage then anticipates an objection: dependence does not always imply superiority, as tafsir depends on grammar but grammar is lower. The answer distinguishes two types of dependence: instrumental (like a carpenter on tools) and conditional (like prayer on ablution). The dependence of fiqh on usul and usul on kalam is not merely instrumental but a dependence of a branch on its foundation, which does entail superiority. This is a key usul principle about the ranking of Islamic sciences.

Key Terms
الشرعیہ (ash-shar'iyya): That which is related to Islamic law; includes fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and kalam.
مبانى (mabani): Foundations; here it refers to the science of kalam as the foundation of usul al-fiqh.
موقوف (mawquf): That which depends on something else; the dependent thing.
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayh): The thing upon which something depends; the foundation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the science of usul al-fiqh superior to the science of fiqh?
A) Because usul al-fiqh is more detailed than fiqh.
B) Because fiqh depends on usul al-fiqh for its rulings, making usul the foundation.
C) Because usul al-fiqh was revealed before fiqh.
D) Because usul al-fiqh has more proofs.

Key Takeaway
The ranking of Islamic sciences is determined by the nature of their dependence: foundational sciences (Kalam, then Usul) are superior to dependent sciences (Fiqh) when the dependence is non-instrumental.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Four Pillars of Islamic Law: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas
Explanation of the four main sources as pillars of shari'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four primary sources (arkan) of Islamic law in Hanafi usul, explain the metaphorical palace analogy, and cite the Quranic evidence for qiyas.

Core Idea
Islamic rulings rest on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, in that order.

This passage from a classical commentary likens the shari'ah rulings to a fortified palace. Just as a palace relies on strong pillars, Islamic law is founded on four core sources. The commentator explains these sources and their hierarchy, and clarifies that the fourth—qiyas (analogical reasoning)—is rooted in a Quranic command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
Locate the four sources explicitly or implicitly mentioned: the Book (Quran), Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas (alluded to as 'the paths of those who consider').
The first three are explicit; the fourth is implied through a phrase.
2
Understand the palace metaphor
Explain why rulings are compared to a palace: whoever takes refuge in them is safe from spiritual enemies and hellfire.
The metaphor emphasizes the protective and foundational role of the sources.
3
Note the order of sources
Observe the fixed sequence: Quran, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. This is the order in which the Lawgiver built rulings.
The order reflects a hierarchy of authority.
4
Recognize the evidence for qiyas
The commentator cites the Quranic verse 'Fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (59:2) as the basis for qiyas. The word 'i'tibara' linguistically implies reflection and analogy.
This shows that qiyas is derived from a direct textual command.
5
Acknowledge a nuance: the position of Sunnah
An objection is raised: the Sunnah does not always precede Ijma; it only does so when the Sunnah is definitive (qat'i). This suggests that when the Sunnah is speculative (zanni), Ijma may take precedence.
This is an advanced point; the full discussion is not provided here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ بَنِى عَلَى أَربَعَةِ أَرْكَانٍ بِمَنزِلَةِ البَدَلِ مِن الجُمَلَةِ السَّابِقَةِ شَبَّهَ الْأَحِكَامَ الشَّرعِيَّةَ بِقَصرِ مِن جِهَةِ أَنَّ المُلتَجِى إِلَيْهَا يَأْمَنُ مِن غَوَايْلِ عَدُوٍّ الدِّينِ وَعَذَابِ النَّارِ فَأَضَافَ المُشَبَّهَ بِهِ إِلَى المُشَبَّهِ كَمَا فِي لُجَينِ المَاءِ وَالأحكامُ تَستَنِدُ إِلَى أَدِلَّةٍ جُزيَّةٍ تَرجِعُ مَعَ كَثرَتِهَا إِلَى أَربَعَةِ دَلَائِلَ هِيَ أَرْكَانُ قَصِرِ الْأَحِكَامِ فَذَكَرَهَا فِي أَثْنَاءِ الكَلَامِ عَلَى التَّرْتِيبِ الَّذِي بَنَى الشَّارِعُ الأحكامَ عَلَيْهَا مِن تَقدِيمِ الكِتَابِ ثُمَّ السُّنَّةِ ثُمَّ الإِجْمَاعِ ثُمَّ العَمَلِ بِالقِيَاسِ ذَكَرَ الثَّلَاثَةَ الْاوَلَ صَرِيحًا وَالْقِيَاسَ بِقَولِهِ وَوَضَعَ مَعَالِمَ العِلمِ عَلَى مَسَالِكِ المُعْتَبِرِينَ أَى القَائِسِينَ المُتَأَمِّلِينَ فِي النُّصُوص وَعِلَلِ الاحكامِ مِن قَوله تَعَالَى فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ تَقُولُ اعْتَبَرَتِ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا نَظَرت إِلَيْهِ وَرَاعَيتَ حَالَهُ وَالمِعْلَمُ الأَثَرُ الَّذِى يُستَدَلُّ بِهِ عَلَى الطَّرِيقِ عَيْرَ بِهِ عَن عِلَّةِ الحُكمِ الَّتِي بِهَا يُستَدَلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ الحُكمِ فِي الْمَقِيسِ فَإِن قُلتَ : لَيْسَ ترتيب الشَّارِعِ تَقدِيمَ السُّنَّةِ عَلَى الإِجماع مُطَلَقًا بَل إِذَا كَانَتَ قَطَعِيَّةُ قُلتُ
His statement: 'built upon four pillars' is in the position of a substitute for the previous sentence. He likened the shari' rulings to a palace, from the perspective that whoever takes refuge in them is secure from the evils of the enemy of religion and the punishment of hellfire. So he added the simile to the compared object, as in 'the silver of water'. And the rulings rely on particular proofs, which despite their multiplicity reduce to four proofs, which are the pillars of the palace of rulings. So he mentioned them in the course of speech according to the order upon which the Lawgiver built the rulings: giving precedence to the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting by Qiyas. He mentioned the first three explicitly, and Qiyas by his saying: 'and he placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who consider' i.e. the measurers who reflect on the texts and the causes of rulings, from His statement Exalted: 'So take warning, O people of insight.' You say: 'i'tabartu al-shay'' when you look at it and observe its condition. And 'al-mi'lam' is the sign by which the road is known; by it is meant the cause of the ruling by which the establishment of the ruling in the analogized case is deduced. If you say: The Lawgiver's order does not always place Sunnah before Ijma; rather only when the Sunnah is definitive... I say:
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn, which described Islamic rulings as built upon four 'pillars' (arkan). The commentator explains the metaphor: rulings are like a palace to which one flees for safety. The palace is supported by four columns, which are the four main evidences: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. The text mentions Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma explicitly, and alludes to Qiyas through the phrase 'placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who consider' (al-mu'tabirin). This phrase refers to practitioners of qiyas, who derive rulings by analogy. The commentator clarifies that 'mi'lam' (landmark) here means the 'illah (legal cause) by which analogy is made. He cites the Quranic verse 'fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (59:2) as evidence for qiyas. Then an objection is raised: the Lawgiver's order of sources does not always place Sunnah before Ijma, but only when the Sunnah is definitive (qat'i). The passage ends abruptly, but the discussion likely continues. This is a standard Hanafi usul presentation of the four sources, emphasizing their hierarchical order: Quran > Sunnah > Ijma > Qiyas.

Key Terms
أَرْكَان (arkan): Pillars or foundational elements upon which something is built; here the four main sources of Islamic law.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illah).
المعالم (al-ma'alim): Landmarks or signs; here used metaphorically for the 'illah (cause) that guides to the ruling in qiyas.
مسالك المعتبرين (masalik al-mu'tabirin): Paths of those who consider/reflect; i.e., the methods of jurists who perform qiyas by studying texts and causes.
قطعية (qat'iyyah): Definitive, certain; used here to describe a Sunnah that is mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and thus yields certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse is cited in this passage as the basis for qiyas?
A) فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ
B) وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ
C) إِنَّا أَنْزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ بِالْحَقِّ
D) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَطِيعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا الرَّسُولَ

Key Takeaway
Islamic rulings rest on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, with the first three explicit and qiyas rooted in the Quranic command to reflect and analogize.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Four Pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas
Explanation of the four sources and their hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources of Islamic rulings, explain their hierarchical order, and defend the Hanafi position on the precedence of the Sunnah over Ijma.

Core Idea
Islamic rulings rest on four proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas — each with its own authority and priority.

This passage introduces the foundational structure of Hanafi legal theory. Rulings are likened to a fortress, and the proofs are its pillars. Understanding the hierarchy of these sources is essential for deriving rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four proofs
Locate the four proofs mentioned: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas. Note that they are called 'arkan' (pillars) of the fortress of rulings.
The fortress analogy emphasizes protection from spiritual harm.
2
Understand the fortress analogy
The author compares rulings to a fortress; the four proofs are its pillars. This highlights their foundational role.
3
Analyze the order of priority
The Lawgiver's order is Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. Recognize that this order is based on the strength and precedence of each source.
The text mentions that the first three are explicit; Qiyas is derived from the Quranic verse 'So take heed'.
4
Evaluate the objection about Sunnah vs Ijma
Consider the objection: is Sunnah always prior to Ijma? The author responds that the text (matn) of Sunnah is inherently prior; delay only occurs due to uncertainty in transmission (zann).
This is a key Hanafi position.
5
Recognize the evidence for Qiyas
The Quranic verse (59:2) 'So take heed, O people of insight' is used as the basis for qiyas. The word 'i'tibar' is the root for analogical reasoning.
