ترجمہ: بنی علی اربعہ ارکان یہ بمنزلہ بدل کے ہے جملہ سابقہ سے تشبیہ دی ہے احکام شرعیہ کو کل کے ساتھ اس جہت سے کہ بے شک پناہ لینے والا ان احکام شرعیہ کی طرف محفوظ ہو جاتا ہے دین کے دشمنوں کے دھوکوں سے اور آگ کے عذاب سے۔ پس اضافت کی ہے مشبہ بہ کی مشبہ کی طرف جیسا کہ جنین الماء میں۔ اور وہ احکام جو منسوب ہوتے ہیں ادلتہ جزئیہ کی طرف وہ لوٹتے ہیں اپنی کثرت کے باوجود چار کی طرف وہ چار جو کہ احکام کے محل کے ارکان ہیں۔ پس ذکر کیا ان کو کلام کے درمیان میں اس ترتیب پر جس پر شارع نے احکام کی بنیا درکھی ہے۔ کتاب کو مقدم کرنے سے پھر سنت پھر اجماع پھر عمل بالقیاس کو ذکر کیا۔ پہلے تین کو صراحتا اور قیاس کو اپنے قول وضع معالم العلم علی مسالک المعتمرین کے ساتھ یعنی وہ قیاس کرنے والے جو غور و فکر کرنے والے ہیں نصوص میں اور احکام کی علتوں میں جو ماخوذ ہیں اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول فاعتبر وا یا اولی الابصار سے۔ تو کہتا ہے اعتبرت الشئی جب تو دیکھے اس کی طرف اور تو رعایت کرے اس کے حال کی ۔ اور معلم وہ اثر کہ استدلال کیا جائے اس کے ساتھ طریق پر اس حال میں کہ اعتبار کیا جائے اس معلم کا اس حکم کی علت کے ساتھ کہ جس سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے حکم کے ثابت ہونے پر منفیس میں۔ پھر اگر تو کہے کہ نہیں ہے شارع کی ترتیب سنت کو اجماع پر مقدم کرنا مطلقاً بلکہ جب ہو وہ سنت قطعی ۔ میں کہوں گا کہ کلام متن سنت میں ہے۔ اور نہیں ہے کوئی خفاء اس متن سنت کے اجماع پر مقدم کرنے میں اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ موخر کیا جاتا ہے جہاں موخر کیا جاتا ہے مگر فن کے عارض کے ساتھ اس سنت کے ثابت ہونے میں پھر کتاب کی بعض اقسام کو ذکر کیا اشارہ کرتے ہوئے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک وہ جیسے مشتمل ہوتا ہے محل او پر اس کے کہ وہ انتہائی ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس چیز پر کہ وہ اس سے کم ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس چیز پر جو انتہائی پوشیدگی اور خفاء میں ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں پہنچ سکتا اس کی طرف محل کے مالک کے علاوہ کوئی ایک اور اس پر کہ وہ اس سے کم مخفی ہے اسی طرح احکام کا محل مشتمل ہوتا ہے محکم پر وہ انتہائی ظہور میں ہے اور نص پر وہ اس سے کم ظاہر ہے اور متشابہ پروہ انتہائی خفاء میں ہے اور جمل پردہ اس سے کم
His statement: 'Built upon four pillars' is in the position of a substitute for the previous sentence. He likened the legal rulings to a fortress because the one who seeks refuge in them is safe from the evil plots of the enemy of the religion and the punishment of fire. So he added the thing compared to the thing compared to, as in 'lujayn al-ma' (silver of water). And the rulings are based on particular evidences which, despite their abundance, go back to four proofs, which are the pillars of the fortress of rulings. So he mentioned them in the course of speech according to the order upon which the Lawgiver built the rulings: giving precedence to the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting by Qiyas. He mentioned the first three explicitly, and Qiyas by his statement: 'And he placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who take heed' i.e., the measurers who reflect on the texts and the causes of rulings, from His statement (Exalted) 'So take heed, O people of insight.' You say: 'I took heed of the thing' when you look at it and consider its state. And 'al-mi'lam' is the trace by which the path is recognized; it is used metaphorically for the cause of the ruling by which the establishment of the ruling in the analogized case is deduced. Then if you say: 'The Lawgiver's order of giving precedence to the Sunnah over Ijma is not absolute; rather, when the Sunnah is definitive.' I say: The discussion is about the text of the Sunnah, and there is no obscurity in its precedence over Ijma. It is only delayed when it is delayed due to the incidental uncertainty in its proof. Then he mentioned some categories of the Book, indicating that just as the fortress includes that which is extreme in clarity and that which is less, and that which is extreme in concealment and secrecy to the extent that no one other than the owner of the fortress can reach it, and that which is less, similarly the fortress of rulings includes Muhkam which is extreme in clarity, Nass which is less than it, Mutashabih which is extreme in concealment, and Mujmal which is less than it. And its explanation will come. Translation: 'Built upon four pillars' is in the position of a substitute for the previous sentence. He likened the legal rulings to a fortress because the one who seeks refuge in them is safe from the deceit of the enemies of the religion and the punishment of fire. So he added the compared to the compared, as in 'jinin al-ma'. And the rulings that are attributed to particular evidences, despite their abundance, go back to four, which are the pillars of the rulings. So he mentioned them in the course of speech in the order upon which the Lawgiver built the rulings: giving precedence to the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting by Qiyas. He mentioned the first three explicitly, and Qiyas by his statement: 'And he placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who take heed' i.e., those who measure, who ponder in the texts and the causes of rulings, taken from Allah's statement 'So take heed, O people of insight.' So it says: 'I took heed of the thing' when you look at it and consider its state. And 'al-mi'lam' is the trace by which the path is deduced, it is used metaphorically for the cause of the ruling by which the rulings are deduced. Then if you say: 'The Lawgiver's order of giving precedence to the Sunnah over Ijma is not absolute; rather, when the Sunnah is definitive.' I say: The discussion is about the text of the Sunnah, and there is no obscurity in its precedence over Ijma. It is only delayed when it is delayed due to the incidental uncertainty in its proof. Then he mentioned some categories of the Book, indicating that just as the fortress includes that which is extreme in clarity and that which is less, and that which is extreme in concealment and secrecy to the extent that no one other than the owner of the fortress can reach it, and that which is less, similarly the fortress of rulings includes Muhkam which is extreme in clarity, and Nass which is less than it, and Mutashabih which is extreme in concealment, and Mujmal which is less than it. And its explanation will come.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage explains that Islamic rulings are built upon four fundamental proofs: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (Ijma), and analogical reasoning (Qiyas). The author uses the simile of a fortress to illustrate that these rulings protect those who adhere to them from spiritual harm. The four proofs are presented in order of priority as established by the Lawgiver: Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. The commentary then addresses a potential objection about the priority of Sunnah over Ijma: it explains that when the Sunnah is definitive (qat'i), it is clearly prior; when it appears delayed, it is due to uncertainty in its transmission (zann). Finally, the passage introduces categories of Quranic texts (Muhkam, Nass, Mutashabih, Mujmal) based on degrees of clarity, comparing them to the varying visibility of parts of a fortress.

Key Terms
أركان (arkan): Pillars or foundations; here the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) upon which rulings are built.
محكم (muhkam): Text that is extreme in clarity (غاية في الظهور); unambiguous.
نص (nass): Text that is clear but less than muhkam; its meaning is apparent but may have some nuance.
متشابه (mutashabih): Text that is extreme in concealment (غاية في الخفاء); ambiguous to all except God.
مجمل (mujmal): Text that is less concealed than mutashabih; requires explanation (bayan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Sunnah given precedence over Ijma?
A) Because the Sunnah is always definitive.
B) Because the discussion is about the text (matn) of the Sunnah, which is clear and prior; delay occurs only due to uncertainty in transmission.
C) Because Ijma is never as strong as the Sunnah.
D) Because the Sunnah comes right after the Quran in revelation.

Key Takeaway
The four proofs are ordered as Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas; the text of Sunnah is inherently prior to Ijma.

Categories of Quranic Texts: Muhkam, Nass, Mutashabih, Mujmal
Explanation of Quranic text categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Muhkam, Nass, Mutashabih, and Mujmal texts and explain their role in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Quranic texts vary in clarity: Muhkam (extremely clear), Nass (clear), Mutashabih (extremely concealed), Mujmal (less concealed) — each requires a different interpretive approach.

This passage extends the fortress analogy to the types of Quranic texts. Just as a fortress has parts that are clearly visible and parts that are hidden, the Quran contains verses of varying degrees of clarity. Understanding these categories is crucial for correct interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The author mentions Muhkam, Nass, Mutashabih, and Mujmal. Recognize that Muhkam is extreme in clarity, Nass is less, Mutashabih is extreme in concealment, Mujmal is less concealed.
This is a Hanafi classification specific to textual clarity.
2
Understand the fortress analogy
Compare the fortress: some parts are clearly visible, some less so, some hidden. Similarly, Quranic texts have a hierarchy of clarity.
3
Distinguish Muhkam from Nass
Muhkam is absolutely clear; Nass is clear but may have some nuance. Both are usable as primary evidence but with different levels of strength.
The passage says muhkam is extreme in clarity (غاية في الظهور), nass is less.
4
Distinguish Mutashabih from Mujmal
Mutashabih is totally ambiguous (only Allah knows its meaning); Mujmal requires explanation (bayan) from other sources.
Mutashabih is extreme in concealment; Mujmal is less concealed.
5
Apply to usul analysis
In deriving rulings, a Muhkam text is self-sufficient; a Mujmal text needs clarification from Sunnah or other sources.

ترجمہ: بنی علی اربعہ ارکان یہ بمنزلہ بدل کے ہے جملہ سابقہ سے تشبیہ دی ہے احکام شرعیہ کو کل کے ساتھ اس جہت سے کہ بے شک پناہ لینے والا ان احکام شرعیہ کی طرف محفوظ ہو جاتا ہے دین کے دشمنوں کے دھوکوں سے اور آگ کے عذاب سے۔ پس اضافت کی ہے مشبہ بہ کی مشبہ کی طرف جیسا کہ جنین الماء میں۔ اور وہ احکام جو منسوب ہوتے ہیں ادلتہ جزئیہ کی طرف وہ لوٹتے ہیں اپنی کثرت کے باوجود چار کی طرف وہ چار جو کہ احکام کے محل کے ارکان ہیں۔ پس ذکر کیا ان کو کلام کے درمیان میں اس ترتیب پر جس پر شارع نے احکام کی بنیا درکھی ہے۔ کتاب کو مقدم کرنے سے پھر سنت پھر اجماع پھر عمل بالقیاس کو ذکر کیا۔ پہلے تین کو صراحتا اور قیاس کو اپنے قول وضع معالم العلم علی مسالک المعتمرین کے ساتھ یعنی وہ قیاس کرنے والے جو غور و فکر کرنے والے ہیں نصوص میں اور احکام کی علتوں میں جو ماخوذ ہیں اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول فاعتبر وا یا اولی الابصار سے۔ تو کہتا ہے اعتبرت الشئی جب تو دیکھے اس کی طرف اور تو رعایت کرے اس کے حال کی ۔ اور معلم وہ اثر کہ استدلال کیا جائے اس کے ساتھ طریق پر اس حال میں کہ اعتبار کیا جائے اس معلم کا اس حکم کی علت کے ساتھ کہ جس سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے حکم کے ثابت ہونے پر منفیس میں۔ پھر اگر تو کہے کہ نہیں ہے شارع کی ترتیب سنت کو اجماع پر مقدم کرنا مطلقاً بلکہ جب ہو وہ سنت قطعی ۔ میں کہوں گا کہ کلام متن سنت میں ہے۔ اور نہیں ہے کوئی خفاء اس متن سنت کے اجماع پر مقدم کرنے میں اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ موخر کیا جاتا ہے جہاں موخر کیا جاتا ہے مگر فن کے عارض کے ساتھ اس سنت کے ثابت ہونے میں پھر کتاب کی بعض اقسام کو ذکر کیا اشارہ کرتے ہوئے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک وہ جیسے مشتمل ہوتا ہے محل او پر اس کے کہ وہ انتہائی ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس چیز پر کہ وہ اس سے کم ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس چیز پر جو انتہائی پوشیدگی اور خفاء میں ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں پہنچ سکتا اس کی طرف محل کے مالک کے علاوہ کوئی ایک اور اس پر کہ وہ اس سے کم مخفی ہے اسی طرح احکام کا محل مشتمل ہوتا ہے محکم پر وہ انتہائی ظہور میں ہے اور نص پر وہ اس سے کم ظاہر ہے اور متشابہ پروہ انتہائی خفاء میں ہے اور جمل پردہ اس سے کم
His statement: 'Built upon four pillars' is in the position of a substitute for the previous sentence. He likened the legal rulings to a fortress because the one who seeks refuge in them is safe from the evil plots of the enemy of the religion and the punishment of fire. So he added the thing compared to the thing compared to, as in 'lujayn al-ma' (silver of water). And the rulings are based on particular evidences which, despite their abundance, go back to four proofs, which are the pillars of the fortress of rulings. So he mentioned them in the course of speech according to the order upon which the Lawgiver built the rulings: giving precedence to the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting by Qiyas. He mentioned the first three explicitly, and Qiyas by his statement: 'And he placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who take heed' i.e., the measurers who reflect on the texts and the causes of rulings, from His statement (Exalted) 'So take heed, O people of insight.' You say: 'I took heed of the thing' when you look at it and consider its state. And 'al-mi'lam' is the trace by which the path is recognized; it is used metaphorically for the cause of the ruling by which the establishment of the ruling in the analogized case is deduced. Then if you say: 'The Lawgiver's order of giving precedence to the Sunnah over Ijma is not absolute; rather, when the Sunnah is definitive.' I say: The discussion is about the text of the Sunnah, and there is no obscurity in its precedence over Ijma. It is only delayed when it is delayed due to the incidental uncertainty in its proof. Then he mentioned some categories of the Book, indicating that just as the fortress includes that which is extreme in clarity and that which is less, and that which is extreme in concealment and secrecy to the extent that no one other than the owner of the fortress can reach it, and that which is less, similarly the fortress of rulings includes Muhkam which is extreme in clarity, Nass which is less than it, Mutashabih which is extreme in concealment, and Mujmal which is less than it. And its explanation will come. Translation: 'Built upon four pillars' is in the position of a substitute for the previous sentence. He likened the legal rulings to a fortress because the one who seeks refuge in them is safe from the deceit of the enemies of the religion and the punishment of fire. So he added the compared to the compared, as in 'jinin al-ma'. And the rulings that are attributed to particular evidences, despite their abundance, go back to four, which are the pillars of the rulings. So he mentioned them in the course of speech in the order upon which the Lawgiver built the rulings: giving precedence to the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting by Qiyas. He mentioned the first three explicitly, and Qiyas by his statement: 'And he placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who take heed' i.e., those who measure, who ponder in the texts and the causes of rulings, taken from Allah's statement 'So take heed, O people of insight.' So it says: 'I took heed of the thing' when you look at it and consider its state. And 'al-mi'lam' is the trace by which the path is deduced, it is used metaphorically for the cause of the ruling by which the rulings are deduced. Then if you say: 'The Lawgiver's order of giving precedence to the Sunnah over Ijma is not absolute; rather, when the Sunnah is definitive.' I say: The discussion is about the text of the Sunnah, and there is no obscurity in its precedence over Ijma. It is only delayed when it is delayed due to the incidental uncertainty in its proof. Then he mentioned some categories of the Book, indicating that just as the fortress includes that which is extreme in clarity and that which is less, and that which is extreme in concealment and secrecy to the extent that no one other than the owner of the fortress can reach it, and that which is less, similarly the fortress of rulings includes Muhkam which is extreme in clarity, and Nass which is less than it, and Mutashabih which is extreme in concealment, and Mujmal which is less than it. And its explanation will come.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage explains that Islamic rulings are built upon four fundamental proofs: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (Ijma), and analogical reasoning (Qiyas). The author uses the simile of a fortress to illustrate that these rulings protect those who adhere to them from spiritual harm. The four proofs are presented in order of priority as established by the Lawgiver: Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. The commentary then addresses a potential objection about the priority of Sunnah over Ijma: it explains that when the Sunnah is definitive (qat'i), it is clearly prior; when it appears delayed, it is due to uncertainty in its transmission (zann). Finally, the passage introduces categories of Quranic texts (Muhkam, Nass, Mutashabih, Mujmal) based on degrees of clarity, comparing them to the varying visibility of parts of a fortress.

Key Terms
أركان (arkan): Pillars or foundations; here the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) upon which rulings are built.
محكم (muhkam): Text that is extreme in clarity (غاية في الظهور); unambiguous.
نص (nass): Text that is clear but less than muhkam; its meaning is apparent but may have some nuance.
متشابه (mutashabih): Text that is extreme in concealment (غاية في الخفاء); ambiguous to all except God.
مجمل (mujmal): Text that is less concealed than mutashabih; requires explanation (bayan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of Quranic text is described as 'extreme in concealment' (غاية في الخفاء)?
A) Muhkam
B) Nass
C) Mutashabih
D) Mujmal

Key Takeaway
Quranic texts are classified by clarity: Muhkam (clear), Nass (less clear), Mujmal (ambiguous), Mutashabih (totally hidden).

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Four Pillars of Legal Rulings: General Proofs and Their Order
Commentary expanding the matn's statement on the four proofs as pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the four general proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are considered the pillars of legal rulings in Hanafi usul, and defend the order and inclusion of Qiyas.

Core Idea
The four proofs are the pillars because every particular ruling derives from them, directly or indirectly.

This lesson unpacks a commentary on Al-Tawdih that clarifies a foundational concept in Hanafi usul: the four general proofs (adillah kulliyyah) are the pillars on which all Shari'ah rulings rest. The commentator addresses common objections about why these sources are called 'pillars' when they seem external to individual rulings, how particular proofs relate to them, the correct order of proofs, and the implicit inclusion of Qiyas. Understanding this structure is essential for grasping how rulings are derived and prioritized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's claim
State the author's assertion: the rulings of Shari'ah are built on four pillars (arkān). Recognize that these pillars are the general proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
The term 'arkan' here is metaphorical.
2
Analyze the objection: pillars are internal parts
Understand the objection: if pillars are integral parts of a thing, how can the general proofs, which are external to rulings, be considered pillars? The commentator provides two answers.
First answer: 'rukn' can refer to external supports (Quran 11:80). Second: by 'pillars' the author means the general-summary proofs, and by 'rulings' the particular-detailed proofs that derive from them.
3
Trace the relationship between general and particular proofs
Examine the objection that rulings are based on particular proofs (e.g., 'Aqimu al-salah') not general ones. The response: particular proofs are subsumed under the general proofs, e.g., all such verses are part of 'Kitab Allah'.
This reinforces the role of general proofs as the ultimate foundation.
4
Understand the order and inclusion of Qiyas
Note the prescribed order: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas. Then see how the author implicitly includes Qiyas in the phrase 'masalik al-mu'tabarin', which derives from 'i'tibar' meaning Qiyas.
This shows the author's method of alluding to Qiyas without explicit mention.
5
Resolve the dispute on hadith precedence over Ijma
Address the objection that only qat'i (definitively transmitted) hadith should precede Ijma, while the author said generally. The commentator distinguishes matn (text) from thubut (transmission): the matn of a hadith is always clear, so it takes precedence over Ijma in Hanafi usul even if ahad, as long as it is not contradicted by a stronger source.
This is a key difference from other schools; for Hanafis, a hadith's matn can outweigh Ijma under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبہ الاحكام ۔ يہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی خوبی بیان کی ہے۔ جس کا حاصل يہ ہے کہ ماتن نے بنی علی اربعہ ارکان قصر الاحکام میں احکام شرعیہ کو تشبیہ دی ہے محل کے ساتھ۔
وجہ تشبیہ :۔ کہ جس طرح محل میں آدمی دشمنوں سے محفوظ ہوتا ہے۔ اور پریشانی سے محفوظ ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح شرعیت کے احکام پر عمل کرنے سے شیطان کی دشمنی و پھسلانے سے اور جہنم کے عذاب سے محفوظ ہو جاتا ہے۔۔
سوال :۔ مئی کے ارکان شئی میں داخل ہوتے ہیں۔ تو ماتن نے دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان کیسے بنا دیا۔ حالانکہ دلائل کلیہ احکام سے خارج ہیں۔
جواب (۱):۔ رکن بھی کبھی کبھی شئی کے اس خارج پر بھی بولا جاتا ہے جس سے قوت حاصل کی جائے جیسے اللہ کا ارشاد ہے فتولی بر کنہ اب يہاں رکن شئی میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ تو يہاں بھی ارکان سے مراد وہ اشیاء لیں گے جوشئی سے خارج ہوں البتہ وہ اس کے لئے مقوی ہوں۔ لہذا دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان بنا سکتے ہیں ۔
جواب (۲):۔ ارکان سے يہی مراد ہے کہ جو ٹی میں داخل ہو لیکن ارکان سے مراد دلائل کلیہ اجمالیہ ہوں گے اور احکام سے مراد دلائل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ ہوں گے جو دلائل کلیہ اجمالیہ پر متفرع ہیں۔ اور دلائل جزئیہ دلائل کلیہ کی طرف مراجع ہیں لہذا دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان بنانا درست ہے۔
قوله فاضاف المشبہ بہ : يہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں ترکیبی تحقیق کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ کہ احکام میں مشتبہ بہ کی اضافت نشتہ کی طرف ہے۔ جیسے جين الماء میں لین مشبہ بہ ہے۔ اور مآ ومشبہ ہے۔ اصل میں تھا۔ الماء لچھیں ۔ قولہ والا حکام:۔ يہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ احکام شرعیہ کی بنیا دادلہ اربعہ پر ہے
سوال: يہ ہے کہ توضیح کی عبارت سے يہ بات معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ احکام شرعیہ کے محل کی بنیا د ادلہ کلیہ پر ہے۔ اور ادلہ کلیہ چار ہیں حالانکہ احکام شرعیہ کی بناء دلائل جزئیہ پر ہے جیسے نماز کا قائم کرنا حکم شرعی ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل اقیمو الصلوٰۃ ہے اور
زکوۃ حکم شرعی ہے دلیل آتو الزکوۃ ہے اور حج کرنا حکم شرعی ہے اور اس کی دلیل اللہ علی الناس حج البیت ہے اور يہ سب دلائل جزئیہ ہیں نہ کہ دلائل کلید تو ماتن کا يہ کہنا کہ احکام شرعیہ کی بنا دلائل کلیہ پر ہے درست نہ ہوا؟
جواب:۔ بے شک احکام شرعیہ کی بناء ادلہ جزئیہ پر ہے۔ لیکن ادلہ جزئیہ باوجود اپنی کثرت کے اولہ کلیہ کے طرف لوٹ آتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ اقیمو الصلوٰۃ ، آتو الزکوۃ ان سب پر کتاب اللہ کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے۔ اور کتاب اللہ ادلہ کلیہ میں سے ایک دلیل
ہے۔
فذ کرھا: يہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی خوبی بیان کی ہے ۔ کہ جس طرح ترتیب کے ساتھ شرعیت نے ارکان اربعہ کو رکھا ہے۔ پہلے نمبر پر کتاب اللہ پھر سنت رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پھر اجماع پھر تیاس کو ، اسی طرح ماتن نے بھی ارکان اربعہ کو اسی ترتیب پر ذکر کیا ہے۔
ذکر الثلاثہ: يہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شارک نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ مائن نے دلائل ثلاثہ ( کتاب اللہ سنت رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور اجماع کو تو اپنی کتاب میں ذکر کیا لیکن قیاس کا کہیں بھی ذکر نہیں کیا۔ جواب: پہلے تین دلائل کا صراحتہ ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور قیاس کو اپنے قول وضع معالم العلم علی مسالک المعتبرین میں ضمنا ذ کر کیا۔ کیونکہ معتبرین مشتق ہے۔ فاعتبر والیا اولی الابصار سے بمعنی اے منظمند و قیاس کرو اس لیے کہ اہل عرب کہتے ہیں اعتبرت الشئی یعنی جب تو کسی شی میں غور و فکر کرے تو معتبرین سے مراد قیاس کرنے والے لوگ ہوں گے ۔ حکم اس اثر کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ذریعہ قیاس پر استدلال کیا جائے ۔ مراد اس سے حکم کی علت ہے۔
متن حدیث مطلقا اجماع پر مقدم ہوتا ہے
فان قلت : ۔ يہ عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت سے سوال اور قلت سے جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال کا حاصل يہ ہے کہ شرعیت نے مطلقا سنت کو اجماع پر مقدم نہیں کیا بلکہ اگر سنت قطعی الثبوت ہوتو وہ اجتماع پر مقدم ہوگی ۔ لیکن ماتن نے مطلقاً سنت کو اجماع پر مقدم کر دیا تو ماتن کی ترتیب شرعیت کی ترتیب کے موافق نہ ہوئی۔
جواب:۔ ایک ہے متن حدیث دوسرا ہے ثبوت حدیث ۔ متن حدیث میں کوئی خفا نہیں يہی وجہ ہے کہ صحابہ کرام کے لئے
The second part of the commentary's text: In this passage, the commentator praised the excellence of the text. The gist is that the author compared the Shari rulings to a fortress [mahall], saying 'built upon four pillars of rulings.' The basis of the comparison: just as in a fortress a person is protected from enemies and protected from distress, similarly by acting upon the Shari rulings one becomes protected from the enmity of Shaitan and his slipping, and from the punishment of Hell. Question: [If] pillars are part of a thing, then how did the author make the general proofs (dila'il kulliyyah) into pillars for the rulings, while the general proofs are external to the rulings? Answer (1): Sometimes the term 'pillar' is applied to something external from which strength is derived, as in Allah's saying 'Fatawalla biruknihi' - here 'rukn' is not part of the thing. So here too by 'pillars' are meant those things that are external to the thing but are strengthening for it. Thus the general proofs can be made pillars for the rulings. Answer (2): It could also mean that by 'pillars' is meant what enters into it [the thing], but by 'pillars' are meant the general-summary proofs and by 'rulings' are meant the particular-detailed proofs which are derived from the general-summary proofs. The particular proofs refer back to the general proofs, so making the general proofs into pillars for the rulings is correct. His statement 'fadif al-mushabbah bihi': This is the third part of the commentary. In it, it points to a compositional analysis: in rulings, the attribution of the thing compared is to the thing compared to [mushabbah ilayh]. For example, 'zeen al-ma' where 'zeen' is the thing compared and 'ma' is the thing compared to. Originally it was 'al-ma' zayyin'. His statement 'wa al-ahkam': This is the fourth part of the commentary. The intention is that the commentator answers a supposed question: the rulings of Shari are based on the four proofs. Question: From the text of Al-Tawdih it appears that the foundation of the rulings is upon the general proofs, and the general proofs are four, while the rulings are built on particular proofs, like establishing prayer is a Shari ruling and its proof is 'Aqimu al-salah', and Zakat is a Shari ruling and its proof is 'Atu al-zakah', and Hajj is a Shari ruling and its proof is 'Lillahi 'ala al-nas hijj al-bayt' - these are all particular proofs not general proofs. So the author's saying that the rulings are built on general proofs is not correct? Answer: Indeed the rulings are built on particular proofs. But the particular proofs, despite their multitude, refer back to the general proofs. Because 'Aqimu al-salah', 'Atu al-zakah' - all of them are covered by the word 'Kitab Allah', and Kitab Allah is one of the general proofs. 'Fadkuraha': This is the fifth part of the commentary. In this, the commentator mentioned the excellence of the text: just as the Sharia has placed the four pillars in order - first Kitab Allah, then Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, then Ijma, then Qiyas - similarly the author mentioned the four pillars in that order. 'Dakr al-thalathah': This is the sixth part of the commentary. In this, the commentator answers a supposed question. Question: The author mentioned the three proofs (Kitab Allah, Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, Ijma) explicitly in his book, but he did not mention Qiyas anywhere. Answer: He mentioned the first three proofs explicitly, and he included Qiyas implicitly in his statement 'wad' ma'alim al-'ilm 'ala masalik al-mu'tabarin'. Because 'mu'tabarin' is derived from 'Fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' meaning 'consider and measure' and it means do Qiyas. Because the Arabs say 'i'tabartu al-shay' meaning when you ponder over a thing. So by 'mu'tabarin' are meant people who do Qiyas. 'Hukm' is the characteristic [effect] by which Qiyas is argued; by it is meant the 'illah of the ruling. The text of hadith is absolutely given precedence over Ijma. 'Fa in qult': This is the seventh part of the commentary. The purpose of this passage is to answer a question. The gist of the question: the Sharia did not absolutely give precedence to Sunnah over Ijma; rather if the Sunnah is qat'i al-thubut (definitive in transmission), then it will be given precedence over Ijma. But the author absolutely gave precedence to Sunnah over Ijma, so the author's order does not align with the Sharia's order. Answer: There is the text of hadith (matn) and there is the thubut (transmission) of hadith. The text of hadith has no concealment; this is why it is for the noble Companions...
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Al-Tawdih, expanding the matn's statement that 'legal rulings are built on four pillars (arkan).' The commentator addresses several points:

1. **Analogy to a fortress**: The rulings are compared to a fortified place (mahall) that protects; similarly, following Shari'ah rulings protects from Shaytan and Hellfire.

2. **Why general proofs are called 'pillars'**: A common objection is that pillars are internal parts of a structure, whereas the general proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are external to the rulings. The commentator gives two responses: (a) Sometimes 'rukn' is used for external supports that strengthen, as in the Quranic verse 'Fatawalla biruknihi' (11:80) where 'rukn' means supporters. (b) Alternatively, by 'pillars' the author means the general-summary proofs, and by 'rulings' he means the particular-detailed proofs that are derived from them. Thus the general proofs are the pillars because particular proofs refer back to them.

3. **Why particular proofs (e.g., 'Aqimu al-salah') are not directly mentioned**: The objection is that rulings are based on particular proofs, not general ones. The answer: Particular proofs (like verses) are subsumed under the general proofs (like Kitab Allah). So the foundation is indeed the general proofs.

4. **Order of the proofs**: The commentator praises that the author followed the Shari'ah order: Quran, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas.

5. **Inclusion of Qiyas**: The author explicitly mentions three (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) and implicitly includes Qiyas in the phrase 'masalik al-mu'tabarin' (paths of the considered ones), derived from 'i'tibar' which implies Qiyas.

6. **Precedence of hadith text over Ijma**: The objection is that only qat'i (definitively transmitted) Sunnah precedes Ijma, but the author gave absolute precedence. The response: The matn (text) of hadith is always clear; the issue is only in thubut (transmission). For the Companions, who dealt with mutawatir or well-known hadith, the matn is authoritative. The author’s order is consistent with Shari'ah because even if a hadith is ahad, its matn is considered over Ijma in Hanafi usul under certain conditions.

Key Terms
اركان (arkan): Here, pillars meaning foundational supports for the rulings, either as integral parts or external strengtheners.
ادلة كلية (adillah kulliyyah): General proofs that encompass many particular proofs (e.g., the Quran as a whole).
متن حديث (matn hadith): The text/content of a hadith, as opposed to its chain of transmission (sanad).
ادلة جزئية (adillah juz'iyyah): Particular proofs that apply to specific rulings, like individual Quranic verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, how does the author of Al-Tawdih include Qiyas among the four pillars?
A) In a separate section explicitly titled 'Qiyas'.
B) Implicitly in the phrase 'masalik al-mu'tabarin', derived from 'i'tibar' meaning Qiyas.
C) By analogy to the three other proofs.
D) By citing a hadith that mentions Qiyas.

Key Takeaway
The four general proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are the foundational pillars of Shari'ah rulings, from which all particular proofs derive and to which they refer back.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
Mutashabih: The Ambiguous Verses Known Only to Allah
Defining mutashabih and its purpose as a test

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutashabih in Hanafi usul, explain its unknowable interpretation, and identify the benefit of its revelation.

Core Idea
Mutashabih verses have rulings known only to Allah, serving as a test for scholars.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the author's classification of Quranic texts, focusing on mutashabih (ambiguous) verses. The Hanafi school holds that the true interpretation (ta'wil) of such verses is inaccessible to human reason. This lesson unpacks the definition, the metaphor of veiled secrets, and the divine wisdom behind revealing ambiguous passages as a test for the deeply learned.

Guided Path
1
Identify textual clarity levels
The passage distinguishes between muhkam (clear) and mutashabih (ambiguous) texts. Recognize that muhkam is the highest clarity in the Hanafi hierarchy (zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam), while mutashabih is the most hidden.
The author uses an analogy of a house: some rulings are apparent, others hidden.
2
Define mutashabih
Mutashabih is a verse whose intended meaning is not accessible to human reason; only Allah knows its ta'wil. The commentator stresses that its appearance is not hoped for at all.
The term 'maqsuraat' (confined) and the metaphor of tents pitched over it emphasize total inaccessibility.
3
Understand the purpose (fa'idah)
The revelation of mutashabih tests the firmly grounded in knowledge (al-rasikhūn fi al-ilm) by preventing them from reflecting and reaching the secrets. This is a trial opposite to their desire.
The trial of the ignorant is pursuing unwanted knowledge; the trial of scholars is restraint from beloved inquiry.
4
Address the objection about rulings
A student may ask: 'If mutashabih is unknowable, does it have rulings?' The passage affirms that mutashabih has rulings, but they are unknown to us. The rulings exist but are not accessible.
This reinforces that mutashabih is not meaningless; its legal content remains hidden.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul hierarchy
Place mutashabih within the Hanafi classification: texts range from zahir (apparent) to muhkam (most clear) and from mujmal (vague) to mutashabih (totally ambiguous).
The passage also mentions khafi (obscure) as an intermediate level.

جواب:۔ یہاں وہ احکام مراد ہیں۔ جو فسر و حکم اور متشابہ وغیرہ سے معلوم ہوں لہذا ماقبل کی تشبیہ کے ساتھ مناسبت واضح ہے۔ سوال:۔ ظاہر نص مفسر محکم کے احکام تو ہوتے ہیں لیکن متشابہہ کے تو احکام نہیں ہوتے۔ لہذا امتشابہات مراد لینا درست نہیں ہے جواب:۔ متشابہہ کے بھی احکام ہوتے ہیں لیکن ہمیں معلوم نہیں ہوتے ۔
قَولُهُ مَقصُورَاتُ أَى مَحبُوسَاتٌ جَعَلَ خِيَامَ الاستتار مَصْرُوبَةً عَلَى المُتَشَابِهِ مُحِيطَةٌ بِهِ بحيث لا يُرجى بُدُوهُ وَظُهُورُهُ أَصَلا عَلَى مَا هُوَ المَذهَبُ مِن أَنَّ المُتَشَابِهَ لَا يَعْلَمُ تَأْوِيلَهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَفَائِدَةُ إنزَالِهِ ابْتِلاءُ الرَّاسِخِينَ فِي العِلمِ بِمَنعِهِمْ عَن التَّفَكُرِ فِيهِ وَالوُصُولِ إِلَى مَا هُوَ غَايَةُ مُتَمَنَّاهُم مِن العِلمِ بِأَسْرَارِهِ فَكَمَا أَنَّ الجُهَّالُ مُبْتَلُونَ بِتَحصِيلِ مَا هُوَ غَيْرُ مَطلوب عِندَهُم مِن العِلمِ وَالإِمْعَانِ فِي الطَّلَبِ كَذَلِكَ العُلَمَاءُ مُبْتَلُونَ بِالوَقفِ وَتَركِ مَا هُوَ مَحبُوبٌ عِندَهُم إِذْ ابْتِلاءُ كُلّ أَحَدٍ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِمَا هُوَ عَلَى خِلَافِ هَوَاهُ وَعَکسِ مُتَمَنَّاهُ . قَولُهُ بِكَبْحٍ عَنَانِ ذَهنِهِم تَقُولُ كَبَحتُ الدَّابَّةَ إِذَا جَذَبَتَهَا إِلَيكَ بِالرِّجَامِ لِكَى تَقِفَ وَلَا تَجْرِيَ قَولُهُ أَودَعَهَا فِيهَا أَى أَودَعَ اللَّهُ الأَسرَارَ فِى المُتَشَابِهَاتِ وَالإِيدَاعُ مُتَعَدٌ إِلَى مَفعُولين تَقُولُ أَو دَعته مَالًا إِذَا دَفَعته إلَيهِ لِيَكُونَ وَدِيعَةٌ عِندَهُ وَإِنَّمَا عَدَّاهُ بِفِي تَسَامُحًا أَو تَضمِينًا بِمَعنَى الإِدْرَاجِ وَالوَضِعِ .
ترجمہ : مقصورات یعنی بند ہیں۔ کر دیا ہے استتار کے خیموں کو بند متشابہہ پر اس حال میں کہ محیط ہیں اس کے ساتھ اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں امید کی جاسکتی اس کے ظاہر ہونے کی بالکل جیسا کہ یہی مذہب ہے (حنفیہ کا) کہ بے شک متشابہ کی تاویل اللہ کے سوا کوئی نہیں جانتا۔ اور ان کے نازل کرنے کا فائدہ رانھیں فی العلم کی آزمائش کرنا ہے ان کو روکنے کے ساتھ غور و فکر کرنے سے اور اپنی تمناو خواہش کی انتہا تک پہنچنے سے اس کے رازوں کو جان لینے سے جیسا کہ بے شک جاہل آزمائے جاتے ہیں اس چیز کے حاصل کرنے کے ساتھ جس کا جاننا نہیں ہوتا مطلوب ان کو اور گہرائی کو طلب کرنے سے اسی طرح علماء آزمائے جاتے نہیں رکنے کے ساتھ اور اس چیز کے ترک کرنے کے ساتھ کہ جو محبوب ہے ان کے نزدیک اس لیے کہ ہر ایک کی آزمائش اس کی خواہش کے خلاف ہوتی ہے اور اس کی تمنا کے برعکس ہوتی ہے۔ قولہ ملیح عنان ومنهم: تو کہتا ہے کہ گھٹ الدلبہ جس وقت تو اس کو لگام سے اپنی طرف کھینچتا کہ وہ جانور رک جائے اور نہ چلے۔ قولہ اودعها فيها: یعنی یہ اور ع الله الاسرار في المتصابہات کے معنی میں ہے ودیعت رکھ دیا اللہ نے رازوں کو متشابہات میں اور لفظ ابداع دو مفعولوں کی طرف متعدی ہوتا ہے تو کہتا ہے اوردعتہ مالا جب تو اس کی طرف مال سپرد کر دے تا کہ یہ اس کے پاس امانت ہو جائے اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ مصنف نے متعدی کیا ہے حرف نی کے ساتھ از روئے تسامح کے یا از روئے تضمین کے اوراج اور وضع کے معنی میں لغوی تحقیق:۔ خیام جمع ہے خیمہ کی۔ مضروبہ : یعنی گاڑے ہوئے ہیں۔ یقال ضرب الخیمہ اس نے خیمہ گاڑ دیا۔ اسرار : جمع سرکی راز ۔ الامعان کسی بھی کی تہہ تک پہنچنا۔ ہوا۔ خواہش۔ تشریح : قولہ مقصورات :۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے متن کی توضیح بیان کی ہے کہ مقصورات الخیام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ متشابہہ جیسے اور پردوں میں اس طرح بند ہیں کہ جس کے ظاہر ہونے کی امید باقی نہیں رہتی ۔ جیسا کہ احناف کا مذہب ہے
The hadith was definitive; thus when Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) argued with the hadith 'Prophets do not bequeath', all the Companions accepted and none rejected, but the proof of the hadith has obscurity because it depends on the chain of transmission, and due to some impediment in the chain, conjecture arises. Summary of the answer: that the text intended by 'hadith' and 'sunnah' is the wording of the hadith, and there is no obscurity in it being given precedence over consensus. Then he mentioned some divisions: This is the last part of the expression. In this expression, the commentator's purpose is to explain the excellence of the text: that the author mentioned the muhkamat and mutashabihat in the text, indicating that within the locus there are some things that are completely apparent and some hidden in veils such that no one besides the owner of the house can reach them. Similarly, the locus of rulings sometimes comprises apparent rulings, and that is the nass, zahir, mufassar, muhkam; and sometimes it comprises extremely hidden things that no one can access except Allah, like mutashabih; and some have lesser obscurity, like khafi, mujmal, etc. Question: These things — mutashabih, muhkam, mujmal, etc. — have no suitability to the simile, because they are categories of the Book of Allah, not of rulings, and the preceding [text] compared rulings to a house, not the Book of Allah. Answer: Here the rulings are meant that are known from the commentary, muhkam, and mutashabih, etc.; thus the suitability to the preceding simile is clear. Question: Zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam have rulings, but mutashabih does not have rulings; therefore taking mutashabihat is not correct. Answer: Mutashabih also has rulings, but we do not know them. His statement: 'maqsuraatu' means confined; he made the tents of concealment pitched over the mutashabih, surrounding it, such that its appearance and emergence is not hoped for at all, according to the school that the interpretation of mutashabih is not known except by Allah. The benefit of its revelation is to test those firmly grounded in knowledge by preventing them from reflecting upon it and reaching the ultimate object of their desire — knowledge of its secrets. Just as the ignorant are tested by acquiring what is not desired by them of knowledge and by persisting in seeking, so too the scholars are tested by stopping and abandoning what is beloved to them. For the trial of everyone is only by that which is contrary to their desire and opposed to their aspiration. His statement: 'with a check of the rein of their mind'; you say 'kabahtu al-dabbata' when you pull the animal towards you with the bridle so that it stops and does not run. His statement: 'He deposited them in it' means Allah deposited the secrets in the mutashabihat; 'idaa' is transitive to two objects; you say 'awda'tuhu maalan' when you give him property to be a trust with him. He made it transitive with 'fi' out of tolerance or by way of inclusion, meaning insertion and placement. Translation: 'Maqsuraat' means confined. He made the tents of concealment pitched over the mutashabih, surrounding it, such that its appearance cannot be hoped for at all, as is the school (of the Hanafis) that the interpretation of mutashabih is not known by anyone except Allah. The benefit of their revelation is to test those firmly grounded in knowledge by preventing them from reflecting and reaching the end of their desire to know its secrets. Just as the ignorant are tested by acquiring what is not desired by them of knowledge and by going deep in seeking, similarly the scholars are tested by stopping and leaving what is beloved to them, because everyone's trial is only by that which is contrary to their desire and opposite to their aspiration. His statement: 'with a check of the rein' — you say 'kabahtu al-dabbata' when you pull the animal towards you with the bridle so that it stops and does not run. His statement: 'He deposited them in it' means Allah deposited the secrets in the mutashabihat; 'idaa' is transitive to two objects; you say 'awda'tuhu maalan' when you give him property to be a trust with him. The author made it transitive with 'fi' by tolerance or by implication meaning insertion and placing. Lexical research: 'Khiyam' is the plural of 'khaimah' (tent). 'Madroobah' means pitched; it is said 'daraba al-khaimah' he pitched the tent. 'Asrar' is the plural of 'sirr' (secret). 'Al-im'an' means reaching the depth of something. 'Hawa' means desire. Commentary: His statement 'maqsuraat': in this passage the commentator explained the elucidation of the text: the meaning of 'maqsuraatu al-khiyam' is that mutashabih is confined in veils such that the hope of its appearance does not remain, as is the school of the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih clarifies the classification of Quranic texts, specifically the distinction between muhkam (clear) and mutashabih (ambiguous). The commentator expands on the author's analogy of a house with rooms: some rulings are apparent (like muhkam) and some are hidden (like mutashabih). The key Hanafi position is that the true interpretation (ta'wil) of mutashabih verses is known only to Allah. This does not mean mutashabih has no rulings; rather, the rulings exist but are unknown to us. The revelation of mutashabih serves as a trial for the deeply learned, preventing them from excessive speculation and testing their submission. The commentator also explains the Arabic terms: 'maqsuraat' (confined), the metaphor of tents pitched over mutashabih, and the concept that secrets are deposited within these verses. The benefit is to test both the ignorant and the scholars in different ways: the ignorant by pursuit of unwanted knowledge, and scholars by restraint from what they love. This passage reinforces the Hanafi methodology of textual analysis, emphasizing that some Quranic knowledge is beyond human reach.

Key Terms
مُحْكَم (muhkam): A verse whose meaning is clear and unambiguous, not subject to abrogation.
مُتَشَابِه (mutashabih): A verse whose intended meaning is not accessible to human reason; only Allah knows its ta'wil.
تأويل (ta'wil): The true interpretation or ultimate meaning of a verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the benefit of mutashabih verses?
A) To provide ambiguous rulings that scholars can interpret freely
B) To test the scholars by preventing them from reflecting on and knowing its secrets
C) To allow for multiple interpretations to accommodate different views
D) To indicate that the Quran is not fully preserved

Key Takeaway
Mutashabih verses are a divine test: their true interpretation is known only to Allah, and scholars must submit without attempting to uncover hidden meanings.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Definition of Mutashabihat and Their Exclusive Ta’wīl
Defining the Hanafi stance on mutashabihat with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mutashabihat according to the Hanafi school and state the Quranic proof that restricts knowledge of their ta’wīl to Allah alone.

Core Idea
The ta’wīl of mutashabihat is known only to Allah; the verse itself is qat ī in dalāla on this exclusivity.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of mutashabihat and the primary proof from Āl ‘Imrān 3:7. The passage glosses the phrase “maqṣūrāt al-khiyām” (confined in veils) to show the hidden nature of these verses, then cites the Quranic verse as the decisive evidence that only Allah knows their true interpretation. We will analyse the proof’s strength and see how the Hanafi school uses it to prohibit speculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Locate the term “al-mutashabihat” in the passage and note how the commentator describes them: verses confined in veils, their meaning hidden, and their true interpretation only known to Allah.
In the Urud commentary, compare the description to the earlier part about خیام (tents) and their confinement.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the citation of Āl ‘Imrān 3:7 in the passage: “وَمَا يَعْلَمُ تَأْوِيلَهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ”. Recognise that this is the core dalīl for the Hanafi position.
The commentator explicitly quotes the verse to support the claim.
3
Analyse the dalāla
Assess the proof’s strength: the verse has qat ī thubūt (Quran) and, in the Hanafi reading, qat ī dalāla because the phrase “إِلَّا اللَّهُ” clearly restricts knowledge to Allah.
Note the difference with the alternative reading that pauses after “الراسخون”.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
State the Hanafi usul rule: a nass text (like this verse) yields certain knowledge. Therefore, the ruling that only Allah knows the ta’wīl is definitive and not open to interpretation.
In Hanafi usul, nass is binding and cannot be overridden by mere opinion.
5
Distinguish from other positions
Recognise that the Shāfi‘ī school reads the verse with a different waqf (pause), allowing that the rāsikhūn may also know the ta’wīl. Understand the thamarah: Hanafis forbid all human ta’wīl of mutashabihat; Shāfi‘īs permit scholarly interpretation.
This difference arises from a textual nuance in qirā’a, not from a contradiction in the sources.

كلّ أحد إنما يكون بما هو على خلاف هواه وعکس متمنّاه . قوله بكبح عنان ذهنهم تقول كبحت الدابة إذا جذبتها إليك بالرجام لكى تقف ولا تجري قوله أودعها فيها أي أودع الله الأسرار في المتشابهات والإيداع متعد إلى مفعولين تقول أودعته مالا إذا دفعته إليه ليكون وديعة عنده وإنما عداه بفي تسامحا أو تضمينا بمعنى الإدراج والوضع .
ترجمہ : مقصورات یعنی بند ہیں۔ کر دیا ہے استتار کے خیموں کو بند متشابہہ پر اس حال میں کہ محیط ہیں اس کے ساتھ اس حیثیت سے کہ نہیں امید کی جاسکتی اس کے ظاہر ہونے کی بالکل جیسا کہ یہی مذہب ہے (حنفیہ کا) کہ بے شک متشابہ کی تاویل اللہ کے سوا کوئی نہیں جانتا۔ اور ان کے نازل کرنے کا فائدہ راسخین فی العلم کی آزمائش کرنا ہے ان کو روکنے کے ساتھ غور و فکر کرنے سے اور اپنی تمناو خواہش کی انتہا تک پہنچنے سے اس کے رازوں کو جان لینے سے جیسا کہ بے شک جاہل آزمائے جاتے ہیں اس چیز کے حاصل کرنے کے ساتھ جس کا جاننا نہیں ہوتا مطلوب ان کو اور گہرائی کو طلب کرنے سے اسی طرح علماء آزمائے جاتے نہیں رکنے کے ساتھ اور اس چیز کے ترک کرنے کے ساتھ کہ جو محبوب ہے ان کے نزدیک اس لیے کہ ہر ایک کی آزمائش اس کی خواہش کے خلاف ہوتی ہے اور اس کی تمنا کے برعکس ہوتی ہے۔ قولہ کبح عنان ومنهم: تو کہتا ہے کہ کبحت الدابة جس وقت تو اس کو لگام سے اپنی طرف کھینچتا کہ وہ جانور رک جائے اور نہ چلے۔ قولہ أودعها فيها: یعنی یہ اور ع الله الاسرار في المتصابہات کے معنی میں ہے (ودیعت رکھ دیا اللہ نے رازوں کو متشابہات میں ) اور لفظ ایداع دو مفعولوں کی طرف متعدی ہوتا ہے تو کہتا ہے اوردعتہ مالا جب تو اس کی طرف مال سپرد کر دے تا کہ یہ اس کے پاس امانت ہو جائے اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ مصنف نے متعدی کیا ہے حرف نی کے ساتھ از روئے تسامح کے یا از روئے تضمین کے اوراج اور وضع کے معنی میں لغوی تحقیق:۔ خیام جمع ہے خیمہ کی۔ مضروبہ : یعنی گاڑے ہوئے ہیں۔ یقال ضرب الخیمہ اس نے خیمہ گاڑ دیا۔ اسرار : جمع سرکی راز ۔ الامعان کسی بھی کی تہہ تک پہنچنا۔ ہوا۔ خواہش۔ تشریح : قولہ مقصورات :۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے متن کی توضیح بیان کی ہے کہ مقصورات الخیام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ متشابہہ جیسے اور پردوں میں اس طرح بند ہیں کہ جس کے ظاہر ہونے کی امید باقی نہیں رہتی ۔ جیسا کہ احناف کا مذہب ہے
متشابہات کی تاویل اللہ کے علاوہ کوئی نہیں جانتا۔ کما قال اللہ تعالیٰ و ہ یعلم تاویلہ الا اللہ۔ متشابہات کے نزول کی حکمت
قولہ وفائدة انزالہ: یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شارح نے سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔
سوال:۔ جب متشابہات کی مراد اللہ تعالٰی کے علاوہ کوئی نہیں جانتا تو ان کے اتارنے (نزول) کا کیا فائدہ ہے؟ جواب:۔ اس سے راسخین فی العلم کا امتحان لینا مقصود ہے کہ ان کی عادت ہوتی ہے کہ ہر چیز میں غور وفکر کرتے ہیں۔ تو متشابہات میں غور و فکر سے روک دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ ہر آدمی کا امتحان اس کی خواہش کے خلاف ہوتا ہے۔ اب اگر وہ غور وفکر نہ کریں کامیاب وگرنہ نا کام ۔ جس طرح جاہلوں کی عادت اور تمنا ہوتی ہے کہ وہ علم نہ حاصل کریں تو ان کو حکم دیا گیا کہ علم حاصل کرو۔ اس میں ان کا امتحان ہے کیونکہ یہ ان کی خواہش کے خلاف ہے۔
لفظ کیم میں عنان کی قید سے تجرید کی گئی ہے
قولہ کچھ عنان :۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے کم کالوی معنی بیان کیاہے کہ بی شق ہے۔ حجت الدا بہ سے اس کامعنی ہے کھینچا تو نے لگام کے ساتھ جانور کو تو یہاں کمج کا معنی کھینچنا ہوگا۔
سوال:۔ جب کج کے معنی میں لگام معتبر ہے تو دوبارہ عنان کو ذکر کرنے کی کیا ضرورت ہے۔ نیز کمک متعدی بنفسہ ہے تو اس کوئن کے ساتھ متعدی کیوں کیا ؟ (متن میں)۔
جواب:۔ اہل عرب کی عادت ہے کہ جب فعل کسی قید کے ساتھ مقید ہوتو کبھی فعل سے قید اور مقید دونوں مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اور کبھی صرف مقید مراد لیتے ہیں اور تجرید کرتے ہیں یعنی قید کا اعتبار نہیں کرتے ۔ تو یہاں لفظ سہج میں صرف کھینچنے والا معنی مراد ہو گا۔ قید کا یعنی لگام کا اعتبار نہیں کریں گے۔ اس لیے اس کے بعد عنان کا ذکر کرنا درست ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ اعتراض کہ اس کو عن کے ساتھ ذکر کیوں کیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں تضمین ہوئی ہے کہ یہ وصول کے معنی میں ہے اور وصول لازم ہے اور اس کا صلہ عن آسکتا ہے۔ قولہ اور عھا فیھا :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں شارح نے (ضمائر) کے مراجع متعین کیسے ہیں ۔ اور معھا میں ضمیر فاعل کا مرجع اللہ تعالیٰ ہیں اور ضمیر مفعول کا مرجع اسرار ہے۔ اور فیھا کی ضمیر کا مرجع متشابھات ہیں۔ معنیٰ ہوگا اللہ نے ودیعت رکھ دیا
Everyone is only tested by what is contrary to his desire and opposite to his wish. His statement: 'by restraining the rein of their minds' – you say 'kabahtu al-dābbah' when you pull the animal towards you with the bridle so that it stops and does not run. His statement: 'He deposited them in them' – meaning Allah deposited the secrets in the mutashabihat; 'īdā'' is transitive to two objects, you say 'awda‘tuhu mālan' when you hand over wealth to him to be a trust with him; he made it transitive with 'fī' due to leniency or by way of inclusion, meaning insertion and placement. [Urdu commentary follows explaining the text in detail.]
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from 'Al-Tarwīh li-ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ', explaining the Hanafi position on the mutashabihat (ambiguous verses of the Quran). The author first glosses the phrase 'maqṣūrāt al-khiyām' from the matn, meaning that the mutashabihat are confined within veils such that no hope remains of their apparent meaning being known. This aligns with the Hanafi doctrine that no one knows the ta’wīl (true interpretation) of the mutashabihat except Allah, as stated in the Quran (Āl ʿImrān 3:7). The commentator then addresses the question: If only Allah knows the interpretation, what is the benefit of revealing these verses? The answer is that it serves as a test for the rāsikhūn fī al-ʿilm (those firmly grounded in knowledge). They are naturally inclined to ponder and investigate everything, but here they are prevented from delving into the mutashabihat — this restraint is contrary to their desire, thus it becomes a test of their obedience. Just as the ignorant are tested by being commanded to seek knowledge (which is against their inclination), the scholars are tested by being commanded to refrain from excessive speculation. The passage then provides lexical analysis: 'kabḥ' means to pull an animal by the bridle to make it stop; 'īdāʿ' means to deposit something as a trust; the phrase 'awdaʿahā fīhā' refers to Allah depositing secrets in the mutashabihat. The commentator explains that the verb 'awdaʿa' is normally transitive to two objects, but here it is used with 'fī' either through tasāmuḥ (leniency) or taḍmīn (inclusion), meaning 'insertion'. Grammatical points are also discussed: the pronoun in 'fīhā' refers to the mutashabihat, and the verb forms are clarified. The overall teaching is that the Hanafi school holds the ta’wīl of mutashabihat as exclusively known to Allah, and the wisdom behind their revelation is to test the steadfastness of the believers.

Key Terms
المتشابهات (al-mutashābihāt): Quranic verses that are ambiguous or resemble other meanings, whose interpretation is known only to Allah.
تأويل (ta’wīl): The ultimate true interpretation or final meaning of a divine text, known only to Allah for mutashabihat.
الراسخون في العلم (al-rāsikhūn fī al-‘ilm): Those firmly grounded in Islamic knowledge; their test is to refrain from pursuing the interpretation of mutashabihat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct reading of Āl ‘Imrān 3:7 regarding the knowledge of ta’wīl?
A) 'wa mā ya‘lamu ta’wīlahu illā allāh' (stops at Allah)
B) 'wa mā ya‘lamu ta’wīlahu illā allāh wa al-rāsikhūn' (includes rāsikhūn)
C) stops at 'rāsikhūn'
D) none of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds the ta’wīl of mutashabihat as exclusively Allah's knowledge, as proven by the nass of Āl ‘Imrān 3:7.

The Wisdom Behind Revealing Mutashabihat: A Test for the Rāsikhūn
Explaining the wisdom behind mutashabihat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for the revelation of mutashabihat as a test for the firmly grounded scholars and apply the concept of testing contrary to one's desires.

Core Idea
Mutashabihat are revealed to test the rāsikhūn by commanding them to refrain from their natural inclination to investigate, contrary to their desires.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage: the wisdom behind revealing mutashabihat. The commentator answers the question: if only Allah knows the ta’wīl, why reveal these verses? The answer is that it serves as a test (imtiḥān) for the rāsikhūn fī al-‘ilm. We will explore how this test works and the linguistic elaboration that follows, including the verb 'kabḥ' (to restrain) and 'īdāʿ' (to deposit).

Guided Path
1
Identify the question and answer
In the passage, find the phrase 'Fā’idatu inzālihī' and note the answer: testing the rāsikhūn.
The question is implied: Why reveal verses whose meaning is hidden?
2
Analyze the test mechanism
Understand that the rāsikhūn are naturally inclined to ponder (ta’ammul), but they are prevented from doing so with the mutashabihat. This restraint is contrary to their desire, thus a test.
The test is not in understanding but in obedience.
3
Compare with the ignorant
Note the parallel: the ignorant are tested by being commanded to seek knowledge (contrary to their desire). Scholars are tested by being commanded to refrain.
Both groups succeed by acting contrary to their innate preferences.
4
Lexical exploration
Examine the words 'kabḥ' (to pull back with a bridle, symbolizing restraint) and 'īdāʿ' (to deposit secrets). Understand how they reinforce the concept.
The lexical analysis is a typical sharh expansion.
5
Derive the usul principle
The underlying principle: mutashabihat are not subject to human ta’wīl; one must affirm without specifying. This is binding based on the earlier proof.
This connects back to the lesson on the proof.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from 'Al-Tarwīh li-ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ', explaining the Hanafi position on the mutashabihat (ambiguous verses of the Quran). The author first glosses the phrase 'maqṣūrāt al-khiyām' from the matn, meaning that the mutashabihat are confined within veils such that no hope remains of their apparent meaning being known. This aligns with the Hanafi doctrine that no one knows the ta’wīl (true interpretation) of the mutashabihat except Allah, as stated in the Quran (Āl ʿImrān 3:7). The commentator then addresses the question: If only Allah knows the interpretation, what is the benefit of revealing these verses? The answer is that it serves as a test for the rāsikhūn fī al-ʿilm (those firmly grounded in knowledge). They are naturally inclined to ponder and investigate everything, but here they are prevented from delving into the mutashabihat — this restraint is contrary to their desire, thus it becomes a test of their obedience. Just as the ignorant are tested by being commanded to seek knowledge (which is against their inclination), the scholars are tested by being commanded to refrain from excessive speculation. The passage then provides lexical analysis: 'kabḥ' means to pull an animal by the bridle to make it stop; 'īdāʿ' means to deposit something as a trust; the phrase 'awdaʿahā fīhā' refers to Allah depositing secrets in the mutashabihat. The commentator explains that the verb 'awdaʿa' is normally transitive to two objects, but here it is used with 'fī' either through tasāmuḥ (leniency) or taḍmīn (inclusion), meaning 'insertion'. Grammatical points are also discussed: the pronoun in 'fīhā' refers to the mutashabihat, and the verb forms are clarified. The overall teaching is that the Hanafi school holds the ta’wīl of mutashabihat as exclusively known to Allah, and the wisdom behind their revelation is to test the steadfastness of the believers.

Key Terms
المتشابهات (al-mutashābihāt): Quranic verses that are ambiguous or resemble other meanings, whose interpretation is known only to Allah.
الراسخون في العلم (al-rāsikhūn fī al-‘ilm): Those firmly grounded in Islamic knowledge; their test is to refrain from pursuing the interpretation of mutashabihat.
كبح (kabḥ): To pull an animal by the bridle to make it stop; used figuratively for restraining the mind.
إيداع (īdāʿ): Depositing something as a trust; here referring to Allah depositing secrets into the mutashabihat.

The Wisdom of Revealing Mutashabihat
Explains the benefit of revealing ambiguous verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the ta'wil of mutashabihat and identify the wisdom behind their revelation as a test for those firmly rooted in knowledge.

Core Idea
The revelation of ambiguous verses is a divine test: the rasikhun are prevented from pondering them, proving their submission.

This passage from a sharh on Al-Taozeeh wa Al-Talweeh addresses a key question in Quranic hermeneutics: if the true meaning of mutashabihat is known only to Allah, why were they revealed? The commentator explains that the benefit (fa'idah) is to test the rasikhun (those firmly rooted in knowledge) by commanding them to refrain from deep speculation. This lesson unpacks that wisdom and the Hanafi approach to dealing with ambiguous verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
The passage begins by quoting Quran 3:7 that only Allah knows the ta'wil of mutashabihat. The implicit question is: what is the benefit of revealing verses whose meaning is inaccessible?
This question arises from a literal reading of the verse.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The Quranic verse (3:7) is cited: 'And none knows its interpretation except Allah.' The Hanafi view takes this as a definitive statement that knowledge of ta'wil is exclusive to Allah.
The verse is used as the primary dalil for the ruling.
3
Understand the test for the rasikhun
The commentator states that the rasikhun are tested by being prevented from pondering mutashabihat, despite their natural inclination to reflect. This test distinguishes those who submit from those who deviate.
The test is tailored to their disposition: it goes against their habit.
4
Contrast with the ignorant
The ignorant naturally dislike seeking knowledge, so they are commanded to acquire it. This also is a test, as it goes against their desire. Thus, the divine method tests each group by what is difficult for them.
This parallel illustrates the general principle of testing.
5
Derive the usul principle
From this, we derive that in Hanafi usul, mutashabihat are accepted as they are without ta'wil. The ruling (hukm) is that it is obligatory for the rasikhun to refrain from speculative interpretation and to affirm faith in the verses.
This principle guides how Hanafi scholars deal with ambiguous verses.

قولہ وفائدة انزالہ: یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔

سوال:۔ جب متشابہات کی مراد اللہ تعالٰی کے علاوہ کوئی نہیں جانتا تو ان کے اتارنے ( نزول ) کا کیا فائدہ ہے؟ جواب:۔ اس سے راسخین فی العلم کا امتحان لینا مقصود ہے کہ ان کی عادت ہوتی ہے کہ ہر چیز میں غور وفکر کرتے ہیں۔ تو متشابہات میں غور و فکر سے روک دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ ہر آدمی کا امتحان اس کی خواہش کے خلاف ہوتا ہے۔ اب اگر وہ غور وفکر نہ کریں کامیاب وگرنہ نا کام ۔ جس طرح جاہلوں کی عادت اور تمنا ہوتی ہے کہ وہ علم نہ حاصل کریں تو ان کو حکم دیا گیا کہ علم حاصل کرو۔ اس میں ان کا امتحان ہے کیونکہ یہ ان کی خواہش کے خلاف ہے۔
None knows the interpretation of the ambiguous verses except Allah. As Allah said: 'And none knows its interpretation except Allah.' The wisdom of revealing the ambiguous verses. Statement: 'And the benefit of its revelation': This is the second part of the expression; in this expression the commentator answered a question. 153 Question: When no one except Allah knows the meaning of the ambiguous verses, what is the benefit of revealing them? Answer: The purpose is to test those firmly rooted in knowledge, because it is their habit to ponder everything. So they are prevented from pondering the ambiguous verses. For every person is tested by what is contrary to his desire. If they refrain from pondering, they succeed; otherwise they fail. Just as the habit and desire of the ignorant is not to acquire knowledge, so they are commanded to acquire knowledge. This is a test for them because it is against their desire.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the wisdom behind revealing mutashabihat (ambiguous) Quranic verses. The author first quotes the Quranic verse (3:7) that only Allah knows their true interpretation. Then the commentator (sharih) explains that the benefit (fa'idah) of revealing such verses is to test those who are firmly rooted in knowledge (rasikhun fi al-ilm). Since these scholars are accustomed to deep reflection, they are prevented from speculating on the mutashabihat. This trial is against their natural inclination, thus a true test. Similarly, the ignorant desire not to learn, so they are commanded to learn, making it a test for them as well. The point is that divine wisdom places tests in matters contrary to one's habits to distinguish the obedient from the disobedient.

Key Terms
متشابہات (mutashabihat): Verses of the Quran whose intended meaning is known only to Allah, and whose apparent meaning may be open to multiple interpretations.
راسخین فی العلم (rasikhun fi al-ilm): Those who are deeply rooted and firm in knowledge, i.e., the learned scholars who are tested by being prevented from pondering the mutashabihat.
تأویل (ta'wil): Interpretation or final understanding of the true meaning of ambiguous verses, which only Allah knows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the primary benefit (faa'idah) of revealing mutashabihat verses?
A) To confuse the ignorant
B) To test those firmly rooted in knowledge
C) To allow scholars to exercise independent reasoning
D) To provide an opportunity for multiple interpretations

Key Takeaway
The revelation of mutashabihat is a divine test; the rasikhun succeed by affirming belief without seeking the true interpretation.

Defining I'jaz: The Inimitability of the Quran
Defining i'jaz and responding to objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define i'jaz as the impossibility of reproducing the Quran's speech, distinguish it from balaghah and sihr al-kalam, and explain the Hanafi response to two key objections.

Core Idea
I'jaz is not just eloquence—it is the impossibility of reproducing the Quran's speech, a fixed limit beyond human capacity.

This passage unpacks the precise definition of i'jaz (inimitability) in the Quran, a foundational concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Understanding this definition is crucial because the Quran's i'jaz establishes its divine origin and thus its authority as a definitive proof (dalil qat'i). The author clarifies that i'jaz is more than mere eloquence—it involves the inability of humans to produce anything like it, and he distinguishes it from verbal magic (sihr al-kalam). We will work through the definition, the two objections raised against it, and the author's responses.

Guided Path
1
Extract the core definition of i'jaz
Read the passage and identify where the author defines i'jaz. Note the phrase 'لا يمكن للبشر الإتيان بمثله' (it is not possible for humans to produce its like). This is the essence: impossibility of imitation.
The author emphasizes that i'jaz is not merely being more eloquent but involves the inability to produce similar speech.
2
Distinguish i'jaz from balaghah and sihr al-kalam
Look for the comparison between i'jaz and both balaghah (eloquence) and sihr al-kalam (verbal magic). The passage states that balaghah alone is insufficient, and sihr al-kalam has no fixed limit and can be imitated, unlike i'jaz which has a fixed limit.
Sihr al-kalam is described as having no boundary, while i'jaz has a definite limit (the highest degree of eloquence or close to it) that cannot be overcome.
3
Analyze the first objection and its answer
The first objection is that i'jaz is only in Allah's speech, so what does 'more eloquent' mean? The answer: it means more eloquent than all actual and hypothetical speech, making imitation impossible.
The author uses the term 'مُحَقَّقًا أَوْ مُقَدَّرًا' (actual or hypothetical) to show the comprehensive nature of i'jaz.
4
Analyze the second objection and its answer
The second objection is that i'jaz can be at different degrees (highest or close), implying multiple kinds. The answer: these degrees are unified because they all represent a limit beyond which no human can go, unlike sihr al-kalam.
The author stresses that i'jaz is a single property regardless of degree, as long as it cannot be opposed.
5
Identify the multiple aspects of i'jaz
The passage mentions different scholarly views on the aspect of i'jaz (eloquence, news of the unseen, unique style, etc.). The author adopts the view that it is the ultimate eloquence that causes inability.
In Hanafi usul, the i'jaz of the Quran is a multifaceted proof, but the common factor is the impossibility of opposition.

The high station that is not possible for humans to produce something like it; both are miracles according to what was mentioned in al-Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz. And then the path of i'jaz also becomes multiple by it being at the highest degree or at some of the close ranks. The answer to the first objection is that i'jaz is only in the speech of Allah, and the meaning of it being more eloquent than all besides it is that it is more eloquent than every speech that is other than the speech of Allah, whether actual or hypothetical, so that others cannot produce its like. The answer to the second objection is that i'jaz, whether it is at the highest degree or close to it, is unified in consideration that it is a limit of speech that is more eloquent than all besides it, meaning that others cannot oppose it or produce its like, unlike verbal sorcery (sihr al-kalam) because it has no fixed limit.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of i'jaz (inimitability) in the Quran. It begins by affirming that both the highest degree of eloquence and degrees close to it are miraculous, citing al-Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz. It then addresses two objections: first, that i'jaz is only in Allah's speech, and its being more eloquent means it surpasses all other speech, whether actual or hypothetical, making it impossible for anyone else to produce its like. Second, that i'jaz is unified whether at the highest or lower ranks because it is a fixed limit of speech that cannot be opposed, unlike sihr al-kalam (word magic) which has no fixed limit. The Urdu commentary expands: the correct definition of i'jaz is not simply conveying meaning in the most eloquent way, but rather that the speech is such that it cannot be contradicted or imitated. There are differences among scholars on the aspect of i'jaz: some say it is due to eloquence, others due to informing of the unseen, others due to its unique style, and others due to Allah turning away minds from opposing it. The correct view is that the i'jaz of the Quran is in its ultimate eloquence and eloquence. The condition in i'jaz is that it surpasses all other speech in eloquence. Unlike sihr al-kalam, which is based on subtle and delicate sources and occurs in multiple ways and ranks, i'jaz is singular. The term 'sihr' is used in the plural and 'urwat al-i'jaz (the handle of i'jaz) in the singular because i'jaz is stronger and has a fixed standard. Two sections are then presented: first, that conveying meaning in a way that is more eloquent than all existing actual methods is not sufficient for i'jaz; rather, it must lead to inability to oppose or produce its like, including all possible methods—though Allah is capable of producing its like despite its being miraculous. Second, that both the highest degree of eloquence and close degrees are miraculous, as mentioned in al-Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz, and thus the ways of i'jaz become multiple. The answer to the first objection is that i'jaz is only in Allah's speech, and its being more eloquent than all others means it surpasses every actual and potential speech. The answer to the second is that i'jaz is unified whether at the highest or near degree, being a single limit of speech that is more eloquent than all others, such that no human can oppose it, unlike sihr al-kalam which has no limiting boundary.

Key Terms
الإعجاز (al-i'jaz): The quality of being inimitable; the inability of others to produce similar speech, not merely being more eloquent.
سحر الكلام (sihr al-kalam): Word magic; speech that captivates through subtlety and delicacy but has no fixed limit and does not reach the level of i'jaz.
البلاغة (al-balaghah): Eloquence; conveying meaning in the most effective way. Not identical to i'jaz, as i'jaz requires the impossibility of opposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be the most eloquent speech among all.
B) It must be impossible to oppose or produce its like.
C) It must be revealed through a prophet.
D) It must have a fixed limit like sihr al-kalam.

Key Takeaway
The i'jaz of the Quran is defined by the impossibility of human imitation, a fixed limit that distinguishes it from mere eloquence and verbal magic.

The Jihah of I'jāz: Hanafi Position on Qur'anic Inimitability
Commentary on definition of I'jāz and resolution of jihah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the jihah of I'jāz and apply the criterion of intrinsic universality to evaluate competing views.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is inimitable because its eloquence is intrinsic to every verse, not due to external factors like news of the unseen.

Scholars agree that the Qur'an is miraculous (I'jāz), but they differ on what aspect (jihah) makes it so. This dispute is not merely theoretical; it affects how we understand the Qur'an's challenge and the nature of its proof for prophethood. In this passage, the commentator defends the Hanafi view that extreme eloquence (balāghah) is the sole intrinsic jihah, rejecting alternatives like news of the unseen or the turning away of minds.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish I'jāz and Balāghah
First, understand that I'jāz is the state of being inimitable, while balāghah is the quality of conveying meaning with eloquence. The objection claims that the matn defined I'jāz when he actually described balāghah. Recognize that I'jāz is broader—it can also be found in aspects other than eloquence, such as news of the unseen.
This distinction is key to the dispute.
2
Identify the Dispute over Jihah
List the four main opinions mentioned: (1) extreme eloquence, (2) news of the unseen, (3) unique style, (4) ṣarf al-ʿuqūl (Allah turning away minds). The commentator will evaluate each.
The dispute is not about the existence of I'jāz but its specific cause.
3
Apply the Hanafi Criterion: Intrinsic and Universal
The commentator argues that the correct jihah must be intrinsic to the Qur'an itself and present in every verse. Reason: the whole Qur'an is miraculous. If the jihah were only in some verses (e.g., those containing news of the unseen), other verses would not be miraculous.
This is a rational (ʿaqlī) argument based on the premise of complete inimitability.
4
Evaluate Alternative Jihahs
Test each alternative against the criterion. News of the unseen: not present in all verses. Unique style: subjective and not universally agreed. Ṣarf al-ʿuqūl: external to the text itself—makes the Qur'an's miraculousness dependent on an external act, not its own quality.
Only eloquence is intrinsic and present in all verses.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi Tarjih
The commentator concludes that extreme eloquence is the chosen (mukhtār) jihah. This view aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on the Qur'an's linguistic miraculousness as a proof of prophethood.
This tarjih is based on dalīl ʿaqlī and the need for universality.

اچک لینا اور ہر اس چیز کو کہتے ہیں جس کا ماخذ لطیف ہو اور دقیق ہو۔ پس وہ سحر ہے اور اس کے پکڑنے کا معنی مبالغہ کرنا ہے کلام کے لطیف ہونے میں اور معانی کے ادا کرنے میں ان عبارات کے ساتھ جو کہ لائق ہیں فائق ہیں یہاں تک کہ وہ قریب ہو جائے سحر کی طرف اور اعجاز کی طرف، اور یہاں دو بخشیں ہیں اول یہ ہے کہ معنی کا ادا کرنا ایسے طریقہ کچھ ساتھ کہ وہ المغل ہو۔ جمیع ماعدا کے طرق محققہ موجودہ سے نہیں ہے وہ کافی اعجاز میں بلکہ ضروری ہے عاجز ہونا اس کے معارضہ کرنے اور اس کی مثل لانے سے۔ اور طرق محققہ ومقدرہ سے (عاجز ہونا) یہاں تک کہ نہ ہو ممکن لانا اس کی مثل کو غیر مشروط ہے اس (اعجاز ) کے لیے بے شک اللہ قادر ہے لانے پر قرآن کے مثل باوجود اسکے معجز ہونے کے۔ پس نہیں ہے کوئی معنی اس کے قول ابلغ من جمیع ماعدا گا۔ اور بحث ثانی بے شک طرف اعلیٰ بلاغت کی اور جو قریب ہے اس سے ان بلند مراتب میں ہے کہ نہیں ہے ممکن انسان کے لیے اس کی مثل لانا دونوں معجز ہیں جیسا کہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے مفتاح میں اور نہایتہ الاعجاز میں ۔ اور اس وقت اعجاز کے طریق بھی متعدد ہو جائینگے بایں طور کہ ہوں وہ طرف اعلیٰ پر یا ان مراتب پر جو قریب ہیں اس سے ، اور جواب اول کا بے شک اعجاز نہیں ہے مگر اللہ تعالیٰ کی کلام میں اور اس کے جمیع ماعد اسے اہلغ ہونے کا معنی یہ ہے کہ وہ ابلغ ہو ہر اس کلام سے جو غیر اللہ کا کلام ہو محققا یا مقدرا۔ یہاں تک کہ نہیں ہے ممکن غیر کے لیے اس کی مثل لانا اور جواب ثانی کا یہ ہے بے شک اعجاز برابر ہے کہ ہو طرف اعلیٰ میں یا اس (طرف) میں جو قریب ہو اس سے متحد ہے اس اعتبار کے ساتھ کے بے شک وہ حد ہے کلام سے کہ وہ ابلغ ہو اس کے جمیع ماعدا سے اس معنی کے ساتھ کہ بے شک نہیں ہے ممکن بشر کے لیے اس کا معارضہ کرنا اور لانا اس کی مثل بخلاف سحر کلام کے پس بے شک نہیں ہے کوئی ایسی حد جو ضبط کرے اس کو ۔
قرآن کریم کیلئے جہت اعجاز کی تعیین
تشریح لان الاعجاز ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شارح نے ایک سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ ماتن نے جو اعجاز کی تعریف کی ہے یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ مائن نے کہا ہے کہ اعجاز فی الکلام یہ ہے کہ معنی کو ایسے طریقہ سے ادا کیا جائے جو ماسوا کے تمام طرق سے ابلغ ہو حالانکہ اعجاز فی الکلام کی تعریف یہ نہیں بن سکتی کیونکہ تعریف کی شرط یہ ہے کہ معرف ( بالکسر ) معرف ( بافتح) کے مساوی ہو یہی وجہ ہے کہ تعریف بالا م اور تعریف بالاخص جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا انسان کی تعریف حیوان کے ساتھ کی جائے یا حیوان کی تعریف انسان کے ساتھ کی جائے تو یہ دونوں نا جائز ہیں جب نیہ بات معلوم ہو گئی تو اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تعریف صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام اعم ہے۔ اور معنی کو ادا کرنا اس طرق پر جو تمام ماسوا کے طرق سے ابلغ ہو ۔ اس کو بلاغت کہتے ہیں اور بلاغت اخص ہے۔ اور اعجاز فی الکلام عام ہونے کی وجہ سے بلاغت کے ماسوا میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔ اور اس پر دلیل کہ اعجاز فی الکلام بلاغت کے ماسوا میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ علماء کا اجماع ہے کہ قرآن معجز ہے اور قرآن کے معجز ہونے پر اتفاق کے باوجود مفسرین کا جہت اعجاز میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض نے کہا ہے که قرآن فصاحت و بلاغت کی انتہا کو پہنچا ہوا ہے اس لئے یہ معجز ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ مغیبات کی خبریں دینے کی وجہ سے یہ معجز ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہ اپنے عجیب و غریب اسلوب کی وجہ سے معجز ہے، اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اس کے معجز ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کے مقابلہ کرنے سے عقلوں کو پھیر دیا ہے تو اگر اعجاز کی یہی تعریف درست ہوتی جو ماتن نے ذکر کی ہے تو پھر قرآن کی جہت اعجاز میں مفسرین کا اختلاف نہ ہوتا۔
جواب:۔ ماتن نے اپنے قول ولان الاعجاز فی الکلام ،، الخ سے اعجاز کی تعریف نہیں کی ہے کیونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام کی تعریف ہے کون الکلام بحیث لا یمکن معارضة والاتیان بمثلہ یعنی کلام کا ایسی حیثیت میں ہوتا کہ اس کا معارضہ نہ کیا جا سکے ۔ راس کی مثل لانا ممکن نہ ہو بلکہ ماتن نے اپنے اس قول میں قرآن کے منیجز ہونے کی جہت کو بیان کیا ہے کہ میرے نزدیک قرآن اس وجہ سے معجز ہے کہ وہ فصاحت و بلاغت کی انتہا کو پہنچا ہوا ہے۔ باقی جو جہات بیان کی گئی ہیں وہ درست نہیں ہیں کیونکہ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ قرآن مغیبات کی خبر دینے کی وجہ سے معجز ہے تو لازم آئے گا کہ جن آیات میں غیب کی خبریں نہیں دی گئیں۔ وہ معجز نہ ہوں ۔ اور یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرآن سارا معجز ہے اور اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ قرآن اس وجہ سے معجز ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کے مقابلے سے عقلوں کو پھیر دیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ قرآن فی نفسہ مسجد نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ خارج کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے معجز ہے۔ حالانکہ قرآن فی نفسہ معجز ہے اس لیے ماحو المختار جہت وہی ہے جو میں نے بیان کی ہے۔
فباعتبار انہ:۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے ایک سوال کا جواب دیا ہے جس کی تفصیل ماقبل کے متن میں گزر چکی ہے۔
