لغوی تحقیق
رب الثوب:۔ یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ لغوی تحقیق بیان کرنا ہے۔ احد اب جمع ہے حدب کی اور حدب الثوب کا مطلب ہوتا ہے وہ پھندن جو کپڑے کے کنارے پر لگائے جاتے ہیں۔ اور عروۃ الکوز لوٹے کے اس کڑے کو کہتے ہیں جس سے لوٹے کو پکڑا جاتا ہے۔ وهی اقوى من الحدب :۔ یہ عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ توضیح میں مذکور دوسرے سوال کے جواب کی طرف
Snatching and it is said for everything whose source is subtle and precise. So it is magic, and its meaning is exaggeration in subtlety of speech and in conveying meanings with expressions that are worthy and excellent until it approaches magic and I'jāz. And here there are two divisions: first, that meaning is conveyed in such a way that it is absolute. It is not from all the other verified existing methods; that suffices for I'jāz, but rather it is necessary to be incapable of opposing it and bringing its like. And from the verified and estimated methods (incapability) to the extent that it is not possible to bring its like is unconditional for this I'jāz. Indeed, Allah is able to bring the like of the Qur'an despite its being miraculous. So there is no meaning to his saying 'more eloquent than all others'. And the second discussion: indeed, the extreme of eloquence and what is close to it are among those high ranks that it is not possible for man to bring its like; both are miraculous, as mentioned in Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jāz. And then the methods of I'jāz will become multiple: either at the extreme level or at the ranks close to it. And the answer to the first: indeed, I'jāz is only in the speech of Allah Almighty, and the meaning of it being more eloquent than all other speech, actual or potential, is that it is more eloquent than every speech that is not from Allah, actual or potential, to the extent that it is not possible for others to bring its like. And the answer to the second: indeed, I'jāz is the same whether it is at the extreme level or at what is close to it; it is unified in the sense that it is a limit of speech that it is more eloquent than all others, with the meaning that it is not possible for any human to oppose it and bring its like. Unlike the speech of magicians, so there is no limit that can restrain it.
Determination of the jihah of I'jāz for the Qur'an.
Explanation of 'since I'jāz'. This is the first part of the commentary's passage. In this passage, the commentator answers a question. Question: The matn's definition of I'jāz is not correct because he said that I'jāz in speech is that meaning is conveyed in a way more eloquent than all other methods, but that cannot be the definition of I'jāz in speech because the condition of definition is that the definiendum and the definition be equivalent. That is why definition by the general and definition by the specific are not permissible. For example, defining man as animal or defining animal as man; both are invalid. Now that this is known, we say that this definition is not correct because I'jāz in speech is more general. And conveying meaning in a way more eloquent than all other methods is called balāghah, and balāghah is more specific. And I'jāz in speech, being general, is also found outside of balāghah. The evidence that I'jāz in speech is found outside of balāghah is the consensus of scholars that the Qur'an is miraculous, and despite the agreement on the Qur'an being miraculous, the exegetes differ on the jihah of I'jāz. Some said that the Qur'an is at the peak of eloquence, therefore it is miraculous. Some said it is miraculous due to giving news of the unseen. Some said it is miraculous due to its wonderful style. Some said the reason for its miraculousness is that Allah turned away minds from opposing it. If the definition that the matn mentioned were correct, then there would be no difference among exegetes regarding the jihah of I'jāz.
Answer: The matn did not define I'jāz in his statement 'since I'jāz in speech', etc. Rather, the definition of I'jāz in speech is that the speech is in such a state that it cannot be opposed and its like cannot be produced. But the matn, in his statement, explained the jihah of the Qur'an being miraculous: that in my view, the Qur'an is miraculous because it has reached the peak of eloquence. As for the other jihahs mentioned, they are not correct. Because if it is said that the Qur'an is miraculous due to giving news of the unseen, then it would follow that the verses that do not give news of the unseen would not be miraculous. That is not correct because the whole Qur'an is miraculous. And if it is said that the Qur'an is miraculous because Allah turned away minds from opposing it, that would mean that the Qur'an is not miraculous in itself, but rather it is miraculous by relation to an external factor. But the Qur'an is miraculous in itself. Therefore, the chosen jihah is the one I have explained.
Then 'by consideration of it': This is the second part of the passage; in this passage, the commentator answers a question whose detail has passed in the previous text.

Linguistic investigation
'Rab al-thawb': This is the third part of the passage; the commentator intends to give a linguistic investigation. 'Aḥdāb' is the plural of 'ḥidāb', and 'ḥidāb al-thawb' means the fringes attached to the edge of the garment. And 'urwat al-kūz' refers to the handle of the jug by which it is held. And 'they are stronger than the ḥidāb': This is the fourth part of the passage; the commentator intends to answer the second question mentioned in al-Tawḍīḥ.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ, dealing with the definition of I'jāz (inimitability) of the Qur'an and its jihah (aspect or direction). The commentator addresses an objection: the matn's statement that I'jāz is conveying meaning in the most eloquent way is actually a definition of balāghah, not I'jāz, because I'jāz is general and balāghah specific. The commentator clarifies that the matn was not defining I'jāz but rather specifying its jihah for the Qur'an. The passage then discusses various opinions on the jihah of I'jāz: extreme eloquence, news of the unseen, unique style, and the turning away of minds (ṣarf al-ʿuqūl). The commentator refutes the alternatives except eloquence, arguing that the Qur'an is miraculous in itself and entirely so. The linguistic section briefly explains 'ḥidāb' (fringes) and 'urwah' (handle), possibly relating to a metaphor in the text.

Key Terms
اعجاز (i'jāz): A miraculous quality in speech that renders it impossible to be challenged or imitated.
بلاغت (balāghah): Eloquence in conveying meaning in the best possible manner.
جہت اعجاز (jihah al-i'jāz): The particular aspect or cause due to which the Qur'an is considered miraculous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the main reason for rejecting 'news of the unseen' as the jihah of I'jāz?
A) News of the unseen is not miraculous.
B) Not all verses contain news of the unseen, so the whole Qur'an would not be miraculous.
C) News of the unseen is only found in the Qur'an, not in previous scriptures.
D) The commentator accepts all jihahs as equally valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Qur'an's I'jāz is rooted in its extreme eloquence, an intrinsic quality present in every verse.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
6 min
The Aspect of I'jaz in the Quran: Eloquence vs. Other Views
Defends the author's view on the precise aspect of Quranic inimitability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the precise aspect (jihah) of Quranic inimitability and evaluate the arguments for and against alternative views.

Core Idea
The Quran’s i'jaz is rooted in its unparalleled eloquence, not in external factors or partial features.

What exactly makes the Quran miraculous? Scholars have debated whether its i'jaz lies in eloquence, predictions of the unseen, unique style, or even a divine prevention of imitation. This passage defends the view that i'jaz is inherently in the Quran's rhetorical excellence, refuting alternative positions that would make the miracle incomplete or extrinsic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim on i'jaz
Determine the author's preferred aspect of i'jaz from the text. The commentator states that the author did not define i'jaz but explained its aspect: the Quran is miraculous because it has reached the extreme of eloquence (fasahah wa balaghah).
The aspect is the specific dimension through which the miracle is manifested.
2
Follow the objector’s argument
The objector claims that if i'jaz were limited to eloquence, there would be no disagreement among exegetes because they mention other aspects. Identify this objection in the passage.
The objector assumes the author's statement is a definition, not an identification of aspect.
3
Analyze the author’s clarification
Explain how the commentator distinguishes between defining i'jaz (as the quality of being inimitable) and specifying its aspect (the cause of that quality in the Quran).
The definition is universal; the aspect is particular to the Quran.
4
Evaluate the refutation of alternative views
For each alternative (reports of the unseen, wondrous style, sarf), identify the logical flaw as stated in the text. For example, the unseen reports view fails because not all verses contain such reports.
The Hanafi response shows that only eloquence applies uniformly to the entire Quran.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Explain why the disagreement matters in usul al-fiqh: it affects how we argue for the Quran's authority and miraculous nature as a source of law.
If i'jaz were extrinsic, the Quran's evidentiary force could be questioned.

اور اس پر دلیل کہ اعجاز فی الکلام بلاغت کے ماسوا میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ علماء کا اجماع ہے کہ قرآن معجز ہے اور قرآن کے معجز ہونے پر اتفاق کے باوجود مفسرین کا جہت اعجاز میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض نے کہا ہے که قرآن فصاحت و بلاغت کی انتہا کو پہنچا ہوا ہے اس لئے یہ معجز ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ مغیبات کی خبریں دینے کی وجہ سے یہ معجز ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہ اپنے عجیب و غریب اسلوب کی وجہ سے معجز ہے، اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اس کے معجز ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کے مقابلہ کرنے سے عقلوں کو پھیر دیا ہے تو اگر اعجاز کی یہی تعریف درست ہوتی جو ماتن نے ذکر کی ہے تو پھر قرآن کی جہت اعجاز میں مفسرین کا اختلاف نہ ہوتا۔
جواب:۔ ماتن نے اپنے قول ولان الاعجاز فی الکلام ،، الخ سے اعجاز کی تعریف نہیں کی ہے کیونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام کی تعریف ہے کون الکلام بحیث لا یمکن معارضة والاتیان بمثلہ یعنی کلام کا ایسی حیثیت میں ہوتا کہ اس کا معارضہ نہ کیا جا سکے ۔ راس کی مثل لا نا ممکن نہ ہو بلکہ ماتن نے اپنے اس قول میں قرآن کے منیجز ہونے کی جہت کو بیان کیا ہے کہ میرے نزدیک قرآن اس وجہ سے معجز ہے کہ وہ فصاحت و بلاغت کی انتہا کو پہنچا ہوا ہے۔ باقی جو جہات بیان کی گئی ہیں وہ درست نہیں ہیں کیونکہ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ قرآن مغیبات کی خبر دینے کی وجہ سے معجز ہے تو لازم آئے گا کہ جن آیات میں غیب کی خبریں نہیں دی گئیں۔ وہ معجز نہ ہوں ۔ اور یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرآن سارا معجز ہے اور اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ قرآن اس وجہ سے معجز ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کے مقابلے سے عقلوں کو پھیر دیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ قرآن فی نفسہ مسجد نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ خارج کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے معجز ہے۔ حالانکہ قرآن فی نفسہ معجز ہے اس لیے ماحو المختار جہت وہی ہے جو میں نے بیان کی ہے۔
And the proof that i'jaz in speech is also found beyond eloquence is that there is consensus of scholars that the Quran is miraculous, and despite agreement on the Quran being miraculous, the exegetes differ on the aspect of i'jaz. Thus some said that the Quran has reached the pinnacle of eloquence and rhetoric, therefore it is miraculous. Some said it is miraculous because it reports unseen matters. Some said it is miraculous due to its wondrous style. And some said the reason for its miraculousness is that Allah turned away minds from competing with it. So if the definition of i'jaz that the author mentioned were correct, then there would be no difference of opinion among exegetes regarding the aspect of i'jaz.
Answer: The author, with his statement 'wa lan al-i'jaz fi al-kalam...' did not define i'jaz, because the definition of i'jaz in speech is that it is such that it cannot be opposed and its like cannot be produced. Rather, the author in this statement explained the aspect of the Quran's miraculousness, that in my view the Quran is miraculous because it has reached the extreme of eloquence and rhetoric. As for the other aspects that have been mentioned, they are not correct. Because if it is said that the Quran is miraculous due to reporting the unseen, then it would follow that those verses that do not report the unseen would not be miraculous, and this is incorrect because the entire Quran is miraculous. And if it is said that the Quran is miraculous because Allah turned minds away from competing with it, then this would mean that the Quran is not miraculous in itself, but rather it is considered miraculous by relation to an external factor, whereas the Quran is miraculous in itself. Therefore the chosen aspect is the one I have mentioned.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute about the exact aspect (jihah) of the Quran's inimitability (i'jaz). The objector argues that if the author's definition of i'jaz restricted it to eloquence, then there would be no disagreement among exegetes, since they hold different views on the cause of i'jaz. However, the commentator clarifies that the author did not define i'jaz but rather identified its aspect—namely, that the Quran's miraculous nature lies in its surpassing eloquence. The commentary then systematically refutes alternative views: (1) predictions of the unseen, because not all verses contain such predictions; (2) wondrous style, which is vague; (3) the theory of sarf (Allah turning minds away), because that would make i'jaz extrinsic rather than intrinsic to the Quran itself. The preferred view is that i'jaz is inherent in the Quran's eloquence.

Key Terms
اعجاز (i'jaz): The inimitability of speech such that it cannot be challenged or imitated; miraculous nature of the Quran.
جہت اعجاز (jihah al-i'jaz): The specific aspect or dimension through which the Quran is miraculous.
صرف (sarf): The theory that i'jaz is due to Allah turning minds away from imitating the Quran; a view rejected in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the view that i'jaz is due to reports of the unseen rejected?
A) Because those reports are not miraculous.
B) Because not all verses contain such reports, so they would not be miraculous.
C) Because the reports are ambiguous.
D) Because the scholars never mentioned this view.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Quran's i'jaz lies in its intrinsic eloquence, a view that alone applies uniformly to the entire text and preserves its inherent miraculous nature.

Defining the Quran's Miraculousness: Actual vs. Potential Eloquence
Analysis of two objections against Quranic i'jaz and their refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul scholars argue that the Quran's i'jaz is defined by superiority over actual (not estimated) speech, and distinguish between universal and individual oneness in i'jaz.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is proven by surpassing all actual eloquent speech at its peak, not by comparison to infinite potential.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text addresses two objections regarding the miraculous nature of the Quran. The first objection questions whether the Quran's eloquence must surpass all possible human speech or only that which actually existed. The second concerns the nature of 'oneness' in i'jaz. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for properly grounding the Quran's authority as a divine proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the text and locate the two questions that the author answers. The first relates to whether i'jaz requires superiority over all estimated ways or only actual ones. The second concerns the nature of 'one' in the definition of i'jaz.
2
Analyze the first answer: actual vs. estimated ways
Examine the author's reasoning: he chooses the second branch, stating that the Quran is more eloquent than all actual ways. He argues that estimated ways are irrelevant because at the time of revelation, eloquence had reached its peak, so comparison with hypothetical lower levels is meaningless.
The author refutes the commentator's claim that estimated ways must be included, calling it 'takalluf' (artificial).
3
Analyze the premise: miracles match their era
The author provides a premise: each prophet was given a miracle corresponding to the peak field of his time. For Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, that field was eloquence (balaghah), hence the Quran's miracle is in its rhetoric.
This premise supports the focus on actual eloquence at its peak.
4
Analyze the second answer: universal vs. individual oneness
The author distinguishes between 'al-wahid al-naw'i' (universal one) and 'al-wahid al-shakhsi' (individual one). He explains that i'jaz is a universal one with a single boundary encompassing all instances, unlike the distortion of speech (tahrif) which has no limit.
This refines the definition: i'jaz is a category, not a specific instance.
5
Summarize the overall argument
Synthesize: The Quran's i'jaz is established by its surpassing all actual eloquent speech at its peak, and it is a unified category that makes human imitation impossible. The objections are answered by clarifying the scope of comparison and the nature of oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب میں یہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ بلاغت کی طرف اعلیٰ اور جو مراتب علیا میں سے طرف اعلیٰ کے قریب ہوں لیکن بشر کے لیے ان کی مثل لا نا ممکن نہ ہو تو یہ دونوں معجز ہیں پھر تو اعجاز فی الکلام کے طرق بھی متعدد ہو گئے۔
سوال اول کا جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ ہم دوسری شق مراد لیتے ہیں کہ وہ طریق ابلغ ہو جمیع ماعدا سے عام ازیں طرق محققہ موجودہ بالفعل سے اہلغ ہو یا طرق مقدرہ سے ابلغ ہو۔ لیکن وہ طرق مخصوص ہیں کلام بشری کے ساتھ قرینہ یہ ہے کہ اعجاز فی الکلام سے کلام اللہ مراد ہے مقصد یہ ہے کہ اعجاز فی کلام اللہ یہ ہے کہ غیر اللہ کی کلام میں جتنے طرق ادا ہو سکتے ہیں خواہ محققہ ہوں خواه مقدرو کلام اللہ ان سب سے ابلغ ہو حتی کہ غیر اللہ کے لئے اس کی مثل لانا ممکن نہ ہواب اللہ تعالی کا اتیان بمثلہ پر قادر ہوتا اعجاز کلام اللہ کے منافی نہ ہوگا۔
ہر نبی کو معجزہ اس زمانہ میں عروج پانے والی مفتی کے مقابلے میں عطا ہوا
جواب ثانی:۔ اس کو سمجھنے سے قبل بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے۔ مقدمہ:۔ ہر نبی کو جو مجزہ عطا ہوا ہے وہ اس زمانہ میں اس شی کے مقابلہ میں ملا ہے جو اپنے عروج و انتہاء کو پہنچی ہوئی تھی مثلا حضرت عیسی علیہ السلام کے دور میں طب اپنی انتہاء کو پہنچی ہوئی تھی تو ان کو احیاء اموات کا معجزہ عطا ہوا، حضرت موسی علیہ السلام کے دور میں سحر و جادو اپنی انتہاء کو پہنچا ہوا تھا تو ان کو عصا کا معجزہ عطا ہوا، اسی طرح حضور اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے دور میں فصاحت و بلاغت اپنی انتہاء کو پہنچی ہوئی تھی کہ کعبتہ اللہ کی چوکھٹ پر سات قصیدے لٹکے ہوئے تھے اور لوگ مقابلہ کرنے سے عاجز تھے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو قرآن کا معجزہ عطا ہوا کہ فصیح بلیغ ہونے کے باوجودلوگ اس کا معارضہ نہ کر سکے۔ حاصیل جواب :۔ اب جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ماعدا کے طرق سے مراد طرق محققہ (موجودہ بالفعل ) ہیں کیونکہ طرق مقدرہ میں کسی طریق کے اہلغ ہونے کا تصور تو تب کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ اس وقت کے طرق محققہ میں بلاغت اپنی انتہاء کو نہ پہنچی ہوئی ہو حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہوسکتا اور اگر اس طرح ہو تو پھر یہ سنت اللہ کے خلاف ہوگا ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ شاریخ کا یہ کہنا کہ اعجاز فی الکلام کے لئے طرق مقدرہ سے ابلغ ہونا ضروری ہے یہ تکلف محض ہے۔
سوال ثانی کا جواب:۔ واحد کی دو قسمیں ہوتی ہیں۔ (۱) واحد نوعی جیسے انسان ۔ (۲) واحد شخصی جیسے زید۔ واحد نوعی کے تحت کئی افراد ہو سکتے ہیں۔ تو یہاں واحد سے مراد و احد نوعی ہے یعنی اعجاز کی ایک حد ہے اور وہ اعجاز کے تمام افراد کو منضبط ہے کہ بشر اس کا معارضہ کرنے سے اور اس کی مثال لانے سے عاجز ہے بخلاف محرفی الکلام کے کہ اس کی کوئی حد نہیں ہے۔ نہ یہ واحد نوعی ہے اور نہ یہ واحد شخصی ہے۔
In the book it is written that the highest level of eloquence and those close to the highest among the high ranks, but it is not impossible for humans to produce something similar, then both are miracles. Then the ways of i'jaz in speech also become numerous.
Answer to the first question: This is that we intend the second branch: that the way is more eloquent than all others, generally more eloquent than the existing actual ways or more eloquent than the estimated ways. But those ways are specific to human speech. The evidence is that i'jaz in speech means the speech of Allah. The purpose is that the i'jaz in the speech of Allah is that the speech of Allah is more eloquent than all the ways that can be expressed in other than Allah's speech, whether actual or estimated, to the extent that it is not possible for other than Allah to bring its like. Allah's ability to bring its like does not contradict the i'jaz of the speech of Allah.
Every prophet was given a miracle in his time in competition with that which was at its peak.
Second answer: Before understanding this, it is necessary to know a premise as an introduction. Premise: Every miracle given to a prophet was given in competition with that thing which had reached its peak and height. For example, in the era of Jesus (peace be upon him), medicine had reached its peak, so he was given the miracle of reviving the dead. In the era of Moses (peace be upon him), magic had reached its peak, so he was given the miracle of the staff. Similarly, in the era of the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him), eloquence and rhetoric had reached their peak, such that seven odes were hung on the threshold of the Kaaba and people were unable to compete, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) was given the miracle of the Qur'an, such that despite being eloquent and rhetorically gifted, people could not oppose it. Summary of the answer: Now the summary of the answer is that by 'ways other than' are meant the actual (existing) ways, because in estimated ways, the concept of being more eloquent in some way can only be imagined if the actual ways of that time have not reached their peak in eloquence, but this cannot happen; and if it were so, then it would be against the sunnah of Allah. In conclusion, the commentator's statement that for i'jaz in speech it is necessary to be more eloquent than the estimated ways is merely artificial.
Answer to the second question: There are two types of 'one' (wahid). (1) Universal one (al-wahid al-naw'i) like human. (2) Individual one (al-wahid al-shakhsi) like Zaid. Under universal one, there can be many individuals. So here by 'one' is meant universal one, i.e., i'jaz has one boundary and it encompasses all individuals of i'jaz, that humans are incapable of opposing it and bringing its like, contrary to distorters of speech (muharrifu al-kalam), which has no boundary. It is neither universal one nor individual one.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the Quran's miraculousness (i'jaz) and addresses two objections. The author first explains that the Quran's i'jaz lies in its being more eloquent than all actual and potential human speech. He then responds to an objection about whether this includes comparison to estimated ways, arguing that only actual ways matter because at the time of revelation eloquence was at its peak. The second objection concerns the definition of 'one' in i'jaz, distinguishing between universal and individual unity. The author concludes that i'jaz is a universal concept with a single boundary, encompassing all instances, unlike the distortions of speech which have no limit.

Key Terms
اعجاز (i'jaz): The miraculous nature of the Quran, its inimitability.
بلاغت (balaghah): Eloquence and rhetoric, the peak of which was achieved in the time of the Prophet.
واحد نوعی (wahid naw'i): Universal one, a category that encompasses many individuals.
واحد شخصی (wahid shakhsi): Individual one, a specific individual.
طرق محققہ (turuq muhahaqqah): Actual established ways of speech that exist.
طرق مقدرہ (turuq muqaddarah): Estimated or hypothetical ways of speech that could exist but do not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because estimated ways are infinite and cannot be compared.
B) Because at the time of revelation, eloquence had reached its peak in actual ways, so comparison with estimated ways is irrelevant.
C) Because the Quran was revealed in Arabic, and estimated ways are in other languages.
D) Because the miracle of the Quran is unique and cannot be compared.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculousness is proven by its surpassing the highest actual eloquence at the time of revelation, not by comparison to hypothetical possibilities.

Definition Types: Haqiqi and Ismi Definitions
Classifying definitions into haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal) based on mahiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions, identify the two types of essences (haqiqiyyah and i'tibariyyah), and apply the rule that non-existents can only have nominal definitions.

Core Idea
A definition is real if it captures an independent essence; nominal if it clarifies a conventional concept.

In usul al-fiqh, understanding how terms are defined is essential for precise legal reasoning. This passage from a classical commentary introduces a fundamental classification: definitions are either real (haqiqi) or nominal (ismi), depending on whether the essence (mahiyyah) has independent existence or is merely a conceptual construct. Learn how this distinction applies to key usul terms like 'asl, fiqh, jins, and naw'.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of definition
Identify the key criterion: a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) makes an independently existing essence mentally present; a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) clarifies what a name was coined for, using a more famous term or a detailed explanation.
The type depends on whether the mahiyyah is haqiqiyyah or i'tibariyyah.
2
Understand the two types of essence
A real essence (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah) has existence in itself regardless of intellectual consideration; if composite, its parts are interdependent. A conceptual essence (mahiyyah i'tibariyyah) exists only by intellectual consideration; its components are not necessarily interdependent.
3
Apply the distinction to examples
For each example given (asl, fiqh, jins, naw'), determine whether the term's essence is real or conceptual, and hence whether its definition is haqiqi or ismi. Note that 'asl' is a conventional term—its definition is ismi.
The passage also clarifies that conceptual entities are better called 'conceptual matters', not 'conceptual essences'.
4
State the rule for non-existents
Non-existent things (ma'dumat) have no realities, only concepts, so their definitions can only be nominal. Existing things can have both real and nominal definitions.
This rule is critical when dealing with legal concepts that refer to non-existent entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ) وَاعْلَمُ أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ إِمَّا حَقِيقِيٌّ ( الْمَاهِيَّةُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا تَحَقُّقُ وَثُبُوتٌ مَعَ قَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ اعْتِبَارِ الْعَقْلِ أَوْ لَا الْأُولَى الْمَاهِيَّةُ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ أَى الثَّابِتَةُ فِي نَفْسِ الْأَمْرِ وَلَا بُدَّ فِيهَا مِنْ احْتِيَاجِ بَعْضِ الْأَجْزَاء إِلَى الْبَعْضِ إِذَا كَانَتْ مُرَكَّبَةٌ وَالثَّانِيَةُ الْمَاهِيَّةُ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةُ أَى الْكَائِنَةُ بِحَسَبِ اعْتِبَارِ الْعَقْلِ كَمَا إِذَا اعْتَبَرَ الْوَاضِعُ عِدَّةَ أُمُورٍ فَوَضَعَ بِإِزَائِهَا اسْمًا مِنْ غَيْرِ احْتِيَاجِ الْأُمُورِ بَعْضِهَا إِلَى بَعْضٍ كَالْأَصْلِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاءِ الشَّيْء وَوَصْفِ ابْتِسَاءِ الْغَيْرِ عَلَيْهِ وَالْفِقْهِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاءِ الْمَسَائِلِ الْمَخْصُوصَةِ وَالْجِنسِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاء الْكُلِّيِّ الْمَقُولِ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالنَّوْعِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاء الْكُلِّيِّ الْمَقُولِ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ وَالتَّمْثِيلُ بِالْمُرَكَّبَةِ مِنْ عِدَّةٍ أُمُورٍ لَا يُنَافِي كَوْنَ بَعْضِ الْمَاهِيَّاتِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ بَسَائِطَ عَلَى أَنَّ الْحَقَّ أَنَّهَا إِنَّمَا يُقَالُ لَهَا الْأُمُورُ الْاعْتِبَارِيَّةُ لَا الْمَاهِيَّاتُ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةُ إِذَا تُمُهَدَ هَذَا فَتَقُولُ مَا يَتَعَقَّلُهُ الْوَاضِعُ لِيَضَعَ بِإِزَائِهِ اسْمًا إِمَّا أن يَكُونَ لَهُ مَاهِيَّةٌ حَقِيقِيَّةٌ أَوْ لَا وَعَلَى الْأَوَّلِ إِمَّا أَن يَكُونَ مُتَعَقَّلُهُ نَفْسَ حَقِيقَةِ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء أَوْ وُجُوهَا وَاعْتِبَارَاتٍ مِنْهُ فَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ لِمُسَمَّى وسمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا مَاهِيَّةٌ حَقِيقِيَّةٌ تَعْرِيفٌ حَقِيقِيٌّ يُفِيدُ تَصَرُّرَ الْمَاهِيَّةِ فِي الذَّهَنِ بالذَّاتِباتِ كُلِّهَا أَوْ بَعْضِهَا أَو بِالْعَرَضِيَّاتِ أَو بِالْمُرَكَّب مِنْهُمَا وَتَعْريفُ مَفهوم الاسْمِ وَمَا تَعَقَّلَهُ الْوَاضِعُ فَوَضَعَ الِاسْمَ بِإِزَائِهِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسْمِيٌّ يُفِيدُ تَبِينَ مَا وُضِعَ الاسمُ بِإِزَائِهِ بِلَفْظِ أَشْهَرَ كَقَوْلِنَا الْغَضَفَرُ الأسَدُ أَو بِلَفْظِ يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى تَفْصِيل ما دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ الاسْمُ إجْمَالًا كَقَوْلِنَا الْأَصْلُ مَا يُبْتَنَى عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَعْدُومَاتِ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا اسْمِيًّا ، إِذْ لَا حَقَائِقَ لَهَا ، بَلْ مَفْهُومَاتٌ وَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ قَدْ يَكُونُ اسْمِيًّا وَقَدْ يَكُونُ حَقِيقِيًّا ، إِذْ لَهَا مَفْهُومَاتٌ وَحَقَائِقُ .
ترجمہ: بہر حال ماہیت یا تو ان دونوں کیلئے تحقیق اور ثبوت ہو گا قطع نظر عقل کے اعتبار کرنے کے یا نہیں پہلی قسم ماہیت حقیقیہ ہے یعنی جو ثابت ہے نفس الامر میں اور ضروری ہے اس میں بعض اجزاء کا محتاج ہونا بعض کی طرف جب کہ ہو مرکبہ اور ثانی ماہیت اعتبار یہ ہے یعنی وہ جو ہونے والی ہے عقل کے اعتبار کرنے سے جیسا کہ جب اعتبار کر نے واضع چند امور کا پس وضع کرے انکے مقابلے میں ایک نام بغیر امور کے محتاج ہونے کے ان میں سے بعض کے بعض کی طرف جیسے اصل وہ ہے کہ جسکو وضع کیا گیا ہے کسی شئی کے مقابلے میں ابتناء الغخیر علیہ کی وصف کیسا تھے ، اور جیسے فقہ وہ کہ وضع کیا گیا ہے مسائل مخصوصہ کے مقابلہ میں اور جیسے جنس وہ کہ جسے وضع کیا گیا ہو اس کلی کے مقابلے میں جو معمول ہوتی ہے مختلف الحقائق کثیر افراد پر اور جیسے نوع وہ کہ جسے وضع کیا گیا ہو اس کلی کے مقابلے میں جو کلی محمول ہوتی ہے متفق الحقائق کثیر افراد پر ماہو کے جواب میں اور مثال بیان
His statement: 'And know that definition is either haqiqi (real).' The essence (mahiyyah) is either such that it has actuality and existence without considering the intellect, or not. The first is the real essence (al-mahiyyah al-haqiqiyyah), i.e., that which is established in itself. And it necessarily requires that some parts depend on others if it is composite. The second is the conceptual essence (al-mahiyyah al-i'tibariyyah), i.e., that which exists by virtue of intellectual consideration, as when the positer considers several matters and then coins a name for them without some matters depending on others. Examples: al-asl (the root) coined for a thing and the description of another's being built upon it; al-fiqh coined for specific issues; al-jins (genus) coined for the universal that is said of many things of different realities; al-naw' (species) coined for the universal that is said of many things of agreeing realities in answer to 'what is it?' And the example of a composite of several matters does not contradict that some conceptual essences are simple. The truth is that they are called conceptual matters, not conceptual essences. When this is established, you say: What the positer conceives in order to coin a name for it either has a real essence or not. In the first case, his conception is either the very reality of that thing or aspects and considerations of it. So the definition of a real essence for a named thing from the aspect that it is a real essence is a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) that brings to mind the essence in the intellect through its essential properties, all or some, or through accidents, or a combination. And the definition of the concept of the name and what the positer conceived when coining the name is a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) that clarifies what the name was coined for with a more famous word, like our saying 'al-ghadafar is the lion,' or with a word that details what the name indicates concisely, like our saying 'al-asl is that upon which something else is built.' Thus, the definition of non-existents can only be nominal, since they have no realities, only concepts. And the definition of existents can be nominal or real, since they have both concepts and realities.
Translation: In any case, the essence is either such that it has actuality and existence without considering the intellect, or not. The first is the real essence, i.e., that which is established in itself, and it necessarily requires some parts to depend on others if it is composite. The second is the conceptual essence, i.e., that which comes to be by intellectual consideration, as when the positer considers several matters and then coins a name for them without the matters depending on each other. For example, al-asl is that which is coined for a thing and the description of another's being built upon it; and like fiqh coined for specific issues; and like jins coined for the universal that is customarily said of many individuals of different realities; and like naw' coined for the universal that is a predicate agreeing in realities upon many individuals in answer to 'what is it' and example...
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the classification of definitions in usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating that definition (ta'rif) is either haqiqi (real) or ismi (nominal). The distinction is based on the nature of the essence (mahiyyah) being defined. A real essence (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah) has independent existence (in itself) and if composite, its parts are interdependent. A conceptual essence (mahiyyah i'tibariyyah) exists only by intellectual consideration; it is a collection of matters grouped under a name without intrinsic dependency. Examples given include: 'asl' (root) defined as the thing on which something else is built; 'fiqh' defined as a set of specific issues; 'jins' (genus) defined as a universal applicable to many different realities; 'naw'' (species) defined as a universal applicable to many agreeing realities in answer to 'what is it?'. The passage then refines: conceptual entities are better called 'conceptual matters' not 'conceptual essences'. If what the positer conceives has a real essence, the definition is either of the reality itself (real definition) or of its aspects (still nominal in some sense). A real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) makes the essence mentally present through essential attributes, accidents, or both. A nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) clarifies the name with a more famous expression or by detailing what the name indicates concisely. The key rule: non-existents (ma'dumat) can only have nominal definitions (no real essence), while existents can have both. This is a foundational lesson in usul al-fiqh regarding how terms are defined and understood, especially relevant for defining legal concepts like 'asl, fiqh, etc., in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta‘rīf ḥaqīqī): A definition that makes the real essence of a thing mentally present, using essential properties or accidents.
تعريف اسمي (ta‘rīf ismī): A definition that clarifies what a name was coined for, using a more famous word or a detailed explanation.
ماهية حقيقية (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah): An essence that has independent existence without intellectual consideration; if composite, parts are interdependent.
ماهية اعتبارية (māhiyyah i‘tibāriyyah): An essence that exists only by intellectual consideration; its components are not necessarily interdependent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can definitions of non-existents only be nominal?
A) Because they have no real essence, only concepts.
B) Because they are not subject to legal rulings.
C) Because they are only used in metaphorical language.
D) Because they require more explanation.

Key Takeaway
The classification of definitions into haqiqi and ismi depends on whether the essence being defined has independent existence or is a conventional concept, a critical distinction for precise usul analysis.

Reward for Abandoning Haram: A Hanafi Usul Distinction
Objection-answer: distinguishing reward for abandoning haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mere non-commission of a prohibited act (adam mubasharah) and active restraint (kaf al-nafs), and explain why only the latter earns reward in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mere non-commission of sin earns no reward; only active restraint against desire is rewarded as an obligatory act.

A classical objection claims that since abandoning the prohibited is wajib, it should bring reward. The Hanafi response reveals a critical distinction: 'abandoning haram' can mean either simply not doing it or actively restraining oneself. The Quranic verse (79:40-41) that promises Paradise to those who 'restrain the soul from desire' supports the active meaning. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications for how we understand reward and obligation.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Objection
Recognize why the objector argues that tark al-haram should be rewarded: because it is wajib, and wajib acts bring reward. The objector also cites the Quranic verse promising Paradise for those who abandon desire.
2
2. Locate the Quranic Dalil
Examine the verse (Surah al-Nazi'at 79:40-41). Identify the key phrase 'wa naha al-nafsa 'ani al-hawa' (and restrained the soul from desire). Note that the verb 'naha' implies an active effort, not mere absence.
3
3. Distinguish the Two Meanings of 'Tark al-Haram'
Understand that 'tark al-haram' can refer to: (a) mere non-commission (adam mubasharah) – the simple absence of the act, and (b) active restraint (kaf al-nafs) – the effortful prevention of oneself. The matn's claim of no reward applies only to the first meaning.
4
4. Derive the Ruling
Conclude that the wajib act that brings reward is the active restraint (kaf al-nafs). Mere non-commission is not rewarded because otherwise it would lead to absurd consequences (infinite reward even while engaged in another sin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاول انہ جعل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا اٹھارہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض پہلے احتمال ( یعنی مالہ سے مراد ثواب اور ماعلیہا سے مراد عقاب) میں ماتن نے ترک حرام کو ان چیزوں میں داخل کیا ہے جن پر نہ تو اب ہوتا ہے نہ عقاب اور یہ غلط ہے کیونکہ ترک حرام، ہمیں فعل واجب ہے اور فعل واجب پر ثواب ہوتا ہے لہذا ترک حرام پر بھی ثواب ہوتا ہے اور قرآن مجید میں بھی ارشاد ہے و اما من خاف مقام ربه ونہی النفس عن الہوئی فان الجنة ہی الماوئی یہاں جنت کی خوشخبری ترک ہوئی پر ہو رہی ہے تو ماتن کو چاہیے تھا کہ ترک حرام کو ان چیزوں میں داخل کرتے جن پر ثواب ہوتا ہے۔ جواب:۔ ثواب ترک حرام پر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فضل واجب پر ہوتا ہے وہ اس طرح کہ ترک حرام کے دو معنی ہیں ایک عدم مباشرة الحرام اور اس پر ثواب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر اس پر ثواب ہو تو پھر ہر لحظہ انسان کو ثواب ملنا چاہئیے بلکہ اگر وہ ایک حرام میں مشغول ہو تو دوسرے حرام کے نہ کرنے پر اس کو اس وقت بھی ثواب ملنا چاہئیے اور یہ میچ نہیں ہے اور دوسرا معنیٰ ہے کف النفس عن فعل
The first that he made: This is the eighteenth part of the commentary text. Purpose: to answer an objection. Objection in the first possibility (i.e., reward from 'ma laha' and punishment from 'ma alayha'): the matn included abandoning haram among things that have neither reward nor punishment, and this is wrong because abandoning haram is for us an obligatory act, and reward is for obligatory acts. Therefore, reward should be for abandoning haram. Moreover, the Quran says: 'But as for he who feared the standing of his Lord and prevented the soul from desire, then indeed Paradise is the refuge.' Here, Paradise is promised for abandoning desire, so the matn should have included abandoning haram among things that get reward. Answer: Reward is not for abandoning haram, but for the obligatory act of refraining. That is, abandoning haram has two meanings: one is mere non-commission of haram (adam mubasharat al-haram), and there is no reward for that, because if there were, a person would get reward every moment, even while engaged in one haram he would get reward for not committing another, which is not correct. The second meaning is restraining the soul from the act (kaf al-nafs an al-fi'l)...
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that the matn incorrectly places abandoning haram in the category of acts with no reward or punishment. The objector argues that abandoning haram is obligatory and thus should yield reward, citing a Quranic verse (Surah al-Nazi'at 79:40-41) that promises Paradise to those who restrain their souls from desire. The answer distinguishes two meanings of 'abandoning haram': (1) mere non-commission (adam mubasharah), which is not rewarded, as it would lead to infinite reward; (2) actively restraining oneself (kaf al-nafs), which is an obligatory act and thus rewarded. The matn refers to the first meaning. This is a standard Hanafi usul distinction: reward is for the act of restraint, not for mere absence of sin.

Key Terms
عدم مباشرة الحرام (adam mubasharat al-haram): Mere non-commission of a prohibited act, without any active restraint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no reward for mere non-commission of haram?
A) Because it is not an act of obedience
B) Because it would lead to infinite reward every moment
C) Because the Quran does not promise reward for it
D) Because it is not obligatory

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, reward for avoiding sin depends on actively restraining oneself (kaf al-nafs), not merely refraining from the act.

No Reward for Mere Avoidance of Haram
Explanation of why mere avoidance of haram yields no reward

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mere non-commission of a forbidden act (adam mubasharat al-haram) and restraining the soul (kaf al-nafs), and apply the Hanafi usul principle that reward is only for the latter.

Core Idea
Merely not doing a sin earns no reward; only restraining the soul despite temptation is an act of obedience rewarded.

An objection is raised: Tark al-haram is wajib, so it should be rewarded. Yet the matn of al-Tawdih lists it among acts with no reward or punishment. This lesson resolves the tension by uncovering two distinct meanings of 'avoidance of the forbidden'—and shows how the Quranic verse itself supports the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that tark al-haram is an obligatory act (wajib) and should be rewarded, citing the Quranic verse. Note the apparent contradiction with the matn.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Examine the verse (79:40-41). The key phrase is 'restrained his soul from desire'. This is the operative part for the analysis.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Analyze the key term 'tark al-haram'
The commentator splits it into two meanings: (1) mere non-commission ('adam mubasharat al-haram) and (2) restraining the soul (kaf al-nafs). Understand the difference.
Kaf al-nafs involves internal struggle against temptation.
4
Apply the first meaning to the matn's claim
Mere non-commission is not an act of the self; it is a passive absence. Therefore it cannot be wajib in the active sense and does not earn reward. This justifies the matn's inclusion.
If it were rewarded, even while sinning one would get reward for not committing other sins—an impossibility.
5
Apply the second meaning to the Quranic verse
The verse explicitly mentions 'nahi al-nafs' (restraining), which matches kaf al-nafs. Hence the reward is for active restraint, not passive avoidance.
The commentator affirms the verse supports his distinction.

الاول انه جعل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا اٹھارہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض پہلے احتمال ( یعنی مالہ سے مراد ثواب اور ماعلیہا سے مراد عقاب) میں ماتن نے ترک حرام کو ان چیزوں میں داخل کیا ہے جن پر نہ ثواب ہوتا ہے نہ عقاب اور یہ غلط ہے کیونکہ ترک حرام، ہمیں فعل واجب ہے اور فعل واجب پر ثواب ہوتا ہے لہذا ترک حرام پر بھی ثواب ہوتا ہے اور قرآن مجید میں بھی ارشاد ہے و اما من خاف مقام ربه ونہی النفس عن الہوئی فان الجنة ہی الماوئی یہاں جنت کی خوشخبری ترک ہوئی پر ہو رہی ہے تو ماتن کو چاہیے تھا کہ ترک حرام کو ان چیزوں میں داخل کرتے جن پر ثواب ہوتا ہے۔ جواب:۔ ثواب ترک حرام پر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فضل واجب پر ہوتا ہے وہ اس طرح کہ ترک حرام کے دو معنی ہیں ایک عدم مباشرة الحرام اور اس پر ثواب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر اس پر ثواب ہو تو پھر ہر لحظہ انسان کو ثواب ملنا چاہئیے بلکہ اگر وہ ایک حرام میں مشغول ہو تو دوسرے حرام کے نہ کرنے پر اس کو اس وقت بھی ثواب ملنا چاہئیے اور یہ محال ہے اور دوسرا معنیٰ ہے کف النفس عن فعل الحرام یعنی گناہ کے اسباب پائے جائیں پھر بھی اپنے آپ کو روک لے اور اس پر ثواب ملتا ہے اب جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ جس ترک حرام کو واجب بنا کر کہہ رہے ہیں کہ اس پر ثواب ملتا ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جب کف النفس ہو کیونکہ کف النفس واقعی واجب ہی ہے لیکن جو مائن نے ترک حرام کو ، ، الا ثاب علیہ ولا یقاب میں داخل کیا ہے وہ اس کے پہلے معنی یعنی عدم مباشرة الحرام کے اعتبار سے ہے اور عدم مباشرة الحرام پر ثواب نہیں ملتا لہذا ماتن کی بات بھی درست ہے اس طرح آیت کریمہ میں بھی ثواب کی بشارت کف النفس پر ہے کیونکہ کہ آیت میں ہے نہی النفس عن الہوئی اور نہی النفس ( نفس کو منع کرنا ) بعینہ کف النفس ہے اور یہ ہم بھی مانتے ہیں لہذا ماتن کی بات بالکل درست ہے۔
The first: he made (that is) this is the eighteenth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to answer an objection. The objection: in the first probability (i.e., mal-hu means reward and ma-alayha means punishment) the author (matn) included avoidance of the forbidden (tark al-haram) among those things for which there is neither reward nor punishment, and this is wrong because avoidance of the forbidden, according to us, is an obligatory act (wajib), and for an obligatory act there is reward, therefore for avoidance of the forbidden there is also reward. And in the Noble Quran there is also the verse: 'But as for him who feared the station of his Lord and restrained his soul from desire, indeed Paradise will be the refuge.' Here glad tidings of Paradise are given for avoidance of desire. So the author should have included avoidance of the forbidden among those things for which there is reward. The answer: Reward is not for avoidance of the forbidden; rather it is for performing an obligatory act (fard wajib) in this way: avoidance of the forbidden has two meanings. One is non-commission of the forbidden ('adam mubasharat al-haram), and for this there is no reward, because if there were reward for it, then at every moment a person should receive reward; rather, if he is engaged in one forbidden act, then for not doing another forbidden act he should also receive reward at that time, and this is impossible. And the second meaning is restraining the soul from the forbidden act (kaf al-nafs 'an fi'l al-haram), i.e., the means of sin exist yet he still holds himself back, and for this there is reward. Now the answer is: The avoidance of the forbidden which you consider obligatory and say that reward is for it—this is when it is kaf al-nafs, because kaf al-nafs is truly obligatory. But what the author (matn) included in 'no reward on it and no punishment' is according to its first meaning, i.e., non-commission of the forbidden, and for non-commission of the forbidden there is no reward. Therefore the author's statement is correct. Similarly, in the noble verse the glad tidings of reward are for kaf al-nafs, because the verse says 'and he restrained his soul from desire' (nahi al-nafs 'an al-hawa), and nahi al-nafs (restraining the soul) is exactly kaf al-nafs, and we also accept this. Therefore the author's statement is absolutely correct.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection against the author (matn) of Al-Tawdih. The objection claims that avoiding the forbidden (tark al-haram) is an obligatory act (wajib) and thus deserves reward, and the Quranic verse supports this. The commentator (sadr al-shariah) resolves this by distinguishing two meanings of tark al-haram: (1) mere non-commission without internal struggle, which is not rewarded, and (2) restraining one's soul (kaf al-nafs) in the presence of temptation, which is obligatory and rewarded. The Quranic verse praises the latter. Hence the author's inclusion of tark al-haram among things with neither reward nor punishment refers to the first meaning, so the objection is invalid. The commentator uses both rational argument (if mere non-commission were rewarded, then even while sinning one would be rewarded for not committing other sins) and textual proof (the Quranic verse applies to kaf al-nafs).

Key Terms
ترک حرام (tark al-haram): Avoidance of the forbidden; here split into two meanings: mere non-commission and restraining the soul.
عدم مباشرة الحرام ('adam mubasharat al-haram): Non-commission of the forbidden act without internal struggle; not an act of obedience and thus not rewarded.
کف النفس (kaf al-nafs): Restraining the soul from sin despite temptation; a wajib act that earns reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between 'adam mubasharat al-haram and kaf al-nafs?
A) They are the same.
B) 'Adam mubasharat al-haram is rewarded, kaf al-nafs is not.
C) 'Adam mubasharat al-haram is just not doing the act, while kaf al-nafs involves internal struggle and is rewarded.
D) Kaf al-nafs is a sin.

Key Takeaway
Reward is not for passive avoidance of sin but for active restraint of the soul in the face of temptation.

Ibn al-Hajib's Objection on Daruri Knowledge and Redundancy of Istidlal
Dispute over redundancy of istidlal in fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate Ibn al-Hajib's objection that the condition of istidlal is not redundant in the definition of fiqh and explain why the Hanafi position supports its inclusion to exclude daruri knowledge.

Core Idea
The condition of istidlal is not redundant; it excludes daruri knowledge, which is not considered fiqh.

This passage presents a critical discussion in Hanafi usul al-fiqh about the proper definition of fiqh. Ibn al-Hajib argues that the condition of istidlal (deduction) must be added to exclude knowledge obtained by necessity (daruri), such as the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet. The matn author mistakenly thought it was redundant because he believed the condition of tafsiliyya already excluded all non-fiqh knowledge. Understanding this dispute sharpens our grasp of how Hanafi usul defines fiqh precisely and why each condition serves a distinct purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge from evidence
The passage distinguishes between daruri (necessary) knowledge obtained without reflection and nazari (theoretical) knowledge obtained through istidlal. Recognize that daruri knowledge includes that of prophets and angels, while nazari knowledge is the result of the mujtahid's ijtihad.
This distinction is crucial to understanding Ibn al-Hajib's objection.
2
Understand Ibn al-Hajib's objection
Ibn al-Hajib argues that because daruri knowledge is not considered fiqh terminologically, a separate condition of istidlal or istinbat must be added to exclude it. He rejects the matn author's assumption that tafsiliyya suffices.
The matn author thought tafsiliyya excludes the muqallid, not daruri knowledge.
3
Analyze the matn author's misconception
The matn author believed that 'min adillatiha al-tafsiliyya' excludes both the muqallid and daruri knowledge, so adding istidlal is repetitive. The commentary shows this is incorrect: tafsiliyya excludes only those who do not have detailed evidence (like the muqallid), not those who have knowledge by necessity.
The muqallid knows rulings but not the detailed evidence; daruri knowledge includes both ruling and evidence without reflection.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Even if one argues that 'husool al-ilm min al-daleel' already implies istidlal, the commentator responds that Ibn al-Hajib's addition is for clarification (bayan), to remove misunderstanding, or for explicit statement, not as a necessary condition. Such explicative additions are common in definitions.
The addition is not redundant if it serves a clarifying purpose.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If istidlal were omitted, daruri knowledge would be included in the definition of fiqh, which is not intended. The practical consequence is a more precise definition that excludes prophetic and angelic knowledge.
This shows that even small definitional changes have significant conceptual effects.

ترجمہ:۔ چلے گئے ابن حاجب اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک احکام عن الادلہ کے علم کا حصول کبھی ہوتا ہے بطریق ضرورت جیسے جبریل علیہ السلام اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا علم اور کبھی ہوتا ہے بطریق استدلال اور استنباط کے جیسے مجتہد کا علم اور اول کا نہیں نام رکھا جا تا فقہ اصطلاحی پس نہیں ہے کوئی چارہ (سوائے ) استدلال و استنباط کی قید کی زیادتی کے ساتھ احتراز کرتے ہوئے اس سے اور مصنف نے وہم کیا ہے کہ بیشک وہ احتراز ہے مقلد کے علم سے پس یقین کیا اس نے اس بات کا کہ وہ مکرر ہے بوجہ خارج ہونے اس سے فول من ادلتها اتفصیلیہ سے پس اگر کہا جائے علم کا حصول دلیل سے مشیر ہے استدلال کی طرف اس لئے کہ نہیں ہے کوئی معنی اس کا مگر یہ کہ ہو علم ماخوذ دلیل سے پس خارج ہو جائے گا جبریل علیہ السلام اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا علم بھی ہم نے کہا اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو استدلال ذکر کیا اس (ابن حاجب) نے تصریح ما علم التزاما کے لئے ہے یا دفع وہم کے لئے یا بیان کے لئے ہوگا احتراز کے علاوہ اور اس کی مشن شائع ہے تعریفات میں ۔
استدلال از شاریخ کہ استدلال کی قید میں تکرار نہیں
تشریح : قوله ولا شک انہ مکررز یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ ماتن پر اعتراض کر رہے ہیں لیکن اس سے پہلے بطور تمہید ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں ۔
مقدمہ:۔ احکام کا جو علم دلیل سے حاصل ہو اس علم کی دو قسمیں ہیں نظری اور ضروری نظری یہ ہے کہ ان احکام کا علم ان کے ادلہ سے غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد حاصل ہوا ہو یعنی استدلال کے ذریعہ اور ضروری یہ ہے کہ ان احکام کا علم بمع ادلہ حاصل ہوا ہو یعنی احکام کا علم بھی حاصل ہو اور ان کے ادلہ کا علم بھی حاصل ہو لیکن ان ادلہ میں غور کرنے کی ضرورت نہ پڑی ہو یعنی اگر ادلہ میں غور وفکر کرنے کے بغیر اولہ کا علم بھی حاصل ہو اور احکام کا علم بھی حاصل ہو جائے تو یہ علم ضروری ہے جیسے حضرت جبریل علیہ
His statement: 'And there is no doubt that it is repetitive. Ibn al-Hajib held that the obtaining of knowledge of rulings from the evidence may be by way of necessity, like the knowledge of Jibril and the Messenger (peace be upon them), and may be by way of deduction (istidlal) or extraction (istinbat), like the knowledge of the mujtahid. The first is not called fiqh terminologically, so there must be an addition of the condition of deduction or extraction as a precaution against it. The author (al-musannif) imagined that it is a precaution against the knowledge of the muqallid, so he asserted that it is repetitive because it is excluded by his statement: 'from its detailed evidence.' For if it is said: 'Obtaining knowledge from the evidence implies deduction, because it has no meaning except that knowledge is taken from the evidence, so the knowledge of Jibril and the Messenger (peace be upon them) would also be excluded.' We say: Even if conceded, he mentioned deduction for explicit statement of what is known implicitly, or to remove misunderstanding, or for clarification, not as a precaution. And similar instances are common in definitions.'
Translation: Ibn al-Hajib inclined to the view that the obtaining of knowledge of rulings from evidence sometimes occurs by way of necessity, like the knowledge of Jibril and the Messenger (peace be upon them), and sometimes by way of deduction (istidlal) and extraction (istinbat), like the knowledge of the mujtahid. The first is not called fiqh terminologically, so there is no alternative but to add the condition of deduction or extraction as a precaution against it. And the author (al-musannif) mistakenly thought that it is a precaution against the knowledge of the muqallid, so he was certain that it is repetitive because it is excluded by his statement: 'from its detailed evidence.' Then if it is said: 'Obtaining knowledge from the evidence indicates deduction, because it has no meaning except that knowledge is taken from the evidence, so the knowledge of Jibril and the Messenger (peace be upon them) would also be excluded.' We say: Even if conceded, he mentioned deduction for explicit statement of what is known implicitly, or to remove misunderstanding, or for clarification, not as a precaution. And such instances are common in definitions.
Deduction from the commentator that the condition of deduction is not repetitive.
Commentary: His statement 'and there is no doubt that it is repetitive' is the first part of the commentary's expression. From here, the commentator is objecting to the author (matn). But before that, as a preface, understand a premise. Premise: The knowledge of rulings that is obtained from the evidence is of two types: theoretical (nazari) and necessary (daruri). Theoretical is that the knowledge of these rulings is obtained after reflection and pondering over their evidence, i.e., through deduction. And necessary is that the knowledge of these rulings is obtained with the evidence, i.e., both the knowledge of the rulings and the knowledge of their evidence are obtained, but there is no need for reflection in those evidence; meaning if without reflection in the evidence, both the knowledge of the evidence and the knowledge of the rulings are obtained, then this knowledge is necessary, like the knowledge of Jibril (peace be upon him)...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) in usul al-fiqh regarding the definition of fiqh. Ibn al-Hajib argues that the condition of 'istidlal' (deduction) or 'istinbat' (extraction) must be added to the definition to exclude knowledge obtained by necessity (daruri), such as the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet (peace be upon them). They knew rulings and their evidence simultaneously without reflection. The author of the matn (possibly al-Tawdih) mistakenly thought that the condition of 'tafsiliyya' already excludes the muqallid, so he considered 'istidlal' redundant. The commentary (sharh) refutes this by explaining that 'tafsiliyya' excludes total evidence, not daruri knowledge. Even if one argues that 'husool al-ilm min al-daleel' implies deduction, the commentator responds that Ibn al-Hajib's addition of 'istidlal' is for clarification (bayan) or to remove misunderstanding, not as a necessary precaution, and such additions are common in definitions. The passage then provides a premise distinguishing theoretical knowledge (nazari, requiring reflection) from necessary knowledge (daruri, obtained without reflection), giving the example of Jibril's knowledge.

Key Terms
استدلال (istidlal): Deduction or reasoning from evidence to derive a ruling through reflection.
ضروری (daruri): Knowledge that is obtained necessarily without need for reflection or deduction, e.g., prophets' knowledge through revelation.
مکرر (mukarrar): Redundant or repetitive, referring to a condition that is already implied by another condition in the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn al-Hajib insist on adding the condition of 'istidlal' to the definition of fiqh?
A) To exclude the knowledge of the muqallid.
B) To exclude knowledge obtained by necessity, such as that of Jibril and the Prophet.
C) To include the knowledge of the mujtahid.
D) To make the definition longer.

Key Takeaway
The condition of istidlal is not redundant but clarifies that fiqh requires knowledge obtained through reflection, excluding daruri knowledge.

Defining Khitab and the Kalam Nafsi Objection
Defining khitab and addressing the kalam nafsi objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lexical and alternative definitions of khitab and explain how the inclusion of kalam nafsi is justified.

Core Idea
Khitab is not limited to verbal speech—mental speech can be considered address under alternative definitions.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary defines khitab and addresses a key objection: if khitab means directing speech to another for understanding, how can Allah's eternal mental speech (kalam nafsi) be considered khitab? The response shows that scholars who include kalam nafsi adopt alternative definitions of khitab that do not require external direction. This illustrates the flexibility of usul definitions and the importance of premises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions of khitab
The passage gives two definitions: lexical (tawjih al-kalam ila al-ghayr li al-ifham) and customary (ma yaga'u bihi al-takhatub). Note that the lexical definition involves direction and intention to make understand.
The customary definition is more general, simply 'that by which address occurs.'
2
Distinguish kalam nafsi and kalam lafzi
Recognize that kalam nafsi is internal mental speech, while kalam lafzi is uttered speech. This distinction is crucial for the objection.
In Hanafi theology, Allah's speech is an eternal attribute (kalam nafsi), and His revealed words are its expression.
3
Understand the objection
The objection states that the lexical definition of khitab cannot apply to kalam nafsi because mental speech is not 'directed' to another; it is internal. Therefore, including kalam nafsi in khitab Allah seems contradictory.
The objector assumes the lexical definition is the only valid one.
4
Analyze the response
The response is that those who include kalam nafsi do not use the lexical definition. Instead, they adopt alternative definitions: 'speech prepared for conveying understanding' or 'speech intended to inform a ready recipient.' Both can apply to mental speech because one can intend to convey meaning even before uttering.
These definitions shift focus from external direction to intention and readiness.
5
Reflect on the significance
This dispute shows that defining core terms in usul al-fiqh is not merely lexical; it often involves theological commitments. The flexibility in definition allows coherence between Allah's eternal speech and His revealed address.
This is an example of how usul definitions are shaped by broader doctrinal stances.

والخطاب فی اللغۃ تو جیعہ : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس میں شاریخ نے خطاب کی تعریف کی ہے ایک لغوی تعریف کی ہے اور ایک عرفی معنی بیان کیا ہے۔
خطاب کی لغوی تعریف : یہ ہے تو یہ الکلام تو خیر الافہام کلام کوغیر کی طرف سمجھانے کے لئے متوجہ کرتا۔
عرفی معنی : ما يقع به التخاطب وہ کئی جس کے ساتھ تخاطب واقع ہوتا ہے۔
و هو هنا الکلام انفسی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے سوال کو بجھنے سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں ۔
مقدمہ: کلام کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) کلام نفسی (۲) کلام لفظی کلام نفسی وہ امور ہیں جو آدمی کے ذہن میں ہوتے ہیں اور ان کو پھر الفاظ میں تبدیل کیا جاتا ہے بالفاظ دیگر آدمی کے ذہن میں جو باتیں ہوتی ہیں ان کے تلفظ سے پہلے پہلے وہ کلام نفسی ہیں اور کلام لفظی وہ باتیں ہیں جن کو آدمی اپنے منہ سے نکالتا ہے اب اس کے بعد بعض حضرات تو خطاب اللہ کا اطلاق کلام نفسی اور از لی دونوں پر کرتے ہیں اور بعض حضرات اس کا اطلاق کلام لفظی پر کرتے ہیں کلام نفسی پر نہیں کرتے۔
وھوھنا: سے بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ جو حضرات خطاب اللہ سے صرف کلام لفظی مراد لیتے ہیں ان پر تو کوئی اشکال نہیں لیکن جو حضرات خطاب اللہ سے کلام لفظی نفسی دونوں مراد لیتے ہیں ان پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ خطاب کی تعریف یہ ہے کلام کو غیر کی طرف سمجھانے کی خاطر متوجہ کرنا ، اور یہ معنی کلام لفظی میں تو پایا جاتا ہے کلام نفس میں نہیں پایا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اس کو غیر کی طرف متوجہ نہیں کیا جاتا تو آپ نے کلام نفسی کو خطاب اللہ میں کیسے داخل کر دیا۔
جواب: ومن ذهب الى ان الج سے جواب ہے کہ جو حضرات خطاب اللہ کا اطلاق کلام نفسی ولفظی دونوں پر کرتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک خطاب کی تعریف وہ نہیں ہے جو تاریخ نے بیان فرمائی ہے یعنی توجیہ الکلام نحو الغير لا افہام ، بلکہ ان کے نزدیک خطاب کی دو تعریفیں اور ہیں (۱) الکلام الموجہ لا فہام ، ، وہ کلام جو کسی کو سمجھانے کے لئے تیار کی گئی ہو وہ خطاب ہے اور یہ معنی کلام نفسی پر بھی صادق آتا ہے (۲) الکلام المقصود منہ افہام من ہو تہی الہمہ ، وہ کلام جس سے مقصود اس شخص کو سمجھانا ہو جو اس کے سمجھنے کے لئے تیار ہو اور یہ معنی بھی کلام نفسی پر صادق آتا ہے۔
And al-khitab lexically: This is the third part of the commentary text. In it, the commentator defines khitab: one lexical definition and one customary meaning. Lexical definition of khitab: It is 'tawjih al-kalam ila al-ghayr li al-ifham' — directing speech towards another for understanding. Customary meaning: ma yaga'u bihi al-takhatub — that by which address occurs. 'And it is here al-kalam al-nafsi': This is the fourth part. Purpose: to answer a hypothetical question. First a premise: Speech is of two types: (1) kalam nafsi (mental speech), (2) kalam lafzi (verbal speech). Kalam nafsi are the matters that exist in one's mind, later converted into words; kalam lafzi is what one utters. Some apply 'khitab Allah' to both kalam nafsi and lafzi, others only to lafzi. 'And here': He says that those who take khitab Allah as only verbal speech face no objection, but those who include mental speech object: the definition of khitab is directing speech towards another for understanding, which applies to verbal speech but not mental speech because it is not directed towards another. So how did you include mental speech? Response: Those who apply khitab Allah to both mental and verbal speech do not accept the definition given by the historian (i.e., 'tawjih al-kalam...'). Rather, they have two definitions: (1) al-kalam al-muwajjah li al-ifham — speech prepared for someone's understanding, which applies to mental speech as well; (2) al-kalam al-maqsud minhu ifham man huwa mutahayyi' lahu — speech intended to inform someone who is prepared to understand it, which also applies to mental speech.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage explains the definition of khitab. The commentator first gives the lexical and customary definitions. Lexically, khitab is 'directing speech towards another for understanding'. Customarily, it is 'that by which address occurs'. Then an objection is raised: Some scholars include both mental speech (kalam nafsi) and verbal speech (kalam lafzi) in the concept of khitab Allah, but the lexical definition seems only to fit verbal speech because mental speech is not 'directed' externally. The response shows that those who include mental speech do not use the lexical definition; they define khitab differently: either as 'speech prepared for conveying understanding' (which mental speech can be) or as 'speech intended to inform a ready recipient' (which also applies to internal speech). This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Key Terms
خطاب (khitab): Speech directed to another for understanding; includes both verbal and mental speech according to some scholars
کلام نفسی (kalam nafsi): Mental speech, i.e., thoughts and meanings in the mind before being expressed in words

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to those who include kalam nafsi in khitab Allah, which definition of khitab do they adopt?
A) The lexical definition: tawjih al-kalam ila al-ghayr li al-ifham.
B) The definition: al-kalam al-muwajjah li al-ifham or al-kalam al-maqsud minhu ifham man huwa mutahayyi' lahu.
C) The customary definition: ma yaga'u bihi al-takhatub.
D) They do not define it at all.

Key Takeaway
The definition of khitab is not fixed; it can be interpreted to include mental speech (kalam nafsi) by focusing on intention and preparation rather than external direction.

Sunnah and Ijma as Independent Sources: Refuting the Kashif Claim
Critical refinement rejecting the kashif-only claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why sunnah and ijma are not merely kashif (revealers) for the Quran but can independently establish (muthbit) rulings, and identify the logical flaw in the contrasting claim.

Core Idea
Sunnah and ijma establish rulings not in the Quran's wording; they are not merely revealers.

In this passage, the author critiques the commentator's (sharih's) assertion that sunnah and ijma are only kashif (revealers) for the Book of Allah, not muthbit (establishing rulings). By analyzing two possible interpretations of 'kashif,' the author demonstrates that the claim is self-defeating: if it means revealing internal speech, it duplicates the Quran's role; if it means revealing verbal speech, it fails to account for rulings proven solely by sunnah or ijma. This refines our usul understanding of the epistemic weight of secondary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sharih's claim
The sharih argued that sunnah and ijma are only mazhir/kashif (manifesters/revealers) for Quranic rulings, not muthbit (establishing). The author objects that this is incorrect.
This is a critical refinement (tarded) within the Hanafi usul tradition.
2
Analyze the two possible meanings of 'kashif for the Book of Allah'
The author bifurcates: (a) revealing the internal divine speech (kalam nafsi), or (b) revealing the verbal speech (kalam lafzi). Both are tested.
This taqsim (division) is a standard rational argument technique.
3
Refute the first possibility (kalam nafsi)
If sunnah/ijma reveal internal speech, the Quran does the same, so singling them out is arbitrary. They would be redundant.
The Quran itself is also kashif for kalam nafsi, so no special role.
4
Refute the second possibility (kalam lafzi)
If they reveal only verbal speech, then many rulings established by sunnah/ijma—but not found in the Quran's wording—would have no basis. Hence, in those cases, sunnah/ijma are muthbit, not kashif.
Example: the prohibition of marrying a woman and her paternal aunt simultaneously is from sunnah, not the Quran.
5
Conclude the refutation
Both possibilities are invalid, so the sharih's claim is unfounded. Sunnah and ijma, like the Quran, are directly part of divine address, unlike qiyas which only reveals the illah.
This preserves the comprehensive definition of fiqh as knowledge of divine rulings from detailed evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تردید :- شاریخ کا ماتن پر یہ اعتراض کرنا اور پھر جواب دینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ شاریح نے جواب میں یہ کہا کہ سنت اور اجماع احکام کے لئے مظہر اور کاشف ہیں اور مثبت نہیں ہیں اور یہ بات درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر سنت اور اجماع کتاب اللہ کے لئے کاشف ہوں (یعنی ان سے صرف یہ وضاحت ہو کہ فلاں حکم میں خطاب اللہ وارد ہے ) تو یہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ اس خطاب اللہ کے لئے کاشف ہیں جو اللہ کی صفت ہے یعنی کلام نفسی جو اصل ہے اور یا اس خطاب اللہ کے لئے کاشف ہیں جو الفاظ کی صورت میں موجود ہیں یعنی کلام لفظی اور یہ دونوں احتمال باطل ہیں اول اس لئے باطل ہے کہ کلام نفسی کیلئے جس طرح سنت و اجماع کاشف و مبین ہیں اسی طرح قرآن (یعنی جس کا ہم تلفظ کرتے ہیں ) بھی کلامِ ازلی کیلئے کاشف ہے تو پھر سنت و اجماع کی تخصیص کا کیا معنی؟ اور ثانی اس لئے باطل ہے کہ کئی احکام ایسے ہیں جو اس کلام لفظی میں نہیں لیکن سنت یا اجماع سے ثابت ہیں تو ان احکام میں سنت یا اجماع مثبت ہوئے نہ کہ کاشف و موضح ۔ لہذا یہ احتمال بھی باطل ہوا جب دونوں احتمال باطل ہوئے تو شاریح کا یہ اعتراض ہی وارد نہیں ہوتا کہ جواب دینے کی ضرورت پڑے۔ کیونکہ قرآن کی طرح سنت اور اجماع بھی کلام ازلی کیلئے کاشف و موضح ہیں اس لئے جس طرح قرآن خطاب میں داخل ہے یہ بھی خطاب میں داخل ہونگے بخلاف قیاس کے کہ وہ قرآن و حدیث میں پائی جانے والی علت کیلئے کاشف ہوتا ہے کلام ازلی کیلئے کاشف و مبین نہیں ہوتا۔
Refutation: The commentator's objection to the matn and then his answer is not correct, because the commentator said in the answer that sunnah and ijma are revealers and discoverers for rulings and not establishers, and this statement is not correct. Because if sunnah and ijma are kashif for the Book of Allah (i.e., they only clarify that the address of Allah has occurred concerning a ruling), then there are two possibilities: either they are kashif for the address of Allah which is His attribute, i.e., the internal speech (kalam nafsi) which is the origin, or they are kashif for the address of Allah which exists in the form of words, i.e., the verbal speech (kalam lafzi). Both possibilities are invalid. The first is invalid because just as sunnah and ijma are kashif and mubin for the internal speech, similarly the Quran (which we recite) is also a kashif for the eternal speech. So what is the meaning of specifying sunnah and ijma? The second is invalid because there are many rulings that are not found in this verbal speech but are established by sunnah or ijma. In those rulings, sunnah or ijma are establishers, not discoverers and clarifiers. So this possibility is also invalid. When both possibilities are invalid, the commentator's objection does not even arise such that a response is needed. Because, like the Quran, sunnah and ijma are also kashif and mubin for the eternal speech; therefore, just as the Quran is included in the divine address, these are also included in the address, unlike qiyas, which is a kashif for the effective cause found in the Quran and hadith, not a kashif and mubin for the eternal speech.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (tarded) by the author of this book, rejecting the sharih's (commentator's) response. The sharih had claimed that sunnah and ijma, like qiyas, are only mazhir/kashif for Quranic rulings and not muthbit. The author refutes this by analyzing the possible meanings of 'kashif for the Book of Allah'. If sunnah and ijma are kashif for the internal divine speech (kalam nafsi), then the Quran itself is also kashif for that, so singling out sunnah and ijma is arbitrary. If they are kashif for the verbal speech (kalam lafzi), then there exist rulings established by sunnah or ijma that are not present in the Quran's wording, meaning they actually establish rulings (muthbit) in those cases. Therefore, the sharih's objection was unnecessary because sunnah and ijma, like the Quran, are directly part of divine address, unlike qiyas which only reveals the effective cause. This distinction preserves the comprehensive definition of fiqh.

Key Terms
کلام نفسی (kalam nafsi): Internal speech of Allah, an attribute of His essence, eternal and not composed of letters or sounds.
کلام لفظی (kalam lafzi): Verbal speech, the words of the Qur'an revealed in Arabic letters and sounds.
علت (illah): Effective cause or reason underlying a legal ruling, used in qiyas to extend rulings.
کاشف (kashif): Revealer or discoverer; a source that only manifests a ruling already established in another source.
مثبت (muthbit): Establisher; a source that independently brings a ruling into existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tarded, why is the sharih's response that sunnah and ijma are only kashif for the Book of Allah invalid?
A) Because sunnah and ijma are never independent sources
B) Because there are rulings established by sunnah/ijma not found in the Quran's verbal speech
C) Because qiyas is the only source that is mazhir
D) Because the Quran is the only kashif for divine speech

Key Takeaway
Sunnah and ijma are independent sources that can establish rulings not explicitly in the Quran, refuting the idea that they are merely kashif.
