Qat'i and Zanni in Ijma and Nass: Hanafi Response to Objection
Responding to the objection that rulings from zanni proof cannot be qat'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi doctrine that text (nass) and consensus (ijma) are inherently qat'i and apply this principle to evaluate whether a ruling from a zanni proof can be considered certain.

Core Idea
Text and ijma are qat'i by essence; external factors affect application, not the source itself.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a crucial objection: if consensus can be proven by a single report (khabar wahid), how can any ruling based on such consensus be definitive (qat'i)? This objection challenges the very foundation of legal certainty in fiqh. The Hanafi response, as explained here, draws a sharp distinction between the intrinsic certainty of the source (nass or ijma) and the circumstantial impediments that may cloud its application. Understanding this distinction is key to appreciating how Hanafi usul categorizes knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the objector's claim? They argue that if the proof of ijma is not definitive, the ruling cannot be definitive.
2
Analyze the Hanafi agreement
The commentator agrees with the logical connection between proof and ruling, but then refines the concept of 'proof'.
3
Focus on the essence of the source
The commentator asserts that text and ijma are mufid lil-qat' in themselves, disregarding external impediments.
This is the core of the response.
4
Distinguish intrinsic vs. extrinsic
The source is qat'i in essence, but the transmission (isnad) may be zanni. The ruling's qat'iyya is about the source, not the transmission.
5
Apply to the dispute
Conclude that in the Hanafi school, rulings from ijma (and nass) are considered part of 'ilm even if transmitted via ahad reports, because the source itself is certain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب تک اجماع کا ثبوت قطعی نہ ہو یعنی اجماع خبر متواتر یاخبر مشہور سے ثابت ہو چنانچہ اگر کسی ایک آدمی نے اجماع کی خبر دے دی تو ثبوت قطعی نہیں ہو گا جب ثبوت قطعی نہیں ہوگا تو حکم بھی قطعی نہیں ہوگا۔ جواب :۔ دیا کہ آپ کی بات درست ہے کہ قطعی حکم اس وقت ہو گا جب ثبوت قطعی ہو ہماری مراد بھی یہی ہے کیونکہ نص اور اجتماع یقین کا فائدہ دیتے ہیں الا یہ کہ کوئی عارض پایا جائے تو پھر یہ قطعیت کا فائدہ نہیں دیتے لیکن ہماری بحث اس میں چل رہی ہے کہ نص اور اجماع قطع نظر عوارض کے یہ مفید للقطع ہیں لہذا جب ذات کے اعتبار سے مفید للقطع ہیں تو فقہ میں داخل رہیں گے فقہ سے خارج نہیں ہونگے۔
When the proof of consensus is not definitive, meaning consensus is proven by mutawatir or mashhur report; if a single person reports consensus, the proof is not definitive, and when the proof is not definitive, the ruling is also not definitive. Response: He said, 'Your statement is correct that a definitive ruling occurs when the proof is definitive. This is also our intention because text and consensus yield certainty unless an impediment occurs, then they do not yield certainty. But our discussion is that text and consensus, disregarding impediments, are productive of certainty. Therefore, when they are productive of certainty by their essence, they will remain within fiqh and will not be excluded from fiqh.'
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding the definitive nature (qat'iyya) of rulings derived from consensus (ijma) and text (nass). The objector argued that since consensus can be proven by a single report (khabar wahid), its proof is not definitive, so rulings based on such consensus cannot be definitive. The commentator (sharih) responds by agreeing that a ruling is definitive only when its proof is definitive. However, he clarifies that the discussion in the text assumes that text and consensus are inherently productive of certainty (mufid lil-qat'), barring any external impediments. Therefore, when considered in themselves, they are definitive and thus remain within the domain of fiqh. This is a classic Hanafi usul principle: the source itself (text or consensus) is qat'i in essence, but its application may be affected by external factors.

Key Terms
قطعي (qat'i): Definitive, certain, not subject to probability
ظني (zanni): Probabilistic, subject to doubt
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah after the Prophet's death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition does the commentator mention for a ruling to be considered qat'i?
A) The ruling must be based on mutawatir hadith only.
B) The proof must be definitive (qat'i) in itself, barring external impediments.
C) The ruling must be agreed upon by all mujtahids.
D) The ruling must come from qiyas jali.

Key Takeaway
Text and ijma are inherently definitive (qat'i) in the Hanafi school; only external impediments can affect their certainty, not their essential nature.

The Four Sources of Fiqh: The Dual Nature of Qiyas
Defining the four sources and explaining Qiyas as both source and branch

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four primary sources of fiqh and explain why qiyas is considered both a source and a branch relative to the first three.

Core Idea
The first three sources are absolute; qiyas is a source that manifests rulings from them.

This passage from a classical usul text introduces the foundational sources of Islamic law. It emphasizes that while the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' are independent proofs, Qiyas (analogical reasoning) occupies a unique position: it is a source for deriving rulings but is ultimately derived from the three primary sources. Understanding this duality is crucial for correctly applying qiyas in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Sources
List the four sources mentioned in the text: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas.
These are the primary sources in Hanafi usul.
2
Distinguish Absolute Sources
Recognize that the first three are called 'absolute sources' because each independently establishes a ruling without need for external proof.
They are uṣūl muṭlaqah.
3
Explain Qiyas as Source
Understand why qiyas is considered a source: it is a source relative to the ruling (aṣl bi-nisbat ilā al-ḥukm) because it establishes a new ruling.
It is not independent but derivative.
4
Explain Qiyas as Branch
Understand why qiyas is a branch: it is a branch relative to the first three (far‘ bi-nisbat ilā al-thalāthah al-ūlā) because its ‘illah is extracted from those sources.
The ruling ultimately traces back to the primary sources.
5
Work Through the Example
Apply the explanation to the provided example: the prohibition of sodomy is derived by qiyas from the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation, which is based on Quran 2:222.
The 'illah is 'harm' (adha).

و أصول الفقه الكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةَ وَالإجمَاعُ وَالْقِيَاسُ وَإِن كَانَ ذَا فَرعًا لِلثلاثَةِ لَمَّا ذَكَرَ أَنَّ أُصُولَ الفِقِهِ مَا يُبَتَنَى عَلَيْهِ الفِقهُ أَرَادَ أَن يُبَيِّنَ أَنَّ مَا يُبَتَنَى عَلَيْهِ الفِقهُ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فَقَالَ هُوَ هَذِهِ الأَربَعَةُ؛ فَالثَّلاثَةُ الأُولُ أُصُولٌ مُطلَقَةٌ؛ لأنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا مُثبِتْ لِلحُكمِ أَمَّا القِيَاسُ فَهُوَ أَصل مِن وَجهِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَصل بِالنِّسبَةِ إِلَى الحكمِ وَفَرحٌ مِن وَجهِ؛ لأنه فرع بِالنِّسبَةِ إِلَى الثَّلَاثَةِ الْأَوَلِ إذ العِلَّةُ فِيهِ مُستَنبَطَةٌ مِن مَوَارِدِهَا فَيَكُونُ الحُكمُ الثَّابِتُ بِالقِيَاسِ ثَابِتًا بِتِلكَ الَّا دِلَّةِ وَأَيضًا هُوَ لَيسَ بِمُثبِت بَل هُوَ مُظهِرٌ أَمَّا نَظِيرُ القِيَاسِ المُستَنبَطِ مِن الكِتَابِ فَكَقِيَاسِ حُرمَةِ اللَّوَاطَةِ عَلَى حُرمَةِ الوَطءِ فِي حَالَةِ الحَيضِ الثَّابِتَةِ بِقَولِهِ تَعَالَى قُل هُوَ أَذًى فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي
And the sources of fiqh are: the Book, the Sunnah, Consensus, and Analogy—even though Analogy is a branch of the three. Since he mentioned that the sources of fiqh are that upon which fiqh is built, he intended to explain what that upon which fiqh is built is. So he said: it is these four. Thus the first three are absolute sources because each of them establishes the ruling. As for analogy (qiyās), it is a source in one respect: because it is a source relative to the ruling; and it is a branch in another respect: because it is a branch relative to the first three, since the cause (ʿillah) in it is derived from their sources. Therefore the ruling established by analogy is established by those proofs. Also, it is not an establisher (muthbit) but rather a manifestor (muẓhir). An example of analogy derived from the Book is like analogizing the prohibition of sodomy (liwāṭah) to the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation, which is established by His saying: 'Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during...'
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage defines the four sources (uṣūl) of fiqh in the Hanafi tradition: the Quran (Kitāb), Sunnah, Consensus (Ijmā‘), and Analogy (Qiyās). The author explains that the first three are absolute sources (uṣūl muṭlaqah) because each independently establishes a ruling. Analogy, however, is a source in one sense and a branch in another. It is a source relative to the ruling because it derives a new ruling, but it is a branch relative to the first three because its legal cause (ʿillah) is extracted from those primary sources. Thus the ruling established by analogy is ultimately grounded in the primary proofs. Analogy does not create a ruling ex nihilo; it merely manifests (muẓhir) what is already implicit in the primary texts. The passage gives an example: the prohibition of sodomy is derived by analogy from the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation, which is based on the Quranic verse 'Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during...' (Quran 2:222). This illustrates how the Quran serves as the original source, and analogy extends the ruling to similar cases. The Hanafi position emphasizes that qiyās is a valid and essential tool for deriving law, but it must be anchored in the primary sources.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (uṣūl al-fiqh): The sources upon which fiqh is built; the four evidence bases for deriving Islamic law.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning: extending a known ruling to a new case due to shared 'illah.
أصل (aṣl): Source; a foundational proof that establishes a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is Qiyās different from the first three sources?
A) Qiyās is not a source at all
B) Qiyās is a source but does not establish a ruling; it only manifests
C) Qiyās is an absolute source like the others
D) Qiyās establishes rulings independently without reference to primary texts

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid source of fiqh, but it is derivative: it manifests rulings already implicit in the primary sources.

The Four Sources of Fiqh and the Nature of Qiyas
Defining the four sources of fiqh and clarifying the role of qiyas as a derivative source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources of fiqh and explain why qiyas is considered both a source and a branch in Hanafi usul, and distinguish between an establisher (muthbit) and a revealer (muzhir).

Core Idea
Qiyas does not create new rulings; it reveals rulings already implicit in the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

This passage from a classic Hanafi usul commentary defines the four foundational sources of fiqh and clarifies the distinct nature of qiyas. While the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma are absolute sources that independently establish rulings, qiyas occupies a unique position: it is a source relative to the ruling it reveals, but a branch relative to the three primary sources. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sources
From the text, list the four sources explicitly mentioned: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), and Qiyas (analogical reasoning).
These are the primary sources in Hanafi usul; secondary sources like istihsan are discussed elsewhere.
2
Distinguish absolute vs. relative sources
Note that the first three are called 'absolute sources' (usul mutlaqah) because each independently establishes (muthbit) a ruling. Qiyas is a source in one respect (relative to the ruling) and a branch in another (relative to the first three).
The term 'muthbit' means establisher; 'muzhir' means revealer. Qiyas is described as muzhir, not muthbit.
3
Understand the derivation of qiyas
The effective cause (illah) in qiyas is derived from the sources of the primary texts (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma). Therefore, the ruling established by qiyas is ultimately rooted in those primary proofs.
This reinforces that qiyas does not introduce a new ruling ex nihilo; it makes explicit what is already implied.
4
Examine the examples of qiyas
Review the three examples provided: from the Quran (prohibition of sodomy analogized to prohibition of intercourse during menstruation based on harm), from the Sunnah (riba prohibition analogized to lime/wheat exchange), and from Ijma (prohibition of marrying the mother of a woman with whom one committed zina based on affinity).
Each example shows the illah extracted from the primary source.

سائل قیاسیہ کا نام ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ ظن طریق میں ہے (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)۔ وصلہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے اس سے غرض تفتازانی فقہ کو قطعی ثابت کرنے کے لئے ماقبل میں جو انتہائی کوشش کی گئی ہے اس پر اعتراض کرتا ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ نے قیاس اول میں جو صغرنی کی دلیل دی اس کو تو ہم مانتے ہیں لیکن قیاس ثانی کا صغری یعنی کل ما يجب العمل علیه قطعا علم قطعا انه حکم اللہ تعالی اس کی دلیل ہم نہیں مانتے کیونکہ اس کی دلیل دی ہے کہ اللہ کے ہاں حکم نہ ہوتا تو عمل واجب نہ ہوتا اس کو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں کہ جس پر عمل واجب ہو وہ قطعا اللہ کی طرف سے ہوایسا بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ کہ عمل واجب ہو اس وجہ سے کہ ظن ہو کہ یہ اللہ کا حکم ہے تو عمل کے واجب ہونے میں عین اختلاف ہے تو اس کو دلیل بنانا درست نہیں خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ کبری غیر مدلل ہے اور اگر کہو یہ قول فرقہ مصوبہ کا ہے تو بھی درست نہیں کیونکہ ان کے نزد یک فقد یجب علیہ العمل والا قضیہ درست نہیں ہے پھر اس کو ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے فلہذا کبری غیر مدلل ہوا خلاصہ یہ کہ شاریخ نے امکانی کوشش کو رد کر دیا ہے۔ در حقیقت غالیہ ما امکن کی تقریر اور اس کے حل کی ضرورت ہی پیش نہیں آتی جب کہ شاریخ کے تمام اعتراضات کے جوابات سابق میں مذکور ہو چکے ہیں ۔ وأصول الفقه الكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةَ وَالإجمَاعُ وَالْقِيَاسُ وَإِن كَانَ ذَا فَرعًا لِلثلاثَةِ لَمَّا ذَكَرَ أَنَّ أُصُولَ الفِقِهِ مَا يُبَتَنَى عَلَيْهِ الفِقهُ أَرَادَ أَن يُبَيِّنَ أَنَّ مَا يُبَتَنَى عَلَيْهِ الفِقهُ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فَقَالَ هُوَ هَذِهِ الأَربَعَةُ ؛ فَالثَّلاثَةُ الأُولُ أُصُولٌ مُطلَقَةٌ ؛ لأنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا مُثبِتْ لِلحُكمِ أَمَّا القِيَاسُ فَهُوَ أَصل مِن وَجهِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَصل بِالنِّسبَةِ إِلَى الحكمِ وَفَرحٌ مِن وَجهِ ؛ لأنه فرع بِالنِّسبَةِ إِلَى الثَّلَاثَةِ الْأَوَلِ إذ العِلَّةُ فِيهِ مُستَنبَطَةٌ مِن مَوَارِدِهَا فَيَكُونُ الحُكمُ الثَّابِتُ بِالقِيَاسِ ثَابِتًا بِتِلكَ الَّا دِلَّةِ وَأَيضًا هُوَ لَيسَ بِمُثبِت بَل هُوَ مُظهِرٌ أَمَّا نَظِيرُ القِيَاسِ المُستَنبَطِ مِن الكِتَابِ فَكَقِيَاسِ حُرمَةِ اللَّوَاطَةِ عَلَى حُرمَةِ الوَطءِ فِي حَالَةِ الحَيضِ الثَّابِتَةِ بِقَولِهِ تَعَالَى قُل هُوَ أَذًى فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي المَحِيضِ وَالعِلَّهُ هِى الأذَى وَأَمَّا المُستَبَطُ مِنَ السُّنَّةِ فَكَقِيَاسِ حُرمَةِ فَفِيزِ مِن الجَصَّ بِقَفِيزَينِ عَلَى حُرمَةِ قَفِيزِ مِن الحِنطَةِ بِقَفِيزَينِ الثَّابِتَةِ بِقَولِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الحِنطَةُ بالحِنطَةِ مَثَلًا بِمَثَلِ يَدًا بِيَدٍ وَالفَضلُ رِبًا وَأَمَّا المُستَنبَطُ مِن الإِجماع فَأَورَدُوا لِنَظِيرهِ قِيَاسَ الوَطءِ الحَرَامِ عَلَى الحَلالِ فِي حُرمَةِ المُصَاهَرَةِ يَعْنِي قِيَاسَ حُرمَةِ وَطءِ أُمِّ المُزَنِيَّةِ عَلَى حُرمَةِ وَطهِ أُمِّ أَمَتِهِ الَّتِي وَطِيَّهَا وَالحُرمَهُ فِي المَقِيسِ عَلَيهِ ثَابِتَةٌ إِجْمَاعًا وَلَا نَصَّ فِيهِ بَل النَّصُّ وَارِدٌ فِي أُمَّهَاتِ النِّسَاءِ مِن غَيرِ اشْتِرَاطِ الوَطءِ . ترجمہ:۔ (اصول فقہ کتاب سنت رسول، اجماع اور قیاس ہیں اگر چہ وہ فرع بنے والا ہے ان تینوں کی ) جب ذکر کیا ہے اس بات کا کہ فقہ کے اصول وہ ہوتے ہیں کہ جن پر فقہ موقوف ہو تو ارادہ کیا اس بات کا کہ یہ کہ بیان کرے اس چیز کو جس پر فقہ موقوف ہو کہ وہ کون سی چیز ہے پس فرمایا کہ وہ یہی چار ہیں۔ پہلے تین اصول مطلقہ ہیں اس لئے کہ ہر ایک ان میں سے مثبت ہے حکم کے لئے ۔ بہر حال قیاس پس وہ اصل ہے من وجہ اس لئے کہ وہ اصل ہے نسبت کرتے ہوئے حکم کی طرف اور فرع ہے من وجہ اس لئے کہ یہ فرع ہے نسبت کرتے ہوئے پہلے تین اصول کی طرف اس لئے کہ علت اس (قیاس ) میں مستنبط ہوتی ہے ان (اصول ثلثہ ) کے وارد ہونے کی جگہوں سے پس ہو جائے گا وہ حکم جو ثابت ہونے والا ہو گا قیاس کے ساتھ وہ ثابت ہونے والا ہو گا ان ادلہ کے ساتھ اور یہ بھی کہ وہ نہیں ہے مثبت بلکہ وہ تو مظہر ہے۔ اور بہر حال اس قیاس کی نظیر سے جو مستنبط ہے کتاب سے پس جیسا کہ لواطت کی حرمت کو قیاس کرنا وطی کی حرمت پر حالت حیض میں جو ثابت ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول قل ہو ازی فاعتزلوا النساء فی الحیض سے اور علت وہ گندگی ہے اور بہر حال مثال اس قیاس کی جو مستنبط ہے سنت سے پس جیسا کہ چونے کی ایک قفیز کی حرمت کو قیاس کرنا دو قفیزوں کے بدلے میں گندم کے ایک قفیز کی حرمت پر دو قفیزوں کے بدلے میں اس میں سے ہے جو ثابت ہونے والے ہیں آپ اللہ کے قول کے ساتھ الحظہ بالحط مثلاً بمثل يدا بيد والفضل ربوا سے اور بہر حال مستقبط من الا جماع کی مثال پس لائے وہ اس کی مثال ولی حرام کو قیاس کرنا ولی حلال پر حرمت مصاہرہ میں یعنی ام مزنیہ کی وطی کی حرمت کو قیاس کرنا اہم موطوہ کی وطی کی حرمت پر اور حرمت مقیس عالیہ میں ثابت ہے اجماعا اور نہیں ہے کوئی نص اس میں بلکہ نص وارد ہونے والی ہے بیویوں کی ماؤں کی حرمت کے بارے میں بغیر ولی کی شرط کے۔
The sources of fiqh are the Book, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma), and analogical reasoning (qiyas), even if it (qiyas) is a branch of the first three. When he mentioned that the sources of fiqh are that upon which fiqh is based, he intended to explain what that upon which fiqh is based is, so he said: It is these four. The first three are absolute sources because each of them establishes a ruling. As for qiyas, it is a source in one respect, because it is a source relative to the ruling, and a branch in one respect, because it is a branch relative to the first three, since the effective cause in it is derived from their sources; thus the ruling established by qiyas is established by those proofs. Also, it is not an establisher but rather a revealer. As for an example of qiyas derived from the Book: it is like measuring the prohibition of sodomy on the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation, which is established by His statement: 'Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation' and the effective cause is harm. As for that derived from the Sunnah: it is like measuring a qafiz of lime for two qafiz [of wheat] on the prohibition of a qafiz of wheat for two qafiz, established by his statement, peace be upon him: 'Wheat for wheat, equal for equal, hand to hand, and excess is usury.' As for that derived from consensus: they provided an example of measuring unlawful intercourse on lawful intercourse in the prohibition of marriage affinity, meaning measuring the prohibition of intercourse with the mother of a woman with whom one has committed zina on the prohibition of intercourse with the mother of one's female slave whom one has had intercourse with, and the prohibition in the analogized-from is established by consensus, and there is no text on it; rather the text is regarding the prohibition of mothers of wives without stipulation of intercourse.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and explanatory text from a Hanafi usul commentary. It first reviews a previous criticism of Taftazani's attempt to prove fiqh as definitive, then proceeds to define the four sources of fiqh: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma), and analogical reasoning (qiyas). The author clarifies that the first three are absolute sources because each independently establishes a ruling. Qiyas, however, is considered a source in one respect (relative to the ruling it reveals) and a branch in another (relative to the first three sources, because its effective cause (illah) is derived from their textual sources). Therefore, the ruling established via qiyas is ultimately rooted in the Quran, Sunnah, or ijma. Moreover, qiyas is not an establisher (muthbit) but a revealer (muzhir) of rulings. The passage then provides concrete examples of qiyas from each of the three primary sources: from the Quran, the prohibition of sodomy is analogized to the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation (based on the verse about harm); from the Sunnah, the prohibition of exchanging one qafiz of lime for two qafiz of wheat is analogized to the prohibition of one qafiz of wheat for two qafiz (based on the hadith on riba); from ijma, the prohibition of marrying the mother of a woman with whom one has committed zina is analogized to the prohibition of marrying the mother of one's female slave after intercourse (a ruling established by consensus). These examples illustrate how qiyas operates within the Hanafi methodology, always deriving its authority from the primary sources.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The four foundational sources upon which fiqh is based: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that derives a ruling for a new case from an existing case based on a shared effective cause (illah); it is a source in one respect (relative to the ruling) and a branch in another (relative to the first three sources).
مُثبِت (muthbit): One who establishes or creates a ruling; the first three sources are muthbit, while qiyas is not.
مُظهِر (muzhir): One who reveals or manifests a ruling that is already established by the primary sources; qiyas is described as muzhir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is described as both a source (asl) in one respect and a branch (far‘) in another?
A) The Quran
B) The Sunnah
C) Consensus (ijma)
D) Analogical reasoning (qiyas)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a derivative source that reveals rulings from the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma; it is not an independent establisher of rulings.

The Four Sources of Usul al-Fiqh and Qiyas from Each
Defining the four sources and illustrating qiyas from each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources of usul al-fiqh, distinguish between absolute and imperfect principles, and explain how qiyas is derived from each of the three primary sources.

Core Idea
The first three sources are independent; qiyas is a branch that manifests their rulings.

This lesson defines the four foundations of Islamic law according to the Hanafi school: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. You will learn why qiyas is considered a subordinate source and see concrete examples of how qiyas is derived from each of the three primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sources
List the four sources as given in the passage: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, the consensus (ijma) of the Ummah, and legal analogy (qiyas).
2
Understand the absolute vs. imperfect distinction
Recognize that the first three are 'absolute principles' (usul mutlaqah) because they are independent and directly establish rulings, while qiyas is a principle in one aspect (as it appears to be the source) but a branch in another (since its illah is derived from the three).
3
Analyze the first example (Quran-based qiyas)
See how liwat (sodomy) with one's wife is analogized to intercourse during menstruation due to the common cause of 'filthiness'. Note the clarification that this qiyas is for the specific case of the wife, not for the general prohibition which is from text.
The passage answers a potential objection to illustrate the scope of qiyas.
4
Analyze the second example (Hadith-based qiyas)
Observe how the prohibition of selling one qafiz of lime for two qafiz is analogized to the six ribawi items mentioned in the hadith, based on the cause of being measurable (qadariyyah) and same genus (jinsiyyah).
5
Analyze the third example (Ijma-based qiyas)
Understand that the prohibition of marrying the mother of a woman with whom one has committed zina is analogized to the prohibition of marrying the mother of a slave woman one has had intercourse with, a ruling proven by ijma, due to the cause of partiality (ba'diyyah).
6
Examine the Talwih classification
Review the systematic division of proofs into revelation (Quran or Sunnah) and non-revelation (ijma or qiyas), and understand that other sources (e.g., shara'i' man qablana, custom) all revert to these four.
This reinforces the absolute vs. subordinate hierarchy.

مصادیق اصول فقہ
تشریح اصول الفقہ : ۔ ماتن نے اصول فقہ کی پہلے تعریف اضافی کی تھی کہ اصول فقہ وہ ہیں جن پر فقہ کی بنیاد ہو اب اس کا مصداق بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اس کا مصداق چار چیزیں ہیں (۱) کتاب اللہ (۲) سنت رسول الله الله (۳) اجماع امت محمدیہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم (۴) قیاس شرعی فرق ان میں یہ ہے کہ پہلے تین اصول مطلقہ ہیں اور چوتھا اصل قیاس یہ اصل ناقص ہے یعنی مین وجہ اصل ہے اور من وجہ فرع ہے اگر حکم کی طرف دیکھیں کہ وہ قیاس سے ثابت ہے تو اس اعتبار سے اصل ہے اور اگر یہ دیکھیں کہ اس کی علت کا استنباط اصول ثلثہ سے ہے تو اس اعتبار سے فرع ہے کیونکہ قیاس سے ثابت ہونے والا حکم در اصل دلائل ثلاثہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے قیاس تو صرف مظہر احکام ہے مثبت احکام نہیں۔
اصول ثلثہ سے مستقبط قیاس کے نظائر
اس قیاس کی مثال جو کتاب اللہ سے مستنبط ہے جیسے لواطت حرام ہے اس کو قیاس کیا ہے حالت حیض میں بیوی سے جماع کرنے کی حرمت پر کہ اس کی علت گندگی ہے لہذا یہ بھی حرام ہے اس علت کی وجہ سے یہ قیاس کتاب اللہ سے مستنبط ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ لواطت کی حرمت کتاب اللہ یعنی نص سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے شرائع من قبلنا کے احکام جو قرآن پاک میں مذکور ہیں اور ان کا رد نہ کیا گیا ہو تو وہ امت محمدیہ پر لازم ہیں لہذا قوم لوط کا تذکرہ قرآن پاک میں موجود ہے اور ان کا عیب بیان کیا گیا ہے اور اس کی حرمت کو رد نہیں کیا گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ لواطت جیسے ان پر حرام ہے ویسے ہم پر بھی حرام ہے یہ مسئلہ تو منصوص علیہا ہے قیاس سے ثابت ہی نہیں کیونکہ قیاس ان مسائل میں ہوتا ہے جن کا اصول ثلاثہ سے ثبوت نہ ہو تو اس کو قیاس کی مثال بنانا درست نہیں ہے۔
جواب (۱):۔ یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں مطلقا لواطت کا ذکر ہے کہ مردوں سے ہو یا عورتوں سے ہو یہاں قیاس کی نظیر بیویوں سے لواطت ہے کیونکہ کسی کو وہم ہوسکتا ہے کہ بیوی سے ہر قسم کا نفع جائز ہے تو لواطت بھی جائز ہو تو فرمایا کہ اپنی بیوی سے بھی لواطت حرام ہے اس کو قیاس کیا ہے اپنی بیوی سے حالت حیض میں وطی کے حرام ہونے پر گندگی کی وجہ سے۔
جواب (۲):۔ کہ ٹھیک ہے کہ لواطت کی حرمت قرآن مجید سے ثابت ہے لیکن لوطی کے انکار کو ختم کرنے کے لئے اور مزید تاکید کے لئے اس کو قیاس کی مثال بنایا ہے کہ جس طرح اس کی حرمت نص سے ثابت ہے اسی طرح قیاس منصوص العلہ سے بھی اس کی حرمت ثابت ہے قیاس مستقبط من الحدیث کی مثال جس طرح چونے کے ایک قفیز کی بیع کی حرمت دو قفیز کے ساتھ اس کو قیاس کیا گیا ان چھ چیزوں کی بیع پر جن کو حدیث میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے المحطة بالحطة مثلا بمثل يدا بيد والفضل ربوا که جس طرح قدریت و جنسیت کی علت کی وجہ سے ان چھ چیزوں میں کمی زیادتی حرام ہے اسی طرح چونے کی بیچ چونے کے ساتھ ہو تو بھی کمی زیادتی حرام ہوگی کیونکہ اس میں بھی علت (قدریت و جنسیت) پائی جاتی ہے قیاس مستنبط من الاجماع کی مثال یہ ہے کہ زانی کے لئے مزنیہ کی ماں حرام ہے اب مزنیہ کی ماں کا حرام ہونا اس کو قیاس کیا ہے موطو ہ لونڈی کی ماں کی حرمت پر مثلاً اگر ایک لونڈی سے وطی کرلے تو لونڈی کی ماں حرام ہو گی اب لونڈی کی ماں کی حرمت قرآن مجید و حدیث میں مذکور نہیں ہے قرآن میں بیوی کی ماں کی حرمت کا ذکر ہے لونڈی والا مسئلہ مذکور نہیں تو اب لونڈی کی ماں کی حرمت اجماع سے ثابت ہے علت بعضیت و جزئیت کی وجہ سے اور یہ علت مزنیہ میں پائی جارہی ہے تو مزنیہ کے اصول و فروع بھی حرام ہونگے ۔
تلویح
قَولُهُ وَأُصُولُ الفِقهِ مَا سَبَقَ كَانَ بَيَانَ مَفهُومٍ أُصُولِ الفِقِهِ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيهِ هَذَا المَفهُومُ مِن الأنواع المُنحَصِرَةِ بِحُكم الاستقرَاءِ فِي الْأَربَعَةِ وَوَجهُ ضَبطِهِ أَنَّ الدَّلِيلَ الشَّرعِيَّ إِمَّا وَحَيٌّ أَو غَيْرُهُ وَالوَحَى إِن كَانَ مَتَلُوا فَالكِتَابُ وَإِلَّا فَالسُّنَّةُ وَغَيْرُ الوَحِي إِن كَانَ قَولَ كُلِّ الْأُمَّةِ مِنْ عَصرِ فَالإِجْمَاعُ وَإِلَّا فَالقِيَاسُ أو أَنَّ الدَّلِيلَ إِمَّا أَن يَضِلَ إِلَيْنَا مِن الرَّسُولِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَو لَا وَالْأَوَّلُ إن تَعَلَّقَ بِنَظمِهِ الإعجاز فَالكِتَابُ وَإِلَّا فَالسُّنَّةُ وَالثَّانِي إِن اشْتَرِطَ عِصمَةً مَن صَدَرَ عَنهُ فَالإِجْمَاعُ وَإِلَّا فَالقِيَاسُ .
وَأَمَّا شَرَائِعُ مَن قَبلَنَا وَالتَّعَامُلُ وَقَولُ الصَّحَابِي وَنَحوُ ذَلِكَ فَرَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى الأربَعَةِ وَكَذَا المَعقُولُ نَوع استدلال بِأَحَدِهَا وَإِلَّا فَلَا دَخَلَ لِلرَّايِ فِي إِثْبَاتِ الًا حَكَامِ وَمَا جَعَلَهُ بَعْضُهُم نَوعًا خَامِسًا مِنَ الَّا دِلَّةِ وَسَمَّاهُ الِاسْتِدَلَالَ فَحَاصِلُهُ يَرجِعُ إِلَى التَّمَسُّكِ بِمَعْقُولِ النَّصّ أو الإجمَاعِ صُرِحَ بِذلِكَ فِي الْأَحكَامِ ثُمَّ الثَّلاثَةُ الأوّلُ أَصُولٌ مُطلَقَةٌ لِكُونِهَا أَدِلَّةٌ مُستَقِلَّةُ مُشتَةٌ لِلْأحكامِ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَصَلِّ مِن وجه لاستنَادِ الحكم إِلَيْهِ ظَاهِرًا دُونَ وَجهِ لِكَونِهِ فَرعًا لِلثَّلَاثَةِ لَا بِتِنَايُهِ عَلَى عِلَّةٍ
Realities of Usul al-Fiqh: Explanation of Usul al-Fiqh: The author first gave an additional definition of usul al-fiqh: usul al-fiqh are those upon which fiqh is based. Now he states its reality: that its reality consists of four things: (1) the Book of Allah, (2) the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), (3) the consensus (ijma) of the Ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him), and (4) legal analogy (qiyas shar'i). The difference between them is that the first three are absolute principles (usul mutlaqah), and the fourth, the principle of qiyas, is an imperfect principle: it is a principle in one aspect and a branch in another. If we look at the ruling that it is proven by qiyas, then in that respect it is a principle; and if we look at the fact that its cause (illah) is derived from the three principles, then in that respect it is a branch. Because the ruling proven by qiyas is originally proven by the three proofs; qiyas is only a manifestation (muzhir) of rulings, not a positive establisher of rulings.
Examples of qiyas derived from the three principles: An example of qiyas derived from the Book of Allah: like that liwat (anal intercourse) is forbidden; it is analogized to the prohibition of intercourse with a wife during menstruation, because its cause (illah) is filthiness (gandagi). Therefore this (liwat) is also forbidden due to this cause. This qiyas is derived from the Book of Allah.
Question: It is said that the prohibition of liwat is proven by the Book of Allah, i.e., by text, because the rule is: the laws of those before us (shara'i' man qablana) that are mentioned in the Holy Quran and not abrogated are binding upon the Ummah of Muhammad. Hence the mention of the people of Lut in the Quran and the condemnation of their act, and the fact that its prohibition is not abrogated, shows that liwat is forbidden for them as it is forbidden for us. This issue is textually specified (mansus 'alayha), not proven by qiyas, because qiyas is applied to issues not proven by the three principles. So making it an example of qiyas is not correct.
Answer (1): It is said that the Quran mentions liwat absolutely, whether with men or women. Here the example of qiyas is liwat with wives, because someone might think that every form of enjoyment with one's wife is permissible, so liwat would also be permissible. So it is said that liwat with one's wife is also forbidden, analogized to the prohibition of intercourse with one's wife during menstruation due to filthiness.
Answer (2): It is correct that the prohibition of liwat is proven by the Quran, but to eliminate the denial of the sodomite and for further emphasis, it is made an example of qiyas: just as its prohibition is proven by text, so also its prohibition is proven by qiyas based on a textually indicated cause (qiyas mansus al-'illah).
Example of qiyas derived from hadith: just as the prohibition of selling one qafiz of lime (chuna) with two qafiz is analogized to the sale of the six items mentioned in the hadith: 'al-mithlu bi al-mithli, mathalan bi mathalin, yadan bi yadin, wa al-fadlu riba.' So just as due to the cause of being a measure and of the same genus (qadariyyah wa jinsiyyah), excess and deficiency are forbidden in those six items, similarly in the sale of lime (chuna) with lime, excess and deficiency are forbidden because the cause (qadariyyah wa jinsiyyah) is also found in it.
Example of qiyas derived from ijma: The mother of a woman with whom one has committed zina (muzniyya) becomes forbidden to the fornicator. The prohibition of the mother of the muzniyya is analogized to the prohibition of the mother of a slave woman with whom one has had intercourse (mawtu'a). For example, if a man has intercourse with a slave woman, then the mother of that slave woman becomes forbidden. Now the prohibition of the mother of a slave woman is not mentioned in the Quran or hadith; the Quran mentions the prohibition of the wife's mother, not the slave woman's mother. So the prohibition of the slave woman's mother is proven by ijma, due to the cause of partiality and particularity (ba'diyyah wa juz'iyyah). And this cause is found in the muzniyya, so her ascendants and descendants also become forbidden.
At-Talwih: His statement: 'And usul al-fiqh have preceded' was an explanation of the concept (mafhum) of usul al-fiqh, and this is an explanation of what this concept applies to (sadaqa 'alayhi) from among the types that are limited by inference (istiqra') to four. And the way to define it is that the legal proof (dalil shar'i) is either revelation (wahy) or other than it. Revelation: if it is recited (matluw) then it is the Book; otherwise it is the Sunnah. Other than revelation: if it is the saying of the entire ummah from a particular era, then it is ijma; otherwise it is qiyas. Or: the proof either reaches us from the Messenger (peace be upon him) or not. The first: if it involves miraculous inimitability (i'jaz) in its wording, then it is the Book; otherwise it is the Sunnah. The second: if it requires infallibility ('ismah) from the one it originates from, then it is ijma; otherwise it is qiyas. As for the laws of those before us (shara'i' man qablana), customary practice (ta'amul), the saying of a Companion (qawl al-sahabi), and the like, they all go back to the four. Likewise, the rational (ma'qul) is a type of inference using one of them; otherwise, there is no role for personal opinion (ra'y) in establishing rulings. What some scholars made a fifth type of proofs and called 'al-istidlal' (inference) ultimately goes back to adhering to the meaning of the text or ijma, as explicitly stated in al-Ahkam. Then the first three are absolute principles (usul mutlaqah) because they are independent proofs that establish rulings directly, while qiyas is a principle in one respect (min wajh) because the ruling is apparently based on it, but not in another respect because it is a branch (far') of the three, as it depends on a cause (illah).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a definition and illustration of the four sources of usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school. It opens by stating that the author (likely al-Taftazani or Sadr al-Shari'ah) previously gave a conceptual definition of usul al-fiqh (as 'the things upon which fiqh is based') and now provides the concrete instances (masadiq) of that concept, which are four: the Quran, the Sunnah, ijma (consensus), and qiyas (analogy). A key distinction is made: the first three are 'absolute principles' (usul mutlaqah) because they are independent and directly establish rulings, while qiyas is a principle in one sense (as it appears to be the source of a ruling) but a branch in another (since its underlying cause (illah) is derived from the three principles). This reflects the Hanafi position that qiyas is a subordinate source—it merely manifests rulings that are essentially derived from the Quran, Sunnah, or ijma.

The passage then gives examples of qiyas derived from each of the three primary sources. For the Quran: the prohibition of liwat (anal intercourse) is analogized to the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation, based on the common cause of 'filthiness.' A question and answer follow, clarifying that the qiyas is not for the basic prohibition of liwat (which is from text via the principle of shara'i' man qablana), but for the specific case of liwat with one's wife, to counter any misconception that marriage allows any form of sexual act. The second answer also emphasizes that the example serves to strengthen the prohibition by showing it is supported both by text and by qiyas.

For the Hadith: the prohibition of selling one measure of lime for two measures is analogized to the six ribawi items mentioned in the hadith, based on the cause of being measurable (qadariyyah) and same genus (jinsiyyah).

For Ijma: the prohibition of marrying the mother of a woman with whom one has committed zina is analogized to the prohibition of marrying the mother of a slave woman one has had intercourse with, a ruling established by ijma (not by Quran or hadith). The common cause is 'partiality' (ba'diyyah) or a specific relationship.

Finally, the passage includes an Arabic excerpt from At-Talwih, which systematically classifies the proofs: revelation (Quran or Sunnah) vs. non-revelation (ijma or qiyas), and explains that other sources like the laws of previous prophets, customs, and Companion sayings all revert to these four. It reiterates that qiyas is a branch relying on the three, and that the first three are absolute principles. This aligns with the Hanafi usul hierarchy where qiyas is a valid but derivative source.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): A source or principle from which rulings are derived; here refers to the four foundations of fiqh.
قياس (qiyas): Legal analogy: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared cause (illah).
علة (illah): The cause or attribute that serves as the basis for analogy, e.g., 'filthiness' (gandagi) for liwat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is qiyas considered an 'imperfect principle' (aṣl nāqiṣ)?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because its ruling is based on a cause (illah) derived from the three primary sources, making it a branch of them
C) Because it was rejected by the early scholars
D) Because it applies only to matters of worship

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a secondary source that manifests the rulings of the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Four Sources of Shari'ah Evidence and the Rejection of a Fifth
Defining the four sources of Shari'ah evidence and refuting a fifth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of legal evidence into four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and explain why istidlal is not an independent source.

Core Idea
All Shari'ah evidence reduces to four: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas derived from them.

In the previous lesson, you learned the definition of usul al-fiqh. Now, al-Taftazani explains what that concept actually refers to: the four types of evidence that are the foundations of Islamic law. The passage uses two logical divisions to show that only these four qualify, and then addresses attempts to add a fifth source (istidlal), carefully demonstrating why it is not independent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions of legal evidence
The passage presents two ways of categorizing evidence: (1) revelation vs. non-revelation, and (2) what reaches us from the Prophet vs. what does not. Follow each division step by step to see how they yield the same four sources.
The first division: Revelation → recited (Quran) or non-recited (Sunnah); non-revelation → consensus of the ummah (Ijma') or else Qiyas.
2
Extract the four sources from both divisions
From either division, the outcome is: 1) Quran, 2) Sunnah, 3) Ijma', 4) Qiyas. Confirm that the passage explicitly states this enumeration.
The second division: From the Prophet → with i'jaz (Quran) or without (Sunnah); not from the Prophet → with infallibility (Ijma') or without (Qiyas).
3
Analyze how other candidate sources are subsumed
The passage mentions laws before us, customary practice, sayings of Companions, etc., and states they all 'return to the four.' Understand that these are not independent but are subcategories of the four sources (e.g., qawl sahabi can be part of Sunnah or Ijma' depending).
Similarly, 'rational meaning' (ma'qul) is a type of inference using one of the four, not a separate source.
4
Examine the rejection of istidlal as a fifth source
Some scholars proposed a fifth source called istidlal (inference). The passage argues that its 'net result returns to adhering to the rational meaning of the text or ijma'.' This means any such inference is ultimately based on one of the four primary sources, particularly Qiyas.
The text cites al-Ahkam for this clarification. Note that Hanafis do not accept istidlal as independent; it is subsumed under the rational extension of the primary texts.
5
Understand the unique status of Qiyas
Qiyas is called a 'principle' (asl) in one respect because rulings are outwardly attributed to it. But it is actually derived from the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma') because its cause (illah) is extracted from them. Thus, the first three are independent; Qiyas is subordinate.
This is why it is often said 'the principles of fiqh are three, and the fourth is Qiyas extracted from them.'

تلویح
قَولُهُ وَأُصُولُ الفِقهِ مَا سَبَقَ كَانَ بَيَانَ مَفهُومٍ أُصُولِ الفِقِهِ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيهِ هَذَا المَفهُومُ مِن الأنواع المُنحَصِرَةِ بِحُكم الاستقرَاءِ فِي الْأَربَعَةِ وَوَجهُ ضَبطِهِ أَنَّ الدَّلِيلَ الشَّرعِيَّ إِمَّا وَحْيٌ أَو غَيْرُهُ وَالوَحَى إِن كَانَ مَتْلُوًا فَالكِتَابُ وَإِلَّا فَالسُّنَّةُ وَغَيْرُ الوَحِي إِن كَانَ قَولَ كُلِّ الْأُمَّةِ مِنْ عَصرِ فَالإِجْمَاعُ وَإِلَّا فَالقِيَاسُ أَو أَنَّ الدَّلِيلَ إِمَّا أَن يَصِلَ إِلَيْنَا مِن الرَّسُولِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَو لَا وَالْأَوَّلُ إن تَعَلَّقَ بِنَظمِهِ الإعجاز فَالكِتَابُ وَإِلَّا فَالسُّنَّةُ وَالثَّانِي إِن اشْتَرِطَ عِصمَةً مَن صَدَرَ عَنهُ فَالإِجْمَاعُ وَإِلَّا فَالقِيَاسُ .
وَأَمَّا شَرَائِعُ مَن قَبلَنَا وَالتَّعَامُلُ وَقَولُ الصَّحَابِي وَنَحوُ ذَلِكَ فَرَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى الأربَعَةِ وَكَذَا المَعقُولُ نَوع استدلال بِأحَدِهَا وَإِلَّا فَلَا دَخَلَ لِلرَّايِ فِي إِثْبَاتِ الأحْكَامِ وَمَا جَعَلَهُ بَعْضُهُم نَوعًا خَامِسًا مِنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَسَمَّاهُ الِاسْتِدْلَالَ فَحَاصِلُهُ يَرجِعُ إِلَى التَّمَسُّكِ بِمَعْقُولِ النَّصّ أو الإجمَاعِ صُرِحَ بِذلِكَ فِي الْأَحكَامِ ثُمَّ الثَّلاثَةُ الأوّلُ أَصُولٌ مُطلَقَةٌ لِكُونِهَا أَدِلَّةٌ مُستَقِلَّةٌ مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلْأحكامِ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَصْلٌ مِن وجه لاستنَادِ الحكم إِلَيْهِ ظَاهِرًا دُونَ وَجهِ لِكُونَهِ فَرعًا لِلثَّلَاثَةِ لِبِنَائِهِ عَلَى عِلَّةٍ مُسْتَبَطَةٍ مِن مَوَارِدِ الكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالإجمَاعِ فَالحُكمُ بِالتَّحقِيقِ مُسْتَنِدٌ إِلَيْهَا وَأَثَرُ القِيَاسِ فِى إظهَارِ الحُكمِ وَتَغييرِ وَصفِهِ مِن الخُصُوص إِلَى العُمُومِ وَمِن هُنَا يُقَالُ أُصول الفقهِ ثَلاثَةُ الكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةُ وَالإِجْمَاعُ وَالأَصلُ الرَّابِعُ القِيَاسُ المُسْتَبَطُ مِن هَذِهِ الْأُصُولِ الثَّلَاثَةِ
ترجمہ: جو گذر چکا وہ اصول فقہ کے مفہوم کا بیان تھا اور یہ اس چیز کا بیان ہے جس پر یہ مفہوم صادق آتا ہے ان انواع میں سے جو منحصر ہیں استقراء کے حکم کے ساتھ چار میں اور اسکی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ بیشک دلیل شرعی یا تو وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی ہوگی اور اگر وحی متلو ہو پس وہ کتاب اللہ ہے وگر نہ پس وہ سنت ہے اور غیر وحی اگر ہو ایک زمانے کے کل مجتہدین کا قول پس اجماع ہے وگرنہ قیاس ہے، یا بیشک دلیل بہر حال یہ کہ پہنچے گی ہماری طرف رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی جانب سے یا نہیں اور اول اگر ہو اس کی نظم کے ساتھ تعلق اعجاز کا پس کتاب ہے وگرنہ پس سنت ہے اور ثانی اگر شرط لگائی گئی اس شخص کی عصمت کی جس سے یہ صادر ہو پس اجماع ہے وگر نہ پس یہ قیاس ہے اور بہر حال شریعتیں جو ہم سے پہلے گزر چکیں اور تعامل الناس اور قول صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ اور اس کی مثل پس لوٹنے والی ہیں چار کی طرف اسی طرح عقلی دلیل بھی ان میں سے ایک قسم ہے وگر نہ پس نہیں ہے کوئی دخل رائے کے لئے احکام کو ثابت کرنے میں اور جو بنایا ہے اس دلیل عقلی کو ان میں سے بعض نے پانچویں قسم ادلتہ سے اور نام رکھا اس کا استدلال پس اس کا حاصل لوٹتا ہے تمسک کرنے کی طرف معقول نص کے ساتھ یا اجماع کے ساتھ تصریح کی گئی ہے اس کے ساتھ احکام میں پھر پہلے تین اصول مطلقہ ہیں بوجہ ہونے ان کے ادلہ مستقلہ مثبتہ الاحکام کے اور قیاس اصل ہے من وجہ بوجہ حکم کے منسوب ہونے اس کی طرف ظاہر ا دون وجہ بوجہ ہونے اس کے فرع تمن کے لئے بوجہ اس کے علت مستقبطہ پر مبنی ہونے کے کتاب اور سنت اور اجماع کے موارد ہے۔ پس حکم یقیناً منسوب ہوتا ہے ان علتوں کی طرف اور قیاس کا اثر حکم کے ظاہر کرنے میں اور اسکی وصف کو خصوص سے عموم کی طرف تبدیل کرنے میں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے کہا جاتا ہے کہ اصول فقہ تین ہیں کتاب اللہ سنت اور اجماع اور اصل چوتھا وہ قیاس ہے جو مستنبط ہوتا ہے ان اصول ثلثہ سے۔
تشریح : قولہ اصول الفقہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شاری ماقبیل سے ربط بیان کرتا ہے کہ پہلے اصول فقہ کی تعریف تھی اب مصداق بیان کرتے ہیں اور وہ چار چیزیں ہیں (۱) کتاب اللہ (۲) سنت رسول اللہ (۳) اجتماع (۴) قیاس۔
(Talwih) His saying: "And the principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) are what preceded." That was an exposition of the concept of usul al-fiqh. And this is an exposition of what this concept applies to from among the types that are confined by the ruling of induction to four. The way to delineate it is that the legal evidence either is revelation or other than it. Revelation if it is recited (mutluw) then it is the Book, otherwise it is the Sunnah. And other than revelation if it is the saying of the entire ummah of an era, then it is consensus (ijma'), otherwise it is analogy (qiyas). Or: the evidence either reaches us from the Messenger (peace be upon him) or not. The first: if its wording is connected with inimitability (i'jaz), then it is the Book; otherwise it is the Sunnah. The second: if infallibility is stipulated for the one from whom it emanated, then it is consensus; otherwise it is qiyas.

As for the laws of those before us, customary practice, the saying of a Companion, and the like, they all return to the four. Similarly, rational meaning (al-ma'qul) is a type of inference using one of them; otherwise there is no role for opinion in establishing rulings. And what some have made as a fifth type of evidence and named it istidlal (inference), its net result returns to adhering to the rational meaning of the text or consensus; this is explicitly stated in al-Ahkam. Then the first three are absolute principles because they are independent evidences that establish rulings. Qiyas is a principle in one respect because the ruling is attributed to it outwardly but not in another respect, because it is a branch of the three, due to its being built upon a cause extracted from the sources of the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma'. So the ruling in reality is attributed to them (the three). The effect of qiyas is in manifesting the ruling and changing its description from particularity to generality. Hence it is said: the principles of fiqh are three: the Book, the Sunnah, and Ijma'; and the fourth principle is qiyas extracted from these three principles.

Translation: "What has passed was an exposition of the concept of usul al-fiqh, and this is an exposition of what this concept applies to from among the types that are confined by the ruling of induction to four. The reason for this enumeration is that the legal evidence is either revelation or non-revelation. Revelation if recited is the Book of Allah, otherwise it is the Sunnah. Non-revelation if it is the statement of all mujtahids of an era, it is ijma', otherwise it is qiyas. Or: the evidence either reaches us from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) or not. The first: if its wording is connected with inimitability, it is the Book, otherwise it is the Sunnah. The second: if infallibility is stipulated for the one from whom it emanates, it is ijma', otherwise it is qiyas. And the laws of those before us, customary practice, the saying of a Companion, and the like, all return to the four. Similarly, rational evidence is a type from among them; otherwise there is no role for opinion in establishing rulings. And what some have made as a fifth type of evidence and named it istidlal, its net result returns to adhering to the rational meaning of the text or ijma'; this is explicitly stated in al-Ahkam. Then the first three are absolute principles because they are independent evidences establishing rulings. Qiyas is a principle in one respect because the ruling is attributed to it outwardly but not in another, because it is a branch for the three, due to its being built upon a cause extracted from the sources of the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma'. So the ruling is certainly attributed to those causes. And the effect of qiyas is in manifesting the ruling and changing its description from particularity to generality. For this reason it is said: the principles of fiqh are three: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, and Ijma'; and the fourth principle is qiyas which is extracted from these three principles."

Commentary: "His saying 'Usul al-fiqh': This is the first part of the sharh's expression. The commentator links to the previous discussion, explaining that previously there was a definition of usul al-fiqh; now he presents the actual referents, which are four things: (1) the Book of Allah, (2) the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, (3) Ijma', (4) Qiyas."
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from al-Talwih (by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani) expands on the definition of usul al-fiqh by detailing the four sources of shari'ah evidence. The presentation begins by stating that the earlier definition of usul al-fiqh is now followed by an explanation of its actual referents (musdaq), which are confined to four types through inductive reasoning. Two methods of division are provided: one based on whether the evidence is revelation or not, and the other based on whether it reaches us from the Prophet directly or not. Both methods yield the same four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. The passage then addresses other potential sources—such as the laws of previous prophets, customary practice, and the sayings of Companions—asserting that they are all reducible to the four. It also rejects the idea of a fifth independent source called istidlal, arguing that it returns to the rational meaning of the text or ijma'. The unique status of qiyas is clarified: it is a principle in one sense because rulings are attributed to it outwardly, but it is not independent; it is derived from the three primary sources. The commentary (tashrih) confirms this classification.

Key Terms
الدليل الشرعي (al-dalil al-shar'i): The evidence from which shari'ah rules are derived; categorized into four types as per Hanafi usul
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning based on a cause (illah) extracted from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma'
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): A term used by some scholars for a purported fifth source of evidence; the text explains it returns to the rational meaning of the text or ijma'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of Qiyas in relation to the other three sources?
A) It is equally independent as the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'.
B) It is a principle (asl) outwardly but actually a branch of the three.
C) It is not a valid source at all.
D) It is only used when consensus is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school confines primary evidence to four sources—Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas—and considers any claimed additional source (like istidlal) as derivative of these.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
12 min
The Four Principles of Usul al-Fiqh and Their Restriction
Classifying and proving the four sources of Islamic law through logical division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi logical division to classify any legal evidence into one of the four usul al-fiqh and explain why other sources (e.g., qawl sahabi, urf) are subsumed under them.

Core Idea
Legal evidence is restricted to four: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas—all other sources revert to these.

In this passage, the commentator establishes the Hanafi position that the sources of Islamic law are limited to four. Through two logical divisions, he demonstrates that every legal evidence must fall into one of these categories. He then addresses potential objections by showing that other commonly cited evidences, such as the practice of people or the statement of a Companion, are not independent but are encompassed by these four. Understanding this classification is fundamental to Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim of restriction
The passage asserts that the principles of fiqh are three (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) plus a fourth (Qiyas) derived from them. Recognize that this is a claim of completeness.
The 'three' are the primary independent sources; Qiyas is derivative but essential.
2
Analyze the first logical division
Trace the division: evidence is either revelation (wahy) or non-revelation. Revelation is either recited (matlu) → Quran, or non-recited → Sunnah. Non-revelation is either consensus of all mujtahids → Ijma, or else → Qiyas.
This division exhaustively covers all possibilities.
3
Analyze the second logical division
Evidence reaches us either through the Prophet (with intermediary) or without. With intermediary: either miraculous (i'jaz) → Quran, or not → Sunnah. Without intermediary: from infallible (ma'sum) → Ijma, or fallible→ Qiyas.
This division provides a different perspective but yields the same four categories.
4
Address objections: other sources
Understand how previous laws, urf, qawl sahabi, and rational evidence are subsumed under the four. For example, previous laws are evidence through Quran/Sunnah; urf through istihsan or qiyas; qawl sahabi as Ijma if unanimous, else basis for qiyas; rational evidence as qiyas.
The commentator's response shows the comprehensive nature of the four.
5
Synthesize: the role of Qiyas
Note that Qiyas is derived from the first three and is a tool for extracting rulings from them. This establishes the four as the complete and sufficient set for istinbat.
Qiyas is the mechanism to extend rulings to new cases.

مُسْتَنْبَطَةٍ مِن مَوَارِدِ الكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالإجمَاعِ فَالحُكمُ بِالتَّحقِيقِ مُسْتَنِدٌ إِلَيْهَا وَأَثَرُ القِيَاسِ فِى إظهَارِ الحُكمِ وَتَغييرِ وَصفِهِ مِن الخُصُوص إِلَى العُمُومِ وَمِن هُنَا يُقَالُ أُصول الفقهِ ثَلاثَةُ الكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةُ وَالإِجْمَاعُ وَالأَصلُ الرَّابِعُ القِيَاسُ المُسْتَنْبَطُ مِن هَذِهِ الْأُصُولِ الثَّلَاثَهِ

تشریح : قولہ اصول الفقہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شاری ماقبیل سے ربط بیان کرتا ہے کہ پہلے اصول فقہ کی تعریف تھی اب مصداق بیان کرتے ہیں اور وہ چار چیزیں ہیں (۱) کتاب اللہ (۲) سنت رسول اللہ (۳) اجتماع (۴) قیاس۔
اصول اربعہ کی وجہ حصر
وجہ ضبطہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ان چاروں کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا ہے اور شاریخ نے دو وجہ حصر بیان کی ہیں لیکن وجہ حصر سے قبل ایک مقدمہ بطور تمہید کے سمجھیں کہ وحی متلو کسے کہتے ہیں؟ عند البعض وحی متلو وہ کلام ہے جس کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت جبریل علیہ السلام پر پڑھا ہو اور جبریل علیہ السلام نے جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر پڑھا ہو اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے امت پر پڑھا ہو اور عند البعض وحی متلو وہ کلام ہے کہ جس کے ساتھ احکام متعلق ہوں اور وہ نمازوں کے اندر پڑھا جاتا ہو اور حدث اکبر میں پڑھنا جائز نہ ہو حدث اصغر کی حالت میں چھونا جائز نہ ہو وغیرڈ لک اب تمہید کے بعد وجد حصر سمجھیں۔
وجہ حصر اول :۔ کہ دلیل شرعی وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی اگر وحی ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں وحی متلو ہوگی یا غیر متلو اگر وحی متلو ہو تو کتاب اللہ ہے اور اگر غیر متلو ہو تو حدیث ہے اور اگر دلیل شرعی غیر وحی ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک زمانہ کے علماء کا اتفاق ہوگا یا نہیں ہو گا اگر اتفاق ہو تو اجماع ہے اور اگر اتفاق نہ ہو تو قیا میں ہے۔
دوسری وجہ حضر: دلیل شرعی دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہم تک نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے واسطے سے پہنچی ہوگی یا بغیر واسطہ کے اگر واسطہ کے ساتھ ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں صفت اعجاز کا اعتبار ہوگا یعنی معجز ہوگی یا معجز نہیں ہوگی اگر صفت اعجاز کا اعتبار ہے تو قرآن ہے ورنہ سنت رسول اللہ اللہ ہے اور اگر نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کے واسطے کے بغیر پہنچی ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں جس سے دلیل صادر ہوتی ہے اس میں عصمت عن الخفاء پائی جائینگی یا عصمت عن الخطا نہیں ہوگی اگر عصمت عن الخطاء ہو تو اجماع ہے ورنہ قیاس ہے۔
شرائع من قبلنا، تعامل الناس ، قول صحابی ، دلیل عقلی وغیرہ اصول اربعہ میں داخل ہیں
و اما شرائع من :۔ یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے شارخ نے اس عبارت میں سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ دلائل شرعیہ کو چار میں بند کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کے علاوہ بھی کئی دلیلیں ہیں جن سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے مثلاً پہلی امتوں کی شریعت کے احکام اگر قرآن وحدیث میں مذکور ہوں اور انکار نہ کیا گیا ہو تو امت محمدیہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لئے ان احکام پر عمل کرنا لازم ہے اب دلیل پہلی امت کی شریعت ہے ایسے ہی لوگوں کا تعامل دلیل بن جاتا ہے مثلاً مصر کے قراء حضرات ضاد کی بجائے دال پڑھتے ہیں یہ لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے نماز کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں تو تعامل الناس دلیل شرعی ہوئی کبھی صحابی کا قول دلیل بن جاتا ہے حالانکہ یہ قول قرآن وحدیث اور اجماع و قیاس میں نہیں ہے اسی طرح ایک
Derived from the sources of the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, so the ruling in reality is based on them. And the effect of analogy is in manifesting the ruling and changing its description from particularity to generality. Hence it is said: The principles of fiqh are three: the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus; and the fourth principle is analogy, which is derived from these three principles.
Translation: What has passed was an explanation of the meaning of usul al-fiqh, and this is an explanation of that to which this meaning applies, from among the types that are restricted by the rule of induction to four. And the reason for restriction is that indeed the legal evidence is either revelation or non-revelation. If it is revealed recitation (wahy matlu), then it is the Book of Allah; otherwise it is the Sunnah. And if it is non-revelation, then either it is the consensus of all mujtahids of one age, so it is ijma; otherwise it is qiyas. Or: indeed the evidence will reach us either with the intermediary of the Messenger of Allah or without. If with intermediary, then if it has the attribute of miraculousness in its wording, it is the Qur'an; otherwise it is the Sunnah. If without intermediary, then if the person from whom it emanates is protected from error, it is ijma; otherwise it is qiyas. And in all cases, the laws of previous nations, the practice of people, the statement of a Companion, and the like revert to these four. Similarly, rational evidence is one of their types; otherwise, there is no room for opinion in establishing rulings. And whoever counted rational evidence as a fifth type from among the evidences and called it istidlal, then its outcome is [لوشیا?] of adhering to a rational text or consensus, which is specified with it in rulings. Then the first three are absolute principles because they are independent evidences that establish rulings, and qiyas is a principle in one respect because the ruling is attributed to it apparently, and in one respect because it is a branch for [تقدیر?] because its cause is derived from the sources of the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. So the ruling is certainly attributed to those causes, and the effect of qiyas is in manifesting the ruling and changing its description from particularity to generality. Thus it is said that the principles of fiqh are three: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, and consensus; and the fourth principle is qiyas which is derived from these three principles.
Commentary: He said "Principles of Fiqh": This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The commentator explains the connection from the previous discussion: previously there was a definition of usul al-fiqh; now he mentions the referent (musaddaq) and they are four things: (1) the Book of Allah, (2) the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, (3) consensus, (4) qiyas.
The reason for restricting to four principles: Justification: This is the second part of the commentary's phrase. The commentator intends to explain the reason for restricting to these four, and he mentions two reasons. But before the reason, we should understand a preliminary: What is wahy matlu? According to some, wahy matlu is speech that Allah recited to Jibril (peace be upon him), and Jibril recited to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the Prophet recited to the Ummah. According to some, wahy matlu is speech to which rulings are attached and which is recited in prayers, and which cannot be recited in major impurity, and cannot be touched in minor impurity, etc. Now after the preliminary, understand the reason for restriction.
First reason: Legal evidence is either revelation or non-revelation. If revelation, then it is either wahy matlu or not. If wahy matlu, then it is the Book of Allah; if not, then it is hadith. If legal evidence is non-revelation, then it is either the agreement of the scholars of one age or not. If agreement, then it is ijma; if not, then it is qiyas.
Second reason: Legal evidence is either reaching us through the intermediary of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or without intermediary. If with intermediary, then it is either miraculous in attribute or not. If miraculous, then it is the Qur'an; otherwise it is the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. If it reached us without the intermediary of the Prophet, then it is either the person from whom the evidence emanates is protected from error or not. If protected from error, then it is ijma; otherwise it is qiyas.
As for the laws of previous nations, the practice of people, the statement of a Companion, rational evidence, etc., they are included in the four principles.
And as for the laws of previous nations: This is the third part of the phrase. The commentator here answers a presumed question. The question is: That restricting legal evidences to four is not correct because besides them there are many evidences that are used, such as the laws of previous nations if mentioned in Qur'an and hadith and not rejected, then it is obligatory for this Ummah to act upon them, so the evidence is the law of the previous nation. Similarly, the practice of people becomes evidence, e.g., the reciters of Egypt pronounce daal instead of daad, they consider prayer permissible due to the practice of people, so 'amal al-nas is legal evidence. Sometimes the statement of a Companion becomes evidence, although it is not from Qur'an, hadith, ijma, or qiyas. Similarly, one...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the sources of Islamic law (usul al-fiqh) within the Hanafi tradition. It opens by stating that analogy (qiyas) is derived from the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma), and that the ruling is ultimately based on these. The legal effect of qiyas is to manifest a ruling and to extend it from a specific case to a general one. The author then asserts that the principles are three, plus a fourth derived from them. The Urdu commentary expands on this by explaining that the meaning of usul al-fiqh is now being fleshed out with its actual referents (musaddaq), which are limited to four by induction (istiqra'). The commentator provides two logical divisions to prove this restriction. The first division: legal evidence is either revelation (wahy) or non-revelation. Revelation is either recited (matlu) → Quran, or non-recited → Sunnah. Non-revelation is either the consensus of all mujtahids of one era → Ijma, or else → Qiyas. The second division: evidence reaches us either through the Prophet (saw) or without. If through the Prophet, it either has the attribute of miraculousness (i'jaz) in its wording → Quran, or not → Sunnah. If without the Prophet, the source either is infallible (ma'sum) → Ijma, or not → Qiyas. This shows that all possible sources are exhausted by these four. The passage then addresses a potential objection: what about the laws of previous nations, the practice of people (ta'amul), the statement of a Companion, and rational evidence? The commentator responds that these are not independent sources but are subsumed under the four. For example, the laws of previous nations, if mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah and not abrogated, are evidence through the Quran or Sunnah, not independently. Similarly, the practice of people (urf) is considered only if it does not contradict a primary text, and it functions as evidence through istihsan or as a specific application of qiyas. The statement of a Companion is considered either as ijma if there is no disagreement, or as a basis for qiyas. Rational evidence (aql) is not an independent source; it is used to derive rulings through ijtihad and qiyas. Thus, the fourth source, qiyas, encompasses all inferential methods. The passage thus firmly establishes the Hanafi position that the foundations of jurisprudence are limited to these four, with qiyas being an essential tool derived from the first three.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction: transferring a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).
وحى متلو (wahy matlu): Recited revelation: speech that is recited verbatim in worship, i.e., the Quran.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of all mujtahids of a generation on a legal ruling.
تعامل الناس (ta'amul al-nas): The prevalent practice of people, considered as evidence when consistent with Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four fundamental usul al-fiqh?
A) The Quran
B) The Sunnah
C) Ijma
D) Qawl al-Sahabi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts the sources of law to four: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, with all other evidences subsumed under them.

Two Rational Methods for Confining the Four Sources
Explains two rational reasons for limiting shar'i proofs to four.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply two rational methods to classify any shar'i proof into one of the four Hanafi sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).

Core Idea
The four sources are not arbitrary—they are derived by dividing all proofs first by mode of revelation and second by chain of transmission.

This passage from al-Tarweeh explains why the Hanafi school recognizes only four sources of Islamic law. The commentator presents two rational divisions that exhaust all possibilities, showing that every shar'i proof falls into either Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas. Understanding this classification is key to the Hanafi usul framework.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish wahy and non-wahy proofs
Begin by dividing all shar'i proofs into those that are divinely revealed (wahy) and those that are not (non-wahy). This is the first bifurcation.
Wahy includes both Quran and Sunnah.
2
Subdivide wahy into matlu and ghayr matlu
Within wahy, separate into wahy matlu (recited revelation, i.e., Quran) and wahy ghayr matlu (non-recited revelation, i.e., Sunnah).
Wahy matlu is unique to the Quran.
3
Subdivide non-wahy into ijma and qiyas
Non-wahy proofs are either based on the agreement of scholars of a time (ijma) or on analogical reasoning (qiyas).
No other category remains.
4
Apply the second method by considering the intermediary
Alternatively, divide proofs by whether they come through the Prophet (with or without miraculous quality) or directly (via infallible or non-infallible source).
This yields the same four sources.
5
Verify exhaustiveness
Check that every conceivable shar'i proof fits into one of the four categories. Both methods show that no proof can belong to a fifth source.
This rational defense underlies the Hanafi insistence on four sources.

اصول اربعہ کی وجہ حصر
وجہ ضبطہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ان چاروں کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا ہے اور شاریخ نے دو وجہ حصر بیان کی ہیں لیکن وجہ حصر سے قبل ایک مقدمہ بطور تمہید کے سمجھیں کہ وحی متلو کسے کہتے ہیں؟ عند البعض وحی متلو وہ کلام ہے جس کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت جبریل علیہ السلام پر پڑھا ہو اور جبریل علیہ السلام نے جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر پڑھا ہو اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے امت پر پڑھا ہو اور عند البعض وحی متلو وہ کلام ہے کہ جس کے ساتھ احکام متعلق ہوں اور وہ نمازوں کے اندر پڑھا جاتا ہو اور حدث اکبر میں پڑھنا جائز نہ ہو حدث اصغر کی حالت میں چھونا جائز نہ ہو وغیرڈ لک اب تمہید کے بعد وجد حصر سمجھیں۔
وجہ حصر اول :۔ کہ دلیل شرعی وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی اگر وحی ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں وحی متلو ہوگی یا غیر متلو اگر وحی متلو ہو تو کتاب اللہ ہے اور اگر غیر متلو ہو تو حدیث ہے اور اگر دلیل شرعی غیر وحی ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک زمانہ کے علماء کا اتفاق ہوگا یا نہیں ہو گا اگر اتفاق ہو تو اجماع ہے اور اگر اتفاق نہ ہو تو قیا میں ہے۔

The Relief for the Solution of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. The Reason for Confining the Four Sources. Explanation: This is the second part of the text. The commentator intends to explain the reason for confining these four. The commentator mentions two reasons for confinement. Before that, as a preamble, know: what is wahy matlu? According to some, wahy matlu is speech that Allah recited to Jibril, Jibril recited to the Messenger, and the Messenger recited to the ummah. According to others, wahy matlu is speech to which rulings are attached, recited in prayers, not permissible to recite in major impurity, not permissible to touch in minor impurity, etc. Now after the preamble, understand the two reasons. First reason for confinement: A shar'i proof is either wahy or non-wahy. If it is wahy, it is either wahy matlu or non-matlu. If wahy matlu, it is the Book of Allah; if non-matlu, it is hadith. If it is non-wahy, then either there is agreement of the scholars of a time (ijma) or not (qiyas). Second reason: A shar'i proof either reaches us through the Prophet or without an intermediary. If with an intermediary, then either it has the quality of i'jaz (miraculous) or not; if miraculous, it is the Quran, otherwise the Sunnah. If without an intermediary, then either the source has infallibility from error or not; if infallible, it is ijma, otherwise qiyas.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining why the Hanafi usul only recognizes four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). The author presents two rational (aqli) arguments for this confinement. The first argument divides all proofs into wahy (divine revelation) and non-wahy. Wahy is further divided into matlu (recited, i.e., Quran) and ghayr matlu (non-recited, i.e., Sunnah). Non-wahy is either based on scholarly consensus (ijma) or analogical reasoning (qiyas). The second argument considers whether the proof came via the Prophet or not. If via the Prophet, it is either miraculous (Quran) or not (Sunnah). If not via the Prophet, it is either from an infallible source (ijma) or not (qiyas). The reasoning shows that all valid proofs are subsumed under these four categories. This is a foundational usul rule in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وحی متلو (wahy matlu): Revelation that is recited as part of worship, i.e., the Quran.
وحی غیر متلو (wahy ghayr matlu): Revelation that is not recited as part of worship, i.e., hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first reason for confinement, if a shar'i proof is non-wahy, what are the two possibilities?
A) Quran or Sunnah
B) Ijma or Qiyas
C) Wahy matlu or ghayr matlu
D) Miracle or no miracle

Key Takeaway
The four sources of Islamic law are exhaustively derived by rational division: all shar'i proofs are either wahy (Quran/Sunnah) or non-wahy (ijma/qiyas).

Conditions of a Legal Proof and Scope of Usul al-Fiqh
Stating conditions for a dalil and debating scope of usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions for a valid legal proof in Hanafi usul and explain how usul al-fiqh applies to both mujtahids and muqallids.

Core Idea
A proof is valid only if unabrogated, unopposed, and based on valid ijtihad; usul al-fiqh guides both mujtahids and muqallids.

This passage from al-Tawdih clarifies that a legal proof (dalil) does not automatically establish a ruling; it must meet specific conditions. The text then addresses a key question: is the science of usul al-fiqh only for mujtahids, or can it also benefit muqallids? By understanding these points, you will grasp the foundational rules that govern how rulings are derived and applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
The passage states that a proof must: (1) have its own conditions, (2) not be abrogated, and (3) have no equal or superior opponent. Additionally, if qiyas is involved, it must be based on a mujtahid's opinion and not contradict ijma.
These conditions are studied in their proper places within usul.
2
Understand why these conditions form universal premises
The conditions are like universal propositions that, when applied to specific evidence, yield fiqh rulings. Knowledge of these conditions is itself part of usul al-fiqh.
Each condition corresponds to a discussion (mabhas) in usul texts.
3
Recognize the two views on the scope of usul al-fiqh
One view restricts usul to mujtahids because only they derive from the four proofs. Another view includes muqallids, since they rely on the mujtahid's statement as their 'proof'.
The author leans toward the inclusive view, noting that taqlid and istifta' are discussed in some usul works.
4
Analyze the muqallid's 'proof'
For a muqallid, the proof is the statement of the mujtahid. The muqallid verifies that the mujtahid's opinion is the correct one, and this verification is a form of istidlal (inference).
Thus, the muqallid also benefits from usul rules that help assess the reliability of the mujtahid's opinion.
5
Define usul al-fiqh based on the passage
The passage concludes: 'Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of the rules by which one reaches the issues of fiqh.' This definition accommodates both the mujtahid (directly) and the muqallid (indirectly).
The phrase 'on the basis of verification' (tahqiq) applies to the muqallid's practice of following a mujtahid with conviction.
