ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ أَنَّ كُلَّ دَلِيلٍ مِنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ إِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ بِهِ الْحُكْمُ إِذَا كَانَ مُشْتَمِلًا عَلَى شَرَائِطَ تُذْكَرُ فِي مَوْضِعِهَا، وَلَا يَكُونُ الدَّلِيلُ مَنْسُوخًا، وَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ مُعَارِضٌ مُسَاوٍ أَوْ رَاجِحٌ. وَيَكُونُ الْقِيَاسُ قَدْ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأْيُ مُجْتَهِدٍ حَتَّى لَوْ خَالَفَ إِجْمَاعَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ يَكُونُ بَاطِلًا فَالْقَضِيَّةُ الْمَذْكُورَةُ سَوَاءٌ جَعَلْنَاهَا كُبْرَى أَوْ مُلَازِمَةً إِنَّمَا تَصْدُقُ كُلِّيَّةً إِذَا اشْتَمَلَتْ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْقُيُودِ فَالْعِلْمُ بِالْمَبَاحِثِ الْمُتَعَلِّقَةِ بِهَذِهِ الْقُيُودِ يَكُونُ عِلْمًا بِالْقَضِيَّةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَيِ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ فَتَكُونُ تِلْكَ الْمَبَاحِثُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَقَوْلُنَا يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَيْهِ. الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّ هَذَا يَخْتَصُّ بِالْمُجْتَهِدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَبْحُوثَ عَنْهُ فِي هَذَا الْعِلْمِ قَوَاعِدُ يَتَوَصَّلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ فَإِنَّ الْمُتَوَصِّلَ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ لَيْسَ إِلَّا الْمُجْتَهِدُ فَإِنَّ الْفِقْهَ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْأَحْكَامِ مِنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ الَّتِي لَيْسَ دَلِيلُ الْمُقَلِّدِ مِنْهَا فَلِهَذَا لَمْ تُذْكَرْ مَبَاحِثُ التَّقْلِيدِ وَالِاسْتِفْتَاءِ فِي كُتُبِنَا وَلَا يَبْعُدُ أَنْ يُقَالَ إِنَّهُ يَعُمُّ الْمُجْتَهِدَ وَالْمُقَلِّدَ وَالْأَدِلَّةُ الْأَرْبَعَةُ إِنَّمَا يَتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا الْمُجْتَهِدُ لَا الْمُقَلِّدُ فَأَمَّا الْمُقَلِّدُ فَالدَّلِيلُ عِنْدَهُ قَوْلُ الْمُجْتَهِدِ فَالْمُقَلِّدُ يَقُولُ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ وَاقِعٌ عِنْدِي؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأْيُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَكُلُّ مَا أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأْيُهُ فَهُوَ وَاقِعٌ عِنْدِي فَالْقَضِيَّةُ الثَّانِيَةُ مِنْ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ أَيْضًا فَلِهَذَا ذَكَرَ بَعْضُ الْعُلَمَاءِ فِي كُتُبِ الْأُصُولِ مَبَاحِثَ التَّقْلِيدِ وَالِاسْتِفْتَاءِ فَعَلَى هَذَا عِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ، وَلَا يُقَالُ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ؛ لِأَنَّ الْفِقْهَ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْأَحْكَامِ مِنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَقَوْلُنَا عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّحْقِيقِ لَا يُنَافِي هَذَا الْمَعْنَى فَإِنَّ تَحْقِيقَ الْمُقَلِّدِ أَنْ يُقَلِّدَ مُجْتَهِدًا يَعْتَقِدُ ذَلِكَ الْمُقَلِّدُ حَقِيقَةَ رَأْيِ ذَلِكَ الْمُجْتَهِدِ
Then know that every proof from the legal proofs only establishes the ruling when it includes conditions that are mentioned in their place, and that the proof is not abrogated, and that it has no equal or superior opponent. And the analogy (qiyas) must be such that the opinion of a mujtahid has led to it, such that if it contradicts the consensus (ijma') of the mujtahids, it is invalid. So the mentioned proposition, whether we make it the major premise or a necessary entailment, is only true universally when it includes these restrictions. So knowledge of the discussions related to these restrictions is knowledge of the universal proposition which is one of the two premises of the proof regarding the issues of fiqh. Thus those discussions become from the issues of usul al-fiqh. And our statement 'by which one reaches it' — apparently this is specific to the mujtahid, because what is investigated in this discipline are rules by which the mujtahid reaches fiqh, because the one who reaches fiqh is only the mujtahid, since fiqh is knowledge of rulings from proofs among which the muqallid's proof is not included. For this reason, the discussions of taqlid and istifta' are not mentioned in our books. And it is not far to say that it encompasses both the mujtahid and the muqallid. The four proofs are only reached by the mujtahid, not the muqallid. As for the muqallid, his proof is the statement of the mujtahid. So the muqallid says: 'This ruling is established in my opinion because the opinion of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, has led to it, and everything his opinion has led to is established in my opinion.' So the second proposition is also from usul al-fiqh. For this reason, some scholars have mentioned the topics of taqlid and istifta' in books of usul. Therefore, the science of usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of the rules by which one reaches the issues of fiqh, and it is not said 'to fiqh' because fiqh is knowledge of rulings from proofs, and our statement 'on the basis of verification' does not contradict this meaning, for the verification of the muqallid is that he follows a mujtahid whom he believes is the true opinion of that mujtahid.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage from the matn of al-Tawdih lays out the conditions for a legal proof to establish a ruling: the proof must be valid (with its conditions), not abrogated, have no equal or stronger opposing evidence, and the analogy must be based on the ijtihad of a mujtahid. If it contradicts the consensus of mujtahids, it is invalid. These conditions are studied in usul al-fiqh because they are the universal premises used to derive rulings. The author then discusses whether usul al-fiqh is specific to mujtahids or includes muqallids. He notes that the apparent meaning is that it is specific to mujtahids because fiqh is knowledge from proofs, and a muqallid does not derive from the four proofs but from the statement of a mujtahid. However, some scholars include topics of taqlid and istifta' in usul al-fiqh, and the author does not consider it far-fetched, explaining that the muqallid's 'proof' is the mujtahid's opinion, and his knowledge of that opinion is also a kind of verification. Thus usul al-fiqh can encompass both.

Key Terms
الدليل (al-dalīl): A legal proof from the four sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) that establishes a ruling.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who is capable of deriving rulings directly from the four proofs.
المقلد (al-muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid without deriving directly from proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for a legal proof to establish a ruling?
A) The proof must include its own conditions.
B) The proof must not be abrogated.
C) The proof must be transmitted by a single narrator.
D) The proof must have no equal or superior opponent.

Key Takeaway
A legal proof is only valid if it is not abrogated, has no equal or stronger opponent, and its qiyas is based on valid ijtihad; usul al-fiqh serves both mujtahids and muqallids, as the muqallid's proof is the mujtahid's statement.

The Hanafi Definition of the Quran as the First Source of Law
usul_definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Quran and identify which types of texts are excluded by each element of the definition.

Core Idea
The Quran is only what is transmitted between the covers of the mus'haf by tawatur – nothing else.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the first source of law is the Quran. But what exactly counts as 'Quran'? This lesson unpacks the technical definition that separates the Quran from other divine texts like hadith qudsi, prophetic hadith, and irregular readings. You will also encounter a logical objection to this definition and consider how later scholars addressed it.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three components of the definition
From the Arabic: 'maa nukila ilayna bayna daffatay al-masahif tawaturan'. Identify the three conditions: (1) transmitted to us, (2) between the covers of the mus'haf, (3) by tawatur.
2
Apply each component to excluded texts
Read the exclusion list: 'all other books, divine and prophetic hadiths, and irregular readings'. Map each exclusion to the condition that eliminates it. For example, 'between the covers of the mus'haf' excludes hadith qudsi and prophetic hadith.
Irregular readings (qira'at shadhdhah) are excluded by the condition of tawatur.
3
Analyze the circularity objection
Ibn al-Hajib argues that the definition is circular: it defines Quran by mus'haf and mus'haf by Quran. Consider why this is problematic and how you might rephrase the definition to avoid the circle.
The commentator does not provide a response here; later Hanafi texts resolve this by defining mus'haf independently (e.g., 'a codex containing the Quran').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَتَضَعُ الْكِتَابَ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ القِسْمُ الأوَّلُ فِي الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَهِيَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَرْكَانِ : الرُّكُنُ الْأَوَّلُ فِي الْكِتَابِ أَى الْقُرْآنِ ، وَهُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا بَيْنَ دَلَّتَيْ الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا) فَخَرَجَ سَائِرُ الْكُتُبِ وَالْأَحَادِيثِ الْإِلَهِيَّةِ وَالنَّبَوِيَّةِ وَالْقِرَاءَاتِ الشَّادّةِ ، وَقَدْ أَوْرَدَ ابْنُ الْحَاجِبِ أَنْ هَذَا التعريف دَورِيٌّ ؛ لأنَّهُ عَرَّفَ الْقُرْآنَ بِمَا نُقِلَ فِي الْمُصْحَفِ ، فَإِنْ سُئِلَ مَا الْمُصْحَفِ فَلا بُدَّ أَنْ يُقَالَ الَّذِي كُتِبَ فِيهِ الْقُرْآنُ
So he divides the book into two parts. The first part is on the legal proofs, and they are four pillars: The first pillar is on the Book, i.e., the Quran, and it is what has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'haf by tawatur. Thus all other books, divine and prophetic hadiths, and irregular readings are excluded. Ibn al-Hajib has objected that this definition is circular because it defined the Quran as what is transmitted in the mus'haf; if one asks 'what is the mus'haf?', one must say 'that in which the Quran is written'.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the Quran as the first source of law (al-adillah al-shar'iyyah) in a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. The author (likely the matn writer) divides the book into two parts, the first being on legal proofs subdivided into four pillars: the Quran, the Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. Here only the Quran is defined. The definition includes three key elements: (1) it is transmitted to us (nuqila ilayna) - so it is not something discovered by reason; (2) between the two covers of the mus'haf - so it is not the unrecited divine speech (kalam nafsi) nor the hadith qudsi; (3) by tawatur - so isolated transmissions (ahad) are excluded. The result excludes all other books (like the Torah and Injil), divinely inspired sayings (ahadith qudsiyyah), prophetic hadith, and irregular qira'at (shadhdhah). Then the commentator notes that Ibn al-Hajib (a Maliki usuli) criticized this definition as circular: the Quran is defined by what is in the mus'haf, but the mus'haf is defined as that which contains the Quran. This objection is recorded but not answered here; later texts typically refine the definition to avoid circularity.

Key Terms
مصحف (mus'haf): The physical codex in which the Quran is written, consisting of two covers and pages.
تواتر (tawatur): Transmission by a large number of narrators such that collusion on a lie is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
قراءات شاذة (qira'at shadhdhah): Irregular readings that do not meet the conditions of tawatur, thus not part of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is excluded from the definition of the Quran according to this passage?
A) The Torah
B) Sunnah mutawatirah
C) Irregular readings
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Quran is defined by three conditions: tawatur, preservation between the covers of the mus'haf, and exclusive revelation to the Prophet – this excludes all other divine and prophetic texts.

Al-Quran as Source

10 min
Definition of the Qur'an and Refutation of Circularity
Defining the Qur'an and refuting circularity objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of the Qur'an and evaluate the response to Ibn al-Hajib's circularity objection.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is defined as mutawatir transmission between mus'haf covers — a specification, not a definition of essence, avoiding circularity.

In this passage, the author presents the foundational Hanafi definition of the Qur'an as the mutawatir transmitted text between the covers of mus'hafs. He then addresses a sophisticated objection from Ibn al-Hajib that the definition is circular. By understanding the distinction between a definition of essence (mahiyya) and a specification (tashkhis), and the role of custom (urf) in knowing what a mus'haf is, you will see why the Hanafi school defends this definition and how it serves as a precise identification of the primary source of law.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
Identify the exact formulation: 'that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'hafs by tawatur.' Note what it includes and excludes.
Excludes previous scriptures, hadith qudsi, hadith nabawi, irregular qira'at.
2
Understand the objection
Recognize Ibn al-Hajib's claim of circularity: the definition uses mus'haf, which itself needs definition by the Qur'an.
This is a classic objection in usul al-fiqh.
3
Follow the Hanafi response (Part 1): Custom
Mus'haf is known by custom (urf), so it does not require a formal definition; hence no circularity.
Custom (urf) is a valid source of knowledge in Hanafi usul.
4
Follow the Hanafi response (Part 2): Specification vs. Essence
The definition is not of the essence (mahiyya) but a specification (tashkhis) to disambiguate the homonym 'Qur'an'. Circularity would only arise if essence were defined.
This is the key analytical move.
5
Apply to homonymy
Realize that the word 'Qur'an' has two meanings: eternal attribute and recited words. The definition picks the latter, which is transmitted in mus'hafs.
Homonymy (ishtirak) is a common feature in Arabic.

Source Text

فَتَضَعُ الْكِتَابَ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ القِسْمُ الأوَّلُ فِي الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَهِيَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَرْكَانِ : الرُّكُنُ الْأَوَّلُ فِي الْكِتَابِ أَى الْقُرْآنِ ، وَهُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا بَيْنَ دَلَّتَيْ الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا) فَخَرَجَ سَائِرُ الْكُتُبِ وَالْأَحَادِيثِ الْإِلَهِيَّةِ وَالنَّبَوِيَّةِ وَالْقِرَاءَاتِ الشَّادّةِ ، وَقَدْ أَوْرَدَ ابْنُ الْحَاجِبِ أَنْ هَذَا التعريف دَورِيٌّ؛ لأنَّهُ عَرَّفَ الْقُرْآنَ بِمَا نُقِلَ فِي الْمُصْحَفِ ، فَإِنْ سُئِلَ مَا الْمُصْحَفِ فَلا بُدَّ أَنْ يُقَالَ الَّذِي كُتِبَ فِيهِ الْقُرْآنُ
فَأَجَبْت عَنْ هَذَا بِقَوْلِى ) وَلَا دَوْرَ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمُصْحَفَ مَعْلُومٌ أَيْ فِي الْعُرْفِ قَلا يَحْتَاجُ إلَى تَعْرِيفِهِ بِقَوْلِهِ الَّذِى كُتِبَ فِيهِ الْقُرْآنُ ثُمَّ أَرَدْت تَحْقِيقًا فِي هَذَا الْمَوْضِعِ لِيُعْلَمَ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفَ أَى نَوْعٍ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ التَّعْرِيفَاتِ فَإِنَّ إِثْمَامَ الْجَوَابِ مَوْقُوت عَلَى هَذَا فَقُلْت ( وَلَيْسَ هَذَا تَعْرِيفُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْكِتَابِ ) بَلْ تَشْخِيصُهُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ كِتَابٍ تُرِيدُ ، ( وَلَا الْقُرْآنِ) فَإِنَّ عُلَمَاء نَا قَالُوا هُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا إِلَخُ فَلَا يَخُلُو إِمَّا أَنْ عَرَّفُوا الْكِتَابَ بِهَذَا أَوْ عَرَّفُوا الْقُرْآنَ بِهَذَا ، فَإِنْ عَرَّفُوا الْكِتَابَ بِهَذَا فَلَيْسَ تَعْرِيفًا لِمَاهِيَّةِ الْكِتَابِ ، بَلْ تَشْخِيصَهُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيَّ كِتَابٍ تُرِيدُ وَإِنْ عَمَّلُوا الْقُرْآنَ بِهَذَا فَلَيْسَ تَعْرِيفًا لِمَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ أَيْضًا ، بَلْ تَشْخِيصَهُ ) لأنَّ الْقُرْآنَ اسْمٌ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْكَلَامِ الْأَزَلِيّ وَعَلَى الْمَقْرُوءٍ فَهَذَا تَعْيِينُ أَحَدٍ مُحْتَمَلَيْهِ ، وَهُوَ الْمَقْرُوءُ) فَإِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ لَفَةٌ مُشْتَرَى يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْكَلَامِ الْأَزَلِيِّ الَّذِى هُوَ صِفَةٌ لِلْحَقِّ عَزَّ وَعَلَا وَيُطْلَقُ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ ، وَهُوَ الْمَقْرُوءٍ فَكَأَنَّهُ قِيلَ أَيْ الْمَعْنَيَيْنِ تُرِيدُ ، فَقَالَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا إِلَخْ أَى نُرِيدُ الْمَقْرُوءِ فَعَلَى هَذَا لَا يَلْزَمُ الدَّورُ وَإِنَّمَا يَلْزَمُ الدَّورُ إِنْ أُرِيدَ تَعْرِيفُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ ; لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ عُرْف مَاهِيَّةَ الْقُرْآنِ بِالْمَكْتُوبِ فِى الْمُصْحَفِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنْ مَعْرِفَةِ مَاهِيَّةِ الْمُصْحَفِ فَلَا يَكْفِي حِينَئِذٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْمُصْحَفِ بِبَعْضِ الْوُجُوهِ كَالْإِشَارَةِ وَنَحْوِهَا ، ثُمَّ مَعْرِفَةُ مَاهِيَّةِ الْمُصْحَفِ مَوْقُوفَةٌ عَلَى مَعْرِفَةِ مَاهِيَّةِ الْقُرْآنِ ..
ترجمہ:۔ پس ہم رکھتے ہیں کتاب کو دو قسموں پر قسم اول اولہ شرعیہ (کے بیان ) میں ہے اور وہ (ادلہ ) چار ارکان پر (مشتمل) ہیں رکن اول کتاب یعنی قرآن میں ہے اور وہ ( قرآن ) وہ ہے جو نقل کیا گیا ہو ہماری طرف مصاحف کے دوستوں کے درمیان تو اتر کے ساتھ پس خارج ہو گئیں باقی تمام کتابیں اور احادیث قدسیہ اور نبویہ اور قراءات شاذہ ۔ اور تحقیق اعتراض کیا ابن حاجب نے کہ بیشک یہ تعریف دوری ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی مانقل فی المصاحف کے ساتھ پس اگر
Then he places the book into two divisions: the first division is on the legal proofs, and they are on four pillars: the first pillar is on the Book, i.e., the Qur'an, and it is that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'hafs by tawatur. So all other books, divine and prophetic hadiths, and irregular readings are excluded. And Ibn al-Hajib has raised the objection that this definition is circular; because he defined the Qur'an by what is transmitted in the mus'haf, for if asked: what is the mus'haf? It must be said: that in which the Qur'an is written.
I answered this by my statement: And there is no circularity, because the mus'haf is known, i.e., in custom, so it does not need to be defined by saying 'that in which the Qur'an is written'. Then I intended a verification at this place so that it is known what type of definition this is; for the completion of the answer depends on this. So I said: This is not a definition of the essence (mahiyya) of the Book, but rather its specification (tashkhis) in answer to 'which book do you intend?' Nor of the Qur'an; for our scholars said it is that which has been transmitted to us, etc. So it is either that they defined the Book by this, or they defined the Qur'an by this. If they defined the Book by this, then it is not a definition of the essence of the Book, but its specification in answer to 'which book do you intend?'. And if they defined the Qur'an by this, then it is also not a definition of the essence of the Qur'an, but its specification, because the word 'Qur'an' is applied to the eternal speech and to the recited (words); so this is a determination (ta'yin) of one of its two possibilities, namely the recited. For the word 'Qur'an' is a homonym (lafzh mushtarak) applied to the eternal speech which is an attribute of Allah Almighty, and also applied to that which indicates it, i.e., the recited. So it is as if it was said: which of the two meanings do you intend? So he said: that which has been transmitted to us, etc., meaning we intend the recited. Thus, on this basis, circularity does not follow. Rather, circularity would follow if a definition of the essence of the Qur'an were intended; because if the essence of the Qur'an were defined by what is written in the mus'haf, then knowledge of the essence of the mus'haf would be required, and then knowledge of the mus'haf by some means like pointing etc. would not suffice. Moreover, knowledge of the essence of the mus'haf is dependent on knowledge of the essence of the Qur'an.
Translation: So we place the book on two divisions: the first division is on the legal proofs, and they consist of four pillars: the first pillar is on the Book, i.e., the Qur'an, and it is that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'hafs by tawatur. So all other books, divine and prophetic hadiths, and irregular readings are excluded. And indeed Ibn al-Hajib raised the objection that this definition is circular, because he defined the Qur'an by what is transmitted in the mus'haf, so if asked: what is the mus'haf? It must be said: that in which the Qur'an is written. So if...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul al-fiqh definition: the Qur'an is defined as that which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'hafs by tawatur. This definition excludes all other revealed texts (previous scriptures, hadith qudsi, hadith nabawi, and irregular qira'at). The author then addresses an objection by Ibn al-Hajib that the definition is circular because it defines the Qur'an by what is in the mus'haf, and the mus'haf is defined by containing the Qur'an. The response is nuanced: the definition is not circular because the mus'haf is known by custom (urf) and does not require a formal definition. More importantly, the definition is not intended as a definition of the essence (mahiyya) of the Qur'an but as a specification (tashkhis) to disambiguate the homonym 'Qur'an' which can refer either to the eternal divine attribute (kalam azali) or to the recited words. By specifying 'that which has been transmitted...', the scholars are indicating the latter meaning. Therefore, no circularity arises because the definition does not aim to define the quiddity of the Qur'an but merely to identify which of its two meanings is intended. This is a classic Hanafi usul position that distinguishes between definition of essence and specification.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qur'an): That which has been transmitted to us between the two covers of the mus'hafs by tawatur; it is a homonym for both the eternal speech of Allah and the recited words.
مصحف (mus'haf): The physical collection of the written text of the Qur'an, known by custom (urf).
تعريف دوري (ta'rif dauri): A circular definition where the definiendum is defined by a term that itself requires the definiendum.
تواتر (tawatur): Continuous transmission by a large number of narrators in each generation, making certainty of the text's authenticity.
لفظ مشترك (lafzh mushtarak): A word that has more than one meaning (homonym).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the definition of the Qur'an as 'what is transmitted between the covers of mus'hafs by tawatur' not circular according to the Hanafi response?
A) Because mus'haf is defined by the Qur'an, so there is no circle.
B) Because mus'haf is known by custom (urf) and the definition is a specification (tashkhis), not a definition of essence.
C) Because the definition only includes the eternal speech, not the recited words.
D) Because Ibn al-Hajib's objection is invalid as he did not understand the definition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Qur'an as mutawatir transmission between mus'haf covers is a specification (tashkhis) that avoids circularity by reliance on custom and by not aiming to define the essence.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
Refuting Circularity in the Definition of Quran: The Role of Custom ('Urf)
First response to circularity objection using 'urf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of 'urf to explain why the Hanafi definition of Quran does not involve circularity.

Core Idea
The mushaf is known by custom, so defining Quran by reference to it does not create circularity.

This lesson examines the objection raised by Ibn al-Hajib against the standard Hanafi definition of the Quran. You will learn how the Hanafi school uses the concept of customary knowledge ('urf) to break the apparent circular dependency between 'Quran' and 'mushaf'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
State the Hanafi definition of Quran: 'That which is written between the two covers of the mushaf and transmitted via tawatur.'
This definition is from the matn in the source.
2
Understand the objection
Ibn al-Hajib argues that the definition is circular because 'mushaf' itself is defined by reference to Quran. If we ask 'What is mushaf?', the answer is 'That in which the Quran is written.' This creates a loop.
3
Analyze the first response
The Hanafi author replies that circularity does not follow because 'mushaf' is known by custom ('urf). In custom, the term 'mushaf' is well-understood and does not require a formal definition.
This response relies on the epistemological weight of 'urf in Hanafi usul.
4
Explain why the circle is broken
Since mushaf is known by custom, understanding it does not depend on understanding Quran. Thus the dependency is one-way (Quran depends on mushaf) but not reciprocal, so no circularity exists.
The second response (rasm) is covered in the next lesson.

سوال کیا جائے کہ مصحف کیا ہے؟ پس ضروری ہے کہ کہا جائے وہ ہے جس میں لکھا گیا ہو قرآن۔ پس میں نے جواب دیا اس اعتراض کا اپنے اس قول کے ساتھ اور نہیں لازم آتا دور کیونکہ مصحف معلوم ہے یعنی عرف میں پس نہیں ہے احتیاج اس کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اس کے قول الذي كتب فيه القرآن کے ساتھ۔ پھر میں نے ارادہ کیا تحقیق کرنے کا اس جگہ میں کہ بے شک یہ تعریف تعریفات کی قسموں میں سے کونسی قسم ہے کیونکہ جواب کا مکمل ہونا موقوف ہے اسی پر پس میں نے کہا اور نہیں ہے یہ تعریف ماہیت کتاب کی بلکہ کتاب کی تشخیص کی ہے ای کتاب ترید کے جواب میں اور نہ ہی قرآن کی ماہیت کی) کیونکہ ہمارے علماء نے کہا ہے کہ وہ ما نقل إلينا الخ ہے پس نہیں ہے خالی یا تو انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی اس طرح یا انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ۔ پس اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی یہ تو پھر نہیں ہے یہ تعریف کتاب کی ماہیت کی بلکہ اس (کتاب) کی تشخیص کی ہے ای کتاب ترید کے جواب میں۔ اور اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ پس نہیں ہے یہ تعریف قرآن کی ماہیت کی بھی بلکہ اس کی تشخیص کی ہے کیونکہ قرآن کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے کلام أزلی پر اور کلام مقروء پر۔ پس یہ (تعریف) متعین کرتا ہے اس کے دو احتمالوں میں سے ایک کو اور وہ کلام مقروء ہے کیونکہ قرآن ایسا لفظ ہے جو مشترک ہے بولا جاتا ہے اس کلام الہی پر وہ جو صفت ہے حق تعالیٰ عزوجل کی۔ اور نیز بولا جاتا ہے اس پر بھی جس پر وہ دلالت کرتا ہے اور وہ کلام مقروء ہے۔ پس گویا کہ کہا گیا دو معنوں میں سے کونسے معنی کا تو ارادہ کرتا ہے پس کہا کہ ما نقل إلينا آخر تک یعنی ہم ارادہ کرتے ہیں کلام مقروء کا۔ پس اس تفصیل پر نہیں لازم آتا دور اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ لازم آتا ہے دور اگر مراد لیا جائے ماہیت قرآن کی تعریف کیونکہ اگر تعریف کی جائے ماہیت قرآن کی بالمكتوب في المصاحف کے ساتھ پس ضروری ہوگی ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت اور نہیں ہے ممکن اس وقت ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت بعض وجوہ کے ساتھ جیسا کہ اشارہ اور اس کی مثل ہے پھر ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت موقوف ہے ماہیت قرآن کی معرفت پر۔

کتاب (تنقیح) میں اقسام مذکورہ کا بیان
فتضع الكتاب : ماتن نے یہاں سے کتاب کی اقسام یا اجزاء کتاب کو بیان کیا ہے کہ کتاب دو قسموں پر مشتمل ہے: قسم اول ادلہ شرعیہ یعنی کتاب اللہ، سنت رسول اللہ ﷺ وغیرہ کے بیان میں ہے اور قسم ثانی احکام کے بیان میں ہے۔ تو پہلے کتاب اللہ کی تعریف کی ہے: کتاب اللہ اور قرآن اس کو کہتے ہیں جو مصحف کے دفتین کے درمیان لکھا ہوا ہے اور تواتر کے ساتھ ہم تک پہنچا ہے۔ پھر فوائد و قیود ذکر کرتے ہیں کہ بين دفتي المصاحف کی قید سے احادیث قدسیہ اور مطلق احادیث خارج ہوگئیں کیونکہ وہ مكتوبة في المصاحف نہیں ہیں اور قراءات شاذة تواتر کی قید سے خارج ہو گئیں لیکن اس تعریف پر علامہ ابن حاجب نے اعتراض کیا ہے۔

التويج لحل التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويج
قرآن کی تعریف پر علامہ ابن حاجب کا اعتراض
اعتراض: یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف دور پر مشتمل ہے اس لئے کہ اس تعریف میں توقف الشيء علی نفسه لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ قرآن کی تعریف کو سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف کی تعریف پر اور اگر مصحف کے بارے میں پوچھا جائے تو کہا جائیگا ما كتب فيه القرآن تو قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا قرآن پر تو قرآن کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف ہو گیا اس لئے کہ شیء کے موقوف علیہ کا موقوف علیہ [مئی؟] کا موقوف علیہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ دور ہے اور دور باطل ہے تو مستلزم دور بھی باطل ہے۔ اس اعتراض کے ماتن نے جواب دیئے۔

جوابات اعتراضات ابن حاجب
جواب (1): یہ بھی جواب ہے کہ یہاں دور لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے کہ قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصحف عرف میں مشہور ہے اور مشہور کی تعریف نہیں ہوتی۔

جواب (2): یہ تحقیقی جواب ہے لیکن اس سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں۔

مقدمہ: تعریف دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس سے مقصود معرف کی ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہوگا یا مقصود صرف معرف کو ماعدا سے جدا کرنا ہوگا یعنی تعین تشخیص مقصود ہوگی۔ مثلا زید معرف ہے اور اس کی ماہیت حیوان ناطق ہے اور تشخیص کے بارے کہا جائیگا کہ فلاں جگہ رہتا ہے ایسا رنگ ہے اتنا قد ہے وغیرہ ذالک۔ تو اگر مقصود ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہو تو یہ حد ہے اور اگر تعریف تشخیص مقصود ہو تو یہ تعریف رسم ہے۔

حد اور رسم میں فرق: حد اور رسم میں کئی فرق ہیں: (۱) حد میں سوال ما حقیقیہ سے ہوگا اور رسم کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوگا۔ مثلا انسان کی تعریف حقیقی کریں گے تو سوال ہوگا ما الانسان اور اگر ماعدا سے امتیاز مقصود ہو تو کہیں گے أي بي الانسان۔ (۲) حد کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے اور رسم کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری نہیں۔ (۳) حد میں صرف اشارہ کافی نہیں ہوتا رسم میں صرف اشارہ کافی ہوتا ہے۔ حد میں ضروری ہے کہ حد کے جتنے اجزاء ہیں ان کی حقیقت بھی معلوم ہو اور رسم میں تمام اجزاء کی حقیقت معلوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔

اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ قرآن کی جو یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے یہ تعریف حد کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے بلکہ رسم کے قبیل سے ہے اس کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوتا ہے یعنی ما نقل إلينا الخ اگر کتاب کی تعریف ہو تو أي كتاب تريد کے سوال
If it is asked: What is mushaf? Then it is necessary to say: It is that in which the Quran is written. So I replied to this objection with my saying: And circularity is not necessary because mushaf is known, i.e., in custom, so there is no need to define it with his saying 'that in which the Quran is written'. Then I intended to investigate in this place that indeed this definition is which type among the types of definitions, because the completeness of the answer depends on it. So I said: And this definition is not the definition of the essence of the book, but rather it is the identification of the book, in answer to 'which book do you intend?' And nor is it the definition of the essence of the Quran, because our scholars said that it is 'what has been transmitted to us' etc. So it is not empty; either they defined the book in this way, or they defined the Quran in this way. If they defined the book in this way, then this is not the definition of the essence of the book, but rather its identification, in answer to 'which book do you intend?' And if they defined the Quran in this way, then this is not the definition of the essence of the Quran either, but rather its identification, because the word 'Quran' is applied to the eternal speech and to the recited speech. So this (definition) specifies one of its two probabilities, and that is the recited speech, because 'Quran' is a word that is shared: it is said of the divine speech which is an attribute of Allah Almighty, and it is also said of that which it indicates, which is the recited speech. So it is as if it was said: Of the two meanings, which meaning do you intend? So it was said: 'what has been transmitted to us' etc., i.e., we intend the recited speech. So based on this detail, circularity does not arise, and there is no exception except that circularity would arise if what is intended is the definition of the essence of the Quran, because if the essence of the Quran is defined by 'that which is written in the mushafs', then it would be necessary to know the essence of mushaf, and at that time it is not possible to know the essence of mushaf through some means like indication and the like, and then the knowledge of the essence of mushaf depends on the knowledge of the essence of the Quran.

Chapter: Mention of the aforementioned divisions in (al-Tanqih)
فتضع الكتاب: The matn has from here explained the divisions or parts of the book, that the book consists of two parts: the first part is about the Shariah proofs, i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), etc.; and the second part is about the rulings. So first he defined the Book of Allah: They call it the Book of Allah and the Quran, that which is written between the two covers of the mushaf and has reached us with tawatur. Then he mentions benefits and restrictions: the restriction 'between the covers of the mushafs' excludes hadith qudsi and absolute hadith, because they are not written in the mushafs; and the restriction 'tawatur' excludes the irregular readings (qira'at shadhdha). But on this definition, Allama Ibn al-Hajib raised an objection.

التويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج
Objection of Allama Ibn al-Hajib on the definition of Quran
Objection: This definition contains circularity, because in this definition the dependence of a thing upon itself becomes necessary: understanding the definition of Quran depends on the definition of mushaf, and if mushaf is asked about, it will be said: 'What is written in it is the Quran.' So understanding Quran depends on mushaf, and understanding mushaf depends on Quran, so understanding Quran depends on Quran, because the dependee of the dependee of a thing is its dependee. And this is circularity, and circularity is false, so what entails circularity is also false. The matn gave answers to this objection.

Answers to Ibn al-Hajib's objections
Answer (1): This is also an answer: that circularity does not arise here, because understanding Quran depends on mushaf, but understanding mushaf does not depend on Quran, because mushaf is well-known in custom, and what is well-known is not defined.

Answer (2): This is a research-based answer, but before it, understand a preamble as a preface.

Preamble: Definition is of two types, not free from either: either it intends to express the essence of the defined, or it intends merely to separate the defined from others, i.e., identification by specification. For example, Zayd is the defined, and his essence is 'rational animal', and regarding identification it will be said: he lives in such a place, has such a color, is such height, etc. So if the intention is to express the essence, it is a hadd; and if the intention is identification by definition, it is a rasm.

Difference between hadd and rasm: There are several differences between hadd and rasm: (1) In hadd, the question is with 'what is it in reality' (ma haqiqiyya), and regarding rasm, the question is about the thing itself. For example, if we give a real definition of man, the question is 'what is man?' (ma al-insan); but if the intention is distinction from others, we say 'which man' (ayy al-insan). (2) For hadd, it is necessary to mention genus and differentia; for rasm, it is not necessary to mention genus and differentia. (3) In hadd, mere indication is not sufficient; in rasm, mere indication is sufficient. In hadd, it is necessary that the reality of all its parts is known; in rasm, it is not necessary to know the reality of all parts.

After this preamble, understand that this definition of the Quran that has been given is not from the category of hadd, but from the category of rasm. Regarding it, the question is about the thing itself, i.e., 'what has been transmitted to us' etc. If it is a definition of the book, then the question is 'which book do you intend?'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of the Quran, addressing an objection of circularity raised by Ibn al-Hajib. The passage type is a dispute: Ibn al-Hajib argues that the definition 'the Quran is what is written between the two covers of the mushaf and transmitted via tawatur' involves circularity because 'mushaf' itself is defined as 'that in which the Quran is written', creating a dependency loop. The Hanafi author provides two responses. First, he argues that no circularity occurs because 'mushaf' is known by customary usage ('urf) and does not require definition; thus, understanding mushaf does not depend on defining Quran. Second, he offers a more sophisticated response distinguishing between two types of definitions: hadd (essential definition, expressing the reality of the thing) and rasm (descriptive definition, merely distinguishing the thing from others). He argues that the definition of the Quran as 'manqul ilayna' (what has been transmitted to us) is not a hadd but a rasm, intended to identify which of the two meanings of 'Quran' (eternal attribute or recited speech) is meant. Therefore, it does not require knowledge of the essence of mushaf. The author then explains the differences between hadd and rasm: hadd answers 'ma huwa' (what is it in essence), requires genus and differentia, and cannot rely on mere indication; rasm answers 'ayyu shay' (which thing), does not need genus and differentia, and can use indication. Applying this, the definition of the Quran as 'manqul ilayna' is a rasm, not a hadd, so it avoids circularity. This response is consistent with Hanafi usul methodology, which emphasizes 'urf and the practical function of definitions in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circularity in definition, where A depends on B and B depends on A, causing a logical loop.
حد (hadd): An essential definition that expresses the reality (mahiyyah) of a thing by mentioning its genus and differentia.
رسم (rasm): A descriptive definition that distinguishes the defined from others without necessarily stating its essence.
تشخیص (tashkhīṣ): Identification or specification of a particular thing among others, often used in definitions to answer 'which one?'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first Hanafi response to Ibn al-Hajib, why does the definition of Quran not involve circularity?
A) because mushaf is defined by custom
B) because the definition is a hadd
C) because Quran is eternal speech
D) because Ibn al-Hajib's objection is baseless

Key Takeaway
Customary knowledge of mushaf resolves the circularity objection, allowing a functional definition of Quran.

Al-Quran as Source

Hadd vs. Rasm: A Hanafi Framework for Evaluating Definitions
Second response using hadd vs rasm distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and rasm and apply this distinction to evaluate the validity of a definition in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A definition may be a rasm (descriptive identification) not a hadd (essential definition), which avoids circularity.

This lesson presents the second and more analytical response to Ibn al-Hajib's circularity objection. You will learn the key differences between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition) and how this distinction saves the Hanafi definition of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Recall the objection
Ibn al-Hajib claims the definition of Quran is circular because it depends on the definition of mushaf.
2
Understand the preamble
Definitions can aim to express the essence (hadd) or merely to identify the thing (rasm). Hadd answers 'what is it?', rasm answers 'which one?'
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply the distinction
The definition 'the Quran is what has been transmitted to us via tawatur' is a rasm, not a hadd. It specifies which meaning of 'Quran' (eternal speech or recited speech) is intended.
As a rasm, it does not require knowledge of the essence of mushaf.
4
Analyze why circularity is avoided
Since the definition is a rasm, it only needs to distinguish the Quran from other things. The reference to mushaf is part of that identification, and mushaf itself can be identified by custom. Thus no essential dependency loop arises.
5
List the differences between hadd and rasm
Hadd requires genus and differentia, and must express essence. Rasm only needs to identify, can use accidents, and mere indication suffices.
These differences are enumerated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال کیا جائے کہ مصحف کیا ہے؟ پس ضروری ہے کہ کہا جائے وہ ہے جس میں لکھا گیا ہو قرآن۔ پس میں نے جواب دیا اس اعتراض کا اپنے اس قول کے ساتھ اور نہیں لازم آتا دور کیونکہ مصحف معلوم ہے یعنی عرف میں پس نہیں ہے احتیاج اس کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اس کے قول الذي كتب فيه القرآن کے ساتھ۔ پھر میں نے ارادہ کیا تحقیق کرنے کا اس جگہ میں کہ بے شک یہ تعریف تعریفات کی قسموں میں سے کونسی قسم ہے کیونکہ جواب کا مکمل ہونا موقوف ہے اسی پر پس میں نے کہا اور نہیں ہے یہ تعریف ماہیت کتاب کی بلکہ کتاب کی تشخیص کی ہے ای کتاب ترید کے جواب میں اور نہ ہی قرآن کی ماہیت کی) کیونکہ ہمارے علماء نے کہا ہے کہ وہ ما نقل إلينا الخ ہے پس نہیں ہے خالی یا تو انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی اس طرح یا انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ۔ پس اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے کتاب کی یہ تو پھر نہیں ہے یہ تعریف کتاب کی ماہیت کی بلکہ اس (کتاب) کی تشخیص کی ہے ای کتاب ترید کے جواب میں۔ اور اگر انہوں نے تعریف کی ہے قرآن کی یہ پس نہیں ہے یہ تعریف قرآن کی ماہیت کی بھی بلکہ اس کی تشخیص کی ہے کیونکہ قرآن کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے کلام أزلی پر اور کلام مقروء پر۔ پس یہ (تعریف) متعین کرتا ہے اس کے دو احتمالوں میں سے ایک کو اور وہ کلام مقروء ہے کیونکہ قرآن ایسا لفظ ہے جو مشترک ہے بولا جاتا ہے اس کلام الہی پر وہ جو صفت ہے حق تعالیٰ عزوجل کی۔ اور نیز بولا جاتا ہے اس پر بھی جس پر وہ دلالت کرتا ہے اور وہ کلام مقروء ہے۔ پس گویا کہ کہا گیا دو معنوں میں سے کونسے معنی کا تو ارادہ کرتا ہے پس کہا کہ ما نقل إلينا آخر تک یعنی ہم ارادہ کرتے ہیں کلام مقروء کا۔ پس اس تفصیل پر نہیں لازم آتا دور اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ لازم آتا ہے دور اگر مراد لیا جائے ماہیت قرآن کی تعریف کیونکہ اگر تعریف کی جائے ماہیت قرآن کی بالمكتوب في المصاحف کے ساتھ پس ضروری ہوگی ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت اور نہیں ہے ممکن اس وقت ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت بعض وجوہ کے ساتھ جیسا کہ اشارہ اور اس کی مثل ہے پھر ماہیت مصحف کی معرفت موقوف ہے ماہیت قرآن کی معرفت پر۔

کتاب (تنقیح) میں اقسام مذکورہ کا بیان
فتضع الكتاب : ماتن نے یہاں سے کتاب کی اقسام یا اجزاء کتاب کو بیان کیا ہے کہ کتاب دو قسموں پر مشتمل ہے: قسم اول ادلہ شرعیہ یعنی کتاب اللہ، سنت رسول اللہ ﷺ وغیرہ کے بیان میں ہے اور قسم ثانی احکام کے بیان میں ہے۔ تو پہلے کتاب اللہ کی تعریف کی ہے: کتاب اللہ اور قرآن اس کو کہتے ہیں جو مصحف کے دفتین کے درمیان لکھا ہوا ہے اور تواتر کے ساتھ ہم تک پہنچا ہے۔ پھر فوائد و قیود ذکر کرتے ہیں کہ بين دفتي المصاحف کی قید سے احادیث قدسیہ اور مطلق احادیث خارج ہوگئیں کیونکہ وہ مكتوبة في المصاحف نہیں ہیں اور قراءات شاذة تواتر کی قید سے خارج ہو گئیں لیکن اس تعریف پر علامہ ابن حاجب نے اعتراض کیا ہے۔

التويج لحل التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويج
قرآن کی تعریف پر علامہ ابن حاجب کا اعتراض
اعتراض: یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف دور پر مشتمل ہے اس لئے کہ اس تعریف میں توقف الشيء علی نفسه لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ قرآن کی تعریف کو سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف کی تعریف پر اور اگر مصحف کے بارے میں پوچھا جائے تو کہا جائیگا ما كتب فيه القرآن تو قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا موقوف ہوا قرآن پر تو قرآن کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف ہو گیا اس لئے کہ شیء کے موقوف علیہ کا موقوف علیہ [مئی؟] کا موقوف علیہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ دور ہے اور دور باطل ہے تو مستلزم دور بھی باطل ہے۔ اس اعتراض کے ماتن نے جواب دیئے۔

جوابات اعتراضات ابن حاجب
جواب (1): یہ بھی جواب ہے کہ یہاں دور لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے کہ قرآن کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے مصحف پر اور مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصحف عرف میں مشہور ہے اور مشہور کی تعریف نہیں ہوتی۔

جواب (2): یہ تحقیقی جواب ہے لیکن اس سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں۔

مقدمہ: تعریف دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس سے مقصود معرف کی ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہوگا یا مقصود صرف معرف کو ماعدا سے جدا کرنا ہوگا یعنی تعین تشخیص مقصود ہوگی۔ مثلا زید معرف ہے اور اس کی ماہیت حیوان ناطق ہے اور تشخیص کے بارے کہا جائیگا کہ فلاں جگہ رہتا ہے ایسا رنگ ہے اتنا قد ہے وغیرہ ذالک۔ تو اگر مقصود ماہیت کو بیان کرنا ہو تو یہ حد ہے اور اگر تعریف تشخیص مقصود ہو تو یہ تعریف رسم ہے۔

حد اور رسم میں فرق: حد اور رسم میں کئی فرق ہیں: (۱) حد میں سوال ما حقیقیہ سے ہوگا اور رسم کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوگا۔ مثلا انسان کی تعریف حقیقی کریں گے تو سوال ہوگا ما الانسان اور اگر ماعدا سے امتیاز مقصود ہو تو کہیں گے أي بي الانسان۔ (۲) حد کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے اور رسم کیلئے جنس و فصل کو ذکر کرنا ضروری نہیں۔ (۳) حد میں صرف اشارہ کافی نہیں ہوتا رسم میں صرف اشارہ کافی ہوتا ہے۔ حد میں ضروری ہے کہ حد کے جتنے اجزاء ہیں ان کی حقیقت بھی معلوم ہو اور رسم میں تمام اجزاء کی حقیقت معلوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔

اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ قرآن کی جو یہ تعریف کی گئی ہے یہ تعریف حد کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے بلکہ رسم کے قبیل سے ہے اس کے بارے میں سوال اسی شئی سے ہوتا ہے یعنی ما نقل إلينا الخ اگر کتاب کی تعریف ہو تو أي كتاب تريد کے سوال
If it is asked: What is mushaf? Then it is necessary to say: It is that in which the Quran is written. So I replied to this objection with my saying: And circularity is not necessary because mushaf is known, i.e., in custom, so there is no need to define it with his saying 'that in which the Quran is written'. Then I intended to investigate in this place that indeed this definition is which type among the types of definitions, because the completeness of the answer depends on it. So I said: And this definition is not the definition of the essence of the book, but rather it is the identification of the book, in answer to 'which book do you intend?' And nor is it the definition of the essence of the Quran, because our scholars said that it is 'what has been transmitted to us' etc. So it is not empty; either they defined the book in this way, or they defined the Quran in this way. If they defined the book in this way, then this is not the definition of the essence of the book, but rather its identification, in answer to 'which book do you intend?' And if they defined the Quran in this way, then this is not the definition of the essence of the Quran either, but rather its identification, because the word 'Quran' is applied to the eternal speech and to the recited speech. So this (definition) specifies one of its two probabilities, and that is the recited speech, because 'Quran' is a word that is shared: it is said of the divine speech which is an attribute of Allah Almighty, and it is also said of that which it indicates, which is the recited speech. So it is as if it was said: Of the two meanings, which meaning do you intend? So it was said: 'what has been transmitted to us' etc., i.e., we intend the recited speech. So based on this detail, circularity does not arise, and there is no exception except that circularity would arise if what is intended is the definition of the essence of the Quran, because if the essence of the Quran is defined by 'that which is written in the mushafs', then it would be necessary to know the essence of mushaf, and at that time it is not possible to know the essence of mushaf through some means like indication and the like, and then the knowledge of the essence of mushaf depends on the knowledge of the essence of the Quran.

Chapter: Mention of the aforementioned divisions in (al-Tanqih)
فتضع الكتاب: The matn has from here explained the divisions or parts of the book, that the book consists of two parts: the first part is about the Shariah proofs, i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), etc.; and the second part is about the rulings. So first he defined the Book of Allah: They call it the Book of Allah and the Quran, that which is written between the two covers of the mushaf and has reached us with tawatur. Then he mentions benefits and restrictions: the restriction 'between the covers of the mushafs' excludes hadith qudsi and absolute hadith, because they are not written in the mushafs; and the restriction 'tawatur' excludes the irregular readings (qira'at shadhdha). But on this definition, Allama Ibn al-Hajib raised an objection.

التويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج
Objection of Allama Ibn al-Hajib on the definition of Quran
Objection: This definition contains circularity, because in this definition the dependence of a thing upon itself becomes necessary: understanding the definition of Quran depends on the definition of mushaf, and if mushaf is asked about, it will be said: 'What is written in it is the Quran.' So understanding Quran depends on mushaf, and understanding mushaf depends on Quran, so understanding Quran depends on Quran, because the dependee of the dependee of a thing is its dependee. And this is circularity, and circularity is false, so what entails circularity is also false. The matn gave answers to this objection.

Answers to Ibn al-Hajib's objections
Answer (1): This is also an answer: that circularity does not arise here, because understanding Quran depends on mushaf, but understanding mushaf does not depend on Quran, because mushaf is well-known in custom, and what is well-known is not defined.

Answer (2): This is a research-based answer, but before it, understand a preamble as a preface.

Preamble: Definition is of two types, not free from either: either it intends to express the essence of the defined, or it intends merely to separate the defined from others, i.e., identification by specification. For example, Zayd is the defined, and his essence is 'rational animal', and regarding identification it will be said: he lives in such a place, has such a color, is such height, etc. So if the intention is to express the essence, it is a hadd; and if the intention is identification by definition, it is a rasm.

Difference between hadd and rasm: There are several differences between hadd and rasm: (1) In hadd, the question is with 'what is it in reality' (ma haqiqiyya), and regarding rasm, the question is about the thing itself. For example, if we give a real definition of man, the question is 'what is man?' (ma al-insan); but if the intention is distinction from others, we say 'which man' (ayy al-insan). (2) For hadd, it is necessary to mention genus and differentia; for rasm, it is not necessary to mention genus and differentia. (3) In hadd, mere indication is not sufficient; in rasm, mere indication is sufficient. In hadd, it is necessary that the reality of all its parts is known; in rasm, it is not necessary to know the reality of all parts.

After this preamble, understand that this definition of the Quran that has been given is not from the category of hadd, but from the category of rasm. Regarding it, the question is about the thing itself, i.e., 'what has been transmitted to us' etc. If it is a definition of the book, then the question is 'which book do you intend?'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of the Quran, addressing an objection of circularity raised by Ibn al-Hajib. The passage type is a dispute: Ibn al-Hajib argues that the definition 'the Quran is what is written between the two covers of the mushaf and transmitted via tawatur' involves circularity because 'mushaf' itself is defined as 'that in which the Quran is written', creating a dependency loop. The Hanafi author provides two responses. First, he argues that no circularity occurs because 'mushaf' is known by customary usage ('urf) and does not require definition; thus, understanding mushaf does not depend on defining Quran. Second, he offers a more sophisticated response distinguishing between two types of definitions: hadd (essential definition, expressing the reality of the thing) and rasm (descriptive definition, merely distinguishing the thing from others). He argues that the definition of the Quran as 'manqul ilayna' (what has been transmitted to us) is not a hadd but a rasm, intended to identify which of the two meanings of 'Quran' (eternal attribute or recited speech) is meant. Therefore, it does not require knowledge of the essence of mushaf. The author then explains the differences between hadd and rasm: hadd answers 'ma huwa' (what is it in essence), requires genus and differentia, and cannot rely on mere indication; rasm answers 'ayyu shay' (which thing), does not need genus and differentia, and can use indication. Applying this, the definition of the Quran as 'manqul ilayna' is a rasm, not a hadd, so it avoids circularity. This response is consistent with Hanafi usul methodology, which emphasizes 'urf and the practical function of definitions in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circularity in definition, where A depends on B and B depends on A, causing a logical loop.
حد (hadd): An essential definition that expresses the reality (mahiyyah) of a thing by mentioning its genus and differentia.
رسم (rasm): A descriptive definition that distinguishes the defined from others without necessarily stating its essence.
تشخیص (tashkhīṣ): Identification or specification of a particular thing among others, often used in definitions to answer 'which one?'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does classifying the definition of Quran as a rasm avoid circularity, according to the passage?
A) Because rasm requires prior knowledge of the thing's essence.
B) Because rasm only needs to identify, not to capture essence.
C) Because rasm uses genus and differentia.
D) Because rasm is always based on custom.

Key Takeaway
The hadd/rasm distinction is a powerful tool in Hanafi usul to defend definitions against charges of circularity.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Definition of the Quran: Hadd or Rasm?
Explains why the Quran's definition is rasm, not hadd, avoiding circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and rasm in the definition of the Quran and explain why the classical definition avoids circularity.

Core Idea
The definition of the Quran as transmitted is a rasm, not a hadd; a hadd would require defining the mus-haf, causing circularity.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies that the common definition of the Quran—'what is transmitted to us tawatur between the covers of the mus-haf'—is not an essential definition (hadd) but a customary one (rasm). This distinction is crucial because an essential definition would lead to a logical circle: to know the Quran you would need to know the mus-haf, and to know the mus-haf you would need to know the Quran. A rasm, however, relies on common recognition and suffices for identification without requiring a full breakdown of components. Let's analyze how this reasoning works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under discussion
The passage evaluates the definition of the Quran as 'what is transmitted to us (manqul ilayna) between the covers of the mus-haf'. Recognize that this is the standard definition used in Hanafi usul.
This definition distinguishes the Quran from the eternal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) and from other scriptures.
2
Classify the definition as hadd or rasm
A hadd enumerates essential constitutive parts (genus and differentia). A rasm identifies by customary features or signs. The passage argues that since the definition does not give a complete logical breakdown but relies on sensory reference (the mus-haf), it is a rasm.
The definition uses 'transmitted to us' and 'between the covers' as identifying signs, not essential properties.
3
Explain the potential circularity if it were a hadd
If the definition were a hadd, one would need to define the mus-haf precisely, which in turn might refer back to the Quran, creating a circle. The passage states: 'If it were a hadd, then circularity would be necessary because then one would have to know the reality of the mus-haf.'
Circularity (dawr) invalidates definitions in logic and usul.
4
Show how the rasm classification resolves circularity
As a rasm, understanding the Quran depends on the mus-haf (a known physical object), but understanding the mus-haf does not depend on a precise definition of the Quran. Thus, there is no mutual dependency, and the definition is sound.
The rasm serves as a sufficient identifier for legal purposes without needing a full hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويع کے جواب میں یہ تعریف واقع ہوگی اور اگر تعریف قرآن کی ہوائی شئی سے سوال ہو گا کیونکہ قرآن کا اطلاق کلام از لی پر بھی ہوتا ہے اور کلام لفظی ( مانقل الیتا الخ) پر بھی ہوتا ہے جو ہم پڑھتے ہیں اب اگر یہ قرآن کی تعریف ہے تو سوال ہو گا ای قرآن ترید جواب میں کہا جائیگا مانقل الینا الخ یعنی ہماری مراد کلام لفظی ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تعریف رسم کے قبیل سے ہے اور رسم کیلئے اشارہ اور عرف کافی ہے اور تمام اجزاء کی تعریف ضروری نہیں ہے تو مصحف کی تعریف بھی ضروری نہیں ہے اب اگر ما نقل الیتا الخ والی تعریف حد ہوتی تو پھر دور لازم آتا کیونکہ پھر مصحف کی حقیقت معلوم کرنا پڑتی تو اب جب یہ تعریف رسم ہے تو قرآن کا سمجھنا تو مصحف پر موقوف ہے لیکن مصحف کا سمجھنا قرآن پر موقوف نہیں تو تو قف اشئی علی نفسہ لازم نہیں آتا۔
The explanation of the definition (of the Quran) occurs in response to this. And if the definition of the Quran is from something, a question arises because the term 'Quran' applies to the eternal speech and also to the verbal speech (which is transmitted to us, etc.) that we recite. Now if this is the definition of the Quran, it would be asked: 'Which Quran do you mean?' In response, one says: 'What is transmitted to us, etc.' – meaning we intend the verbal speech. So it becomes known that this definition is of the type of rasm (customary definition), and for a rasm, a sign and common usage suffice; it is not necessary to define all components. Thus, the definition of the mus-haf is also not necessary. If the definition 'what is transmitted to us, etc.' were a hadd (essential definition), then circularity would be necessary because then one would have to know the reality of the mus-haf. But since this definition is a rasm, understanding the Quran depends on the mus-haf, but understanding the mus-haf does not depend on the Quran, so circularity does not arise.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the definition of the Quran. The author clarifies that the common definition of the Quran as 'that which is transmitted to us tawatur between the covers of the mus-haf' is not an essential definition (hadd) but a customary description (rasm). If it were a hadd, it would require a precise breakdown and could lead to circularity because understanding the mus-haf would presuppose understanding the Quran. However, as a rasm, it is sufficient for identification without needing to define every component. This distinction is important in usul al-fiqh for properly categorizing the primary source of evidence.

Key Terms
رسم (rasm): A definition that describes by customary usage or salient features, not by essential constitutive parts.
حد (hadd): An essential definition that enumerates the genus and differentia of a thing.
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning, where A depends on B and B depends on A.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the definition 'manqul ilayna' (transmitted to us) is a rasm and not a hadd?
A) Because it does not mention the content of the Quran.
B) Because a hadd would require knowing the mus-haf first, causing circularity.
C) Because the Quran can only be defined by its miraculous nature.
D) Because the definition is taken from the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's definition as a rasm suffices for usul al-fiqh and avoids circular reasoning that a hadd would entail.
